Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Hiring a Camel Without Specifying the Load: Customary Load and the Role of Istihsan
Commentary on fasid lease validation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a hired camel dies after carrying a customary load in a lease initially defective due to unspecified load, and explain how istihsan overrides qiyas to validate the contract and fix the named wage.

Core Idea
A fasid lease becomes valid when uncertainty is resolved through customary performance.

In Hanafi fiqh, a lease contract with an unspecified subject matter is initially fasid (defective) because of uncertainty (jahalah). However, when the hirer actually performs the service in a customary manner, the uncertainty is removed, and the contract becomes sahih. This lesson examines a classic case from al-Wiqaya: hiring a camel without naming the load. We will explore how the principle of istihsan (juristic preference) allows the contract to be validated retroactively, and what happens if the camel dies. We will also look at an intra-Hanafi dispute about liability when the hirer denies the lease mid-journey.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial defect
The lease is fasid because the load is unspecified, leading to jahalah that could cause dispute. The contract lacks certainty in the subject matter.
Jahalah in a contract essential term renders it fasid in Hanafi law, not batil.
2
Locate the proof for validation
When the hirer loads a customary load, the uncertainty is removed. The commentator applies istihsan: the lease becomes valid retroactively from the moment of loading, and the named wage is binding.
Strict qiyas would require ujr al-mithl, but istihsan overrides due to removal of hardship.
3
Contrast with qiyas
Under qiyas, since the lease was fasid at inception, the hirer would owe the equivalent market wage (ujr al-mithl). But by istihsan, the named wage stands because the defect was cured by performance.
The commentator explicitly says 'In qiyas: the equivalent wage is obligatory; by istihsan, the named wage.'
4
Apply the condition of custom
If the load exceeds the customary weight, the hirer is liable for transgression (ta'addi) and must pay damages. Custom defines the permissible limit.
Absolute permission is restricted to the customary.
5
Note the sub-issue: denial of lease
If the hirer denies the lease mid-journey, Abu Yusuf holds only wage before denial (post-denial he is a usurper), while Muhammad holds full wage (he refrained from use).
This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf does not affect the main ruling.

Source Text

[٤]قوله : لأن الإجارة ... الخ ؛ حاصله : إنّ العين أمانة في يد المستأجر، وإن كانت الإجارة فاسدة ؛ لأنّ الفساد معتبر بالصحيح ؛ لكونه مشروعاً من وجه.

[٣]

[١]قوله : استحساناً ؛ فإنّ الفساد كان للجهالة، فإذا حمل عليه شيئاً يحمل على مثله تعين ذلك، فانقلب صحيحاً ؛ لأنّ الموجب للفساد قد زال، وفي القياس : يجب أجر المثل لفساد الإجارة. And whoever hires a camel to Egypt, and does not name its load, then loads the customary load and it dies, he is not liable, because the lease is fasid, so the object is a trust as in a valid lease. And its text: from Ya'qub from Abu Hanifa regarding a man who leases land and does not name what he will plant, he said: the lease is fasid, if they dispute before he works on it, I annul it; if he plants and the term passes, he gets the named wage. So ponder. End.
[1] His statement: it is removed; by the occurrence of what occurred of planting. If it is said: if the ignorance is removed by mere planting, then it is possible that what he planted harms the land, so dispute occurs for this reason; we say: the prohibiting factor explained is the expectation of dispute between them regarding the determination of the contracted subject, and this expectation is removed, so the contract becomes permissible.
[2] His statement: before completion of the contract; i.e., before the end of its term. And the statement of al-'Inaya: before completion of the contract, the judge annuls it, which sound nature does not accept, for it is rescinded from the origin by the judge's annulment, so how is it completed? And completion of a thing is from the effects of its continuity. Mentioned by 'Allamah al-Shami quoting al-Turi.
[3] His statement: and the customary load; it is only qualified because if he loads on it what is not customarily loaded, then that camel perishes, liability is obligatory due to apparent transgression, contrary to the customary load, for absolute permission is restricted to the customary, and he did not transgress the customary.
[4] His statement: because the lease... etc.; its summary: that the object is a trust in the hands of the lessee, even if the lease is fasid; because the fasid is considered with the valid, due to being legislated from one aspect.
Book of Ijarah / Chapter of Fasid Ijarah
And if it arrives, he gets the named [wage]; if they dispute before planting or loading, the judge annuls the lease contract. (And if it arrives, he gets the named): i.e., by istihsan, as we mentioned in the matter of planting. (If they dispute before planting or loading, the judge annuls the lease contract): i.e., if the two contracting parties dispute before planting in the matter of leasing land without mentioning the crop, and before loading in this matter, the judge annuls the contract in its essence without its description, so he is not liable as long as he does not transgress; if he transgresses, he is liable and has no wage. [1] His statement: by istihsan; for the fasid was due to ignorance, so when he loads something that is loaded on its like, it becomes determined, so it turns valid; because the cause of fasid has ceased. In qiyas: the equivalent wage is obligatory due to the fasid lease. [2] His statement: as we mentioned in the matter of planting; where he said: the ignorance is removed before completion of the contract, end. So when he loads on the camel a customary load, it becomes determined and the ignorance that leads to dispute is removed, so the lease turns to permissibility, and what he specified of wage is obligatory. [3] His statement: the judge annuls... etc.; for the fasid remains after the lease contract before loading on the camel and before planting in the land. And if a person hires a riding animal, then denies the lease in some part of the road, then he is obligated the wage for what he rode before the denial, and the wage for what comes after is not obligatory according to Abu Yusuf, because through denial he became a usurper, and wage and liability cannot combine. And Muhammad said: the entire wage is obligatory, because he refrained from use, so liability ceases. Al-Zayla'i mentioned it quoting from al-Kafi.
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary (sharh) on a matn from al-Wiqaya dealing with a specific case of fasid (defective) lease. The base ruling states: if someone hires a camel to travel to Egypt without specifying the load, then loads an amount that is customary for such a camel, and the camel dies on the journey, the hirer (musta'jir) is not liable for the camel's value. The commentator explains the legal reasoning. The lease is initially fasid because the subject matter (the load) is unspecified, creating uncertainty (jahalah) that could lead to dispute. However, when the hirer actually loads a customary load, the uncertainty is removed because the contracted service (transporting that load) becomes determined. This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) — the lease becomes valid retroactively from the moment of loading. Under strict qiyas (analogy), since the lease was fasid at inception, the hirer would owe the equivalent market wage (ujr al-mithl) for the journey. But by istihsan, because the parties originally agreed on a named wage and the uncertainty was resolved through performance, the named wage is binding and the lease is deemed valid. The condition that the load must be 'customary' is crucial: if the hirer loads an unusually heavy load that causes the camel's death, he is liable because he transgressed (ta'addi). The general principle is that in a fasid lease, the hired object (here the camel) is held as a trust (amanah) in the hirer's hands, similar to a valid lease. Thus, no liability arises unless the hirer exceeds the customary use. The passage also includes a sub-ruling: if the contracting parties dispute before the performance (planting or loading), the judge annuls the contract entirely because the fasid element remains. After performance, the contract is ratified. Finally, an additional example is given: if a lessee (musta'jir) denies the lease during the journey (juhud), Abu Yusuf holds that after the denial he becomes a usurper (ghasib), so he owes wage only for the period before denial, and no wage afterward because wage and liability (daman) cannot coexist. Muhammad holds that since he refrained from using the animal after denial, he is not a usurper, so he owes the entire wage. The relied-upon position is the one consistent with istihsan for the original issue.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): A lease contract that is defective in its conditions (e.g., unspecified subject matter) but still produces some legal effects (e.g., object is amanah).
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Uncertainty or ignorance about a essential term (e.g., load weight) that initially renders the contract fasid.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference: departing from strict analogy (qiyas) due to a stronger consideration (maslahah or removal of hardship).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the lessee not owe liability when the camel dies after loading a customary load, even though the lease was fasid?
A) Because the lease was valid from the start due to the existence of a named wage.
B) Because the camel is considered a trust (amanah) in the lessee's hands, and only transgression makes him liable.
C) Because the lessee did not actually cause the camel's death.
D) Because the lessor assumed the risk of customary transportation.

Key Takeaway
A fasid lease with unspecified subject matter becomes valid through customary performance by istihsan, and the hired object remains a trust absent transgression.

Invalid Ijarah Becoming Valid by Actualization: Istihsan and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Denial
Commentary on istihsan ruling for invalid Ijarah becoming valid and an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when an invalid Ijarah becomes valid by istihsan, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the wage when the hirer denies the contract mid-journey.

Core Idea
An invalid Ijarah becomes valid by istihsan when the uncertain element is actualized; but if the hirer denies the contract mid-journey, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on the wage.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah explains the Hanafi ruling on an invalid Ijarah contract that becomes valid through actualization. It also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the wage due when the hirer denies the contract mid-journey. Understanding this illustrates the use of istihsan to override qiyas and the application of legal reasoning to contractual disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the ruling: an invalid Ijarah (due to uncertainty) becomes valid when the uncertain element is actualized (e.g., the camel carries a customary load or the land is cultivated). The ruling is that it becomes sahih by istihsan and the named wage is due.
The matn states: 'wa in balagha falahu al-musamma' (if it is fulfilled, the named wage is his).
2
Understand the istihsan reasoning
The invalidity was due to uncertainty. When the uncertain matter becomes specified through customary actualization, the cause of invalidity ceases. Istihsan overrides qiyas (which would require ujrat al-mithl).
The commentator explains: 'fainna al-fasad kana lil-jahalah, faidha hamala alayhi shayan yahmilu ala mithlihi ta'ayyana dhalika, fanqalaba sahihan.'
3
Note the two scenarios: actualization vs dispute before actualization
If the parties dispute before actualization, the judge rescinds the contract entirely (not just its description). The lessor is not liable unless he transgressed (e.g., overloading). If he transgresses, he is liable and no wage is due.
The contract remains invalid until actualization, so it can be rescinded.
4
State the intra-Hanafi dispute
If the hirer denies the contract (juhud) mid-journey after using the hired animal, Abu Yusuf holds that wage is due only for the portion before denial, because after denial the hirer becomes a usurper (ghasib), and wage and liability cannot combine. Muhammad holds that the entire wage is due because the usage before denial was lawful and liability does not retroactively apply.
The passage cites al-Zayla'i from al-Kafi.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Abu Yusuf's view results in a lower wage (only for the lawful usage before denial); Muhammad's view results in the full wage. The passage does not give a tarjih.
This affects how a judge would decide in such a case.

Source Text

[٣]

[١]قوله : استحساناً ؛ فإنّ الفساد كان للجهالة، فإذا حمل عليه شيئاً يحمل على مثله تعين ذلك، فانقلب صحيحاً ؛ لأنّ الموجب للفساد قد زال، وفي القياس : يجب أجر المثل لفساد الإجارة. [٣] قوله : ينقض القاضي ... الخ ؛ فإنّ الفساد قائم بعد عقد الإجارة قبل الحمل على الجمل وقبل الزراعة في الأرض، ولو استأجر دابة ثم جحد الإجارة في بعض الطريق وجب عليه أجر ما ركب قبل الإنكار ، ولا تجب الأجر لمـا بعـده عند أبي يوسف له ؛ لأنه بالجحود صار غاصباً، والأجر والضمان لا يجتمعان. وقال محمد الله : يجب الأجرُ كلّه ؛ لأنه سلم من الاستعمال فسقط الضمان.

Book of Ijarah / Chapter on Invalid Ijarah
(And if it is fulfilled, then the named wage is for him) meaning by istihsan, as we mentioned in the issue of cultivation (13). (And if they dispute before planting or carrying, the Ijarah contract is rescinded): meaning if the two contracting parties dispute before planting in the case of renting land without mentioning the crop, and before carrying in this case, the judge rescinds the contract. In its essence without its description, so he is not liable as long as he has not transgressed; if he transgresses, he is liable and there is no wage for him. According to qiyas, the rent of the like is due due to the invalidity of the Ijarah. [2] His statement: 'as we mentioned in the issue of cultivation' where he said: the uncertainty has been removed before the completion of the contract. Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah discusses the ruling of an invalid Ijarah contract that becomes valid through actualization. The passage type is a commentary expanding on a matn ruling, specifically addressing istihsan and an intra-Hanafi dispute.
The author first states the ruling: if the uncertain element (such as the crop in land rental or the load on a camel) is actualized, then the contract becomes valid and the named wage is due by istihsan. The commentator explains that istihsan is used because the invalidity was due to uncertainty; when the uncertain matter is resolved through custom (e.g., carrying a customary load), the cause of invalidity is removed, and the contract becomes sound. In contrast, qiyas would require the rent of the like (ujrat al-mithl) because the contract was originally invalid.
The second part discusses what happens if the parties dispute before the actualization. In that case, the judge rescinds the contract entirely (not just its description), meaning the contract is voided retroactively. The lessor is not liable for the lessee's use unless he transgressed (e.g., overloading); if he did transgress, he is liable and also not entitled to any wage.
The third part presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding juhud (denial) of the contract during a journey. If a person hires a riding animal and then denies the contract on part of the way, Abu Yusuf rules that the wage is only due for the portion ridden before the denial, because after denial the hirer becomes a usurper (ghasib), and wage and liability cannot combine. Muhammad rules that the entire wage is due because the hirer's usage was lawful (safe from liability) during that period, and his later denial does not retroactively invalidate the lawful usage. The commentator notes that this discussion is cited from al-Zayla'i from al-Kafi.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijārah al-fāsidah): An Ijarah contract that is invalid due to a defect such as uncertainty (jahalah) in the subject matter or wage, but may become valid if the defect is cured.
استحسان (istiḥsān): A method of juristic preference that sets aside a strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling due to custom, necessity, or other consideration.
جحود (juḥūd): Denial of a contractual obligation by a party, which can render the denier a usurper (ghasib) from that point onward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Abu Yusuf regarding the wage when the hirer denies the Ijarah contract mid-journey?
A) The entire wage is due.
B) Only the wage for the portion before denial is due.
C) No wage is due because the contract is invalid.
D) The wage is doubled as a penalty.

Key Takeaway
An invalid Ijarah can become valid by actualization via istihsan, but if the hirer denies the contract mid-term, the wage due is disputed between Abu Yusuf (partial) and Muhammad (full).

Definition and Ruling of the Common and Special Hireling
Defining the two types of hirelings and their respective rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the common hireling from the special hireling and state the ruling on who may work for multiple employers.

Core Idea
The common hireling works for many; the special hireling works for one, paid for availability, not output.

In the chapter on ijarah, this passage defines the two categories of hirelings: common (ajir mushtarak) and special (ajir khas). The definition may seem straightforward, but classical Hanafi scholars differed on the precise criteria: some used the number of employers, others used the basis of wage entitlement. Understanding this classification is crucial because it determines whether a hireling can accept work from multiple people and how his wage is earned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Read the passage to find the two categories of hirelings: common (ajir mushtarak) and special (ajir khas).
2
Understand the definitional dispute
Note that some mashayikh defined them by the number of employers (common = more than one, special = one), while al-Quduri defined them by wage entitlement (common = wage only by work, special = wage by self-surrender). The commentator criticizes the latter as circular.
Circularity means the definition presupposes knowledge of what it defines.
3
Apply the ruling on working for multiple employers
The common hireling may work for the public because his benefit is not owed exclusively to any one employer. The special hireling cannot work for others because his benefit during the contract period is owned by the employer.
This ruling is consistent regardless of the definitional preference.
4
Recognize the basis of wage entitlement
For the common hireling, wage is earned by performing work. For the special hireling, wage is earned simply by making himself available during the period, even if no work is done.
This follows from the fact that the wage is in exchange for the benefit (availability), not the actual output.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب من الإجارة [فصل ضمان الأجير]
(الأجير المشترك (۳) يستحق الأجر بالعمل ، فله أن يعمل للعامة)، إنَّما أدخل الفاءَ في قوله : فله ؛ لأنَّ هذا مبني على ما سبق ؛ لأن الواجب عليه أن يعمل هذا العمل من غير أن يصير منافع الأجير للمستأجر ، فسمي بهذا : أي بالأجير المشترك. [١] قوله : باب من الإجارة ؛ أي هذا قطعة من بيان الإجارة ذكر فيها ضمان الأجير وغيره لما فرغ المصنّف له عن ذكر أنواع الإجارة صحيحها وفاسدها شرع في بيان الضمان ؛ لأنه من جملة العوارض التي تترتب على عقد الإجارة، فيحتاج الى بيانه. ذكره الإِثْقَانِيُّ، وغيره.
[٢] قوله : الأجير المشترك ؛ الأجير على ضربين : أجير مشترك، وأجير خاص،
وقد اختلفت عبارة المشايخ في حدهما :
فقال بعضهم: الأجير المشترك : مَن يتقبل العمل من غير واحد، والأجير
الخاص : مَن يتقبل العمل من واحد.
وقال القُدُوري له : المشترك من لا يستحقُ الأجر حتى يعمل، والأجير الخاص: الذي يستحق الأجر بتسليم نفسه في المدة، وإن لم يعمل، وهذا يؤول إلى الدور ؛ لأنّ هذا حكم لا يعرفه إلا من يعرف الأجير المشترك والخاص.
وحكمه : أن المشترك له أن يتقبل العمل من أشخاص ؛ لأنّ المعقود عليه في حقه هو العمل أو أثره ، فكان له أن يتقبل من العامة ؛ لأنّ منافعه لم تصر مستحقة لواحد ، فمَن هذا الوجه سُمِيَ مشتركاً، والأجيرُ الخاص لا يمكنه أن يعمل لغيره ؛ لأنّ منافعه في المدة صارت مستحقة للمستأجر، والأجر مقابل بالمنافع ؛ ولهذا يبقى الأجر مستحقاً،
وإن نقص العمل. كذا في «التبيين»(۱).
Chapter on Hire (Ijarah), Section on the Liability of the Hireling. The common hireling is entitled to the wage by work, so he may work for the public. The fa in his statement 'so he may' is inserted because this is built on what preceded: because it is obligatory upon him to do this work without the hireling's benefits becoming owned by the employer, so he is called by this: i.e., the common hireling. [1] His statement: 'Chapter on Hire' – i.e., this is a part of the exposition of hire in which the liability of the hireling and other matters are mentioned. When the author finished mentioning the types of hire, valid and invalid, he started explaining liability because it is among the consequences that follow upon the contract of hire; thus it needs explanation. Mentioned by al-Ithqani and others. [2] His statement: 'the common hireling' – the hireling is of two types: common hireling and special hireling. The expressions of the mashayikh have differed regarding their definitions: some said: the common hireling is the one who accepts work from more than one, and the special hireling is the one who accepts work from one. Al-Quduri said: the common hireling is the one who does not deserve the wage until he works, and the special hireling is the one who deserves the wage by surrendering himself during the period even if he does not work. This amounts to circularity because this is a ruling that is not known except by one who knows the common and special hireling. Its ruling: that the common hireling may accept work from individuals because what is contracted with respect to him is the work or its effect, so he may accept from the public because his benefits have not become due to one; from this aspect he is called 'common'. The special hireling cannot work for others because his benefits during the period have become due to the employer, and the wage is in exchange for benefits; therefore the wage remains due even if the work is diminished. As in al-Tabyin.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on ijarah defines the two categories of hirelings: the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) and the special hireling (ajir khas). The commentary begins by explaining why the author used the word 'fa' (so) in the phrase 'so he may work for the public'. This indicates a logical consequence: since the common hireling's obligation is merely to perform the work without transferring ownership of his benefit to any particular employer, he is free to work for multiple people. The passage then notes that scholars differed over the precise definition. Some defined them in terms of the number of employers: common hireling accepts work from more than one, special from one. Al-Quduri defined them in terms of entitlement to wage: common does not deserve wage until he works, special deserves wage by merely making himself available during the agreed period. The commentator points out that this latter definition is circular because it assumes knowledge of the terms. The ruling is then stated: the common hireling may work for multiple people because his benefit is not exclusively owed to any one; the special hireling's benefit during the contract period is exclusively owed to the employer, so he cannot work for others. Importantly, the special hireling's wage remains due even if he does not perform the actual work, because the wage is in exchange for the benefit (the availability of his services), not merely for the output of work. This is taken from al-Tabyin.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A hireling who accepts work from multiple employers and is entitled to wage only after performing the work; his benefits are not exclusively owed to any one employer.
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A hireling who works exclusively for one employer and is entitled to wage by making himself available during the period, even if he does no work.
أجر (ajr): Wage or compensation paid in exchange for the benefit (manfa'ah) or work provided by the hireling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the key difference between a common hireling (ajir mushtarak) and a special hireling (ajir khas)?
A) The common hireling is entitled to wage only after work; the special hireling is entitled from the start regardless of work.
B) The common hireling may work for multiple employers; the special hireling may only work for one employer.
C) The common hireling's benefit is owned by the employer; the special hireling's benefit is not.
D) Both are the same; the distinction is merely terminological.

Key Takeaway
The common hireling may work for many, the special hireling works for one; the classification determines wage entitlement: the special hireling is paid for availability, not output.

Definitions of the Common and Specific Hireling (Ajir Mushtarak and Ajir Khas)
Defines and distinguishes the two types of hirelings in Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the ajir mushtarak and ajir khas according to the preferred Hanafi definition and explain the practical legal consequence of this distinction.

Core Idea
The ajir mushtarak is hired for a specific work, not his time, so he can work for many; the ajir khas is hired for his time, so his benefits are owned exclusively.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks the foundational definitions of two types of hirelings in Hanafi fiqh: the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) and the specific hireling (ajir khas). The distinction turns on what is contracted—work or benefits—and determines when wage is due and whether the hireling may work for multiple parties. We will explore the different definitions offered by earlier scholars and see why al-Awjah's formulation is preferred for its analytical clarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of hirelings
Read the passage to extract the two categories: ajir mushtarak and ajir khas. Note the defining features mentioned by the mashayikh and al-Quduri.
Keep track of the key terms: 'work' (amal) vs 'benefits' (manafi).
2
Recognize the circularity in al-Quduri's definition
Al-Quduri defined the types by their ruling on wage entitlement. The commentator notes this leads to circular reasoning because the definition presupposes knowledge of the types. Understand why this is a logical flaw.
Circularity: you cannot define a term by a ruling that itself depends on knowing the term.
3
Understand al-Awjah's preferred definition
Al-Awjah defines the ajir mushtarak as one whose contract is for a specified work (e.g., sewing a garment), and the ajir khas as one whose contract is for his benefits over a period. This is non-circular and based on the object of the contract.
This definition has direct legal consequences: wage entitlement and ability to work for others.
4
Apply the definition to the ruling on wage and multiple contracts
From the preferred definition, derive the rulings: the ajir mushtarak is entitled to wage upon performing the work and may accept work from multiple parties because his benefits are not exclusively owned; the ajir khas is entitled to wage merely by making himself available and cannot work for others because his benefits are owned by the lessee.
This distinction also relates to liability for loss, which will be covered in subsequent sections.

Chapter of Ijarah: Section on the Liability of the Hireling. The common hireling (ajir mushtarak) is entitled to the wage by working, so he may work for the general public. Chapter of Ijarah. [1] Section on the Liability of the Hireling. (The common hireling is entitled to the wage by working, so he may work for the general public). He inserted the 'fa' in his saying 'falahu' because this is built upon what preceded; because the obligation upon him is to perform this work without the hireling's benefits becoming owned by the lessee, so he is called by this: i.e., the common hireling. [1] His saying: Chapter of Ijarah; meaning this is a portion of the exposition of Ijarah in which the liability of the hireling and other matters are mentioned. When the author finished mentioning the types of Ijarah, its valid and invalid, he began to explain liability because it is among the incidental matters that follow from the contract of Ijarah, so it needs explanation. Al-Ithqani and others mentioned it. [2] His saying: The common hireling; the hireling is of two types: a common hireling (ajir mushtarak) and a specific hireling (ajir khas). The expression of the mashayikh differed regarding their definition. Some said: The common hireling is one who accepts work from more than one person, and the specific hireling is one who accepts work from one person. Al-Quduri said: The common hireling is one who is not entitled to the wage until he works, and the specific hireling is one who is entitled to the wage by handing over himself for the period, even if he does not work. This leads to circularity because this is a ruling that is not known except by one who knows the common and specific hireling. His ruling: The common hireling may accept work from individuals because what is contracted in his case is the work or its effect, so he may accept from the public because his benefits have not become owned by one person; from this aspect he is called common. And the specific hireling cannot work for others because his benefits in the period have become owned by the lessee, and the wage is in exchange for benefits; for this reason the wage remains due even if the work is deficient. Thus in al-Tabyin (1:134). The essence of the final commentary: (1) Like the tailor and the like, and he does not guarantee what perishes in his hand, even if he stipulates guarantee upon him. Like the tailor and the like, and he does not guarantee what perishes in his hand, even if he stipulates guarantee upon him. And it can be answered about it: That it has been known from what preceded in the chapter on wage when it is due that some wage is due by work, so its knowledge is not dependent on knowledge of the definer. So the better is what al-Awjah said: It should be said: The common hireling is one whose contract is entered into for a specified work by specifying its place, to be safe from criticism. And the specific hireling is one whose contract is entered into for his benefits, and his benefits are not known except by mentioning the period or the distance, and his benefits are in the category of a specific asset. So when they become owned by a person through a contract of exchange, he cannot obligate them to another, unlike the common hireling because what is contracted in his case is the attribute that occurs in the asset through his work, so there is no need to mention the period, and accepting similar work from others is not prohibited because what the first person has a right to is in the category of a debt in his liability. And this is analogous to salam in contrast to sale of a specific asset. For the seller in salam, since what is owed is a debt on his liability, he is not prevented by it from accepting salam from others; whereas sale meets the specific asset, so after selling it he does not own selling it to another. For this reason he is common, and the first is a single hireling and a specific hireling. End.
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the section of Ijarah dealing with the liability of the hireling. The author begins by explaining the matn (base text) which states that the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) is entitled to wage upon doing the work, and therefore he may work for the general public. The commentator clarifies that the addition of the word 'fa' (so) in 'falahu' is to indicate that this ruling is built upon the preceding principle: the hireling's benefits are not transferred to the lessee, so the hireling remains free to work for others. The commentator then defines the two types of hireling. According to some mashayikh, the ajir mushtarak is one who accepts work from multiple parties, while the ajir khas accepts work from only one. Al-Quduri defined them based on entitlement to wage: the common hireling is not entitled until he works, whereas the specific hireling is entitled simply by making himself available for the period, even if he does no work. The commentator notes that this definition is circular because it presupposes knowledge of the types. The preferred definition, as stated by al-Awjah, is that the common hireling's contract is for a specific work defined by its location (e.g., tailoring a garment), so he does not need to mention a period and can accept work from others because his work is a debt in his liability, similar to salam (advance sale). The specific hireling's contract is for his benefits during a period, so his benefits become owned by the lessee, and he cannot work for others. This distinction is crucial for determining liability: the common hireling does not guarantee what perishes in his hand, as will be discussed in the next section.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A hireling whose contract is entered into for a specific work (e.g., sewing a garment), not for his time. He is entitled to wage upon completion of work and may work for multiple customers.
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A hireling whose contract is entered into for his benefits over a period. He is entitled to wage by making himself available, and cannot work for others during the hire period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The ajir mushtarak works for a wage, the ajir khas works for free.
B) The ajir mushtarak is hired for a specific work, the ajir khas is hired for his time.
C) The ajir mushtarak is liable for loss, the ajir khas is not.
D) The ajir mushtarak cannot work for others, the ajir khas can.

Key Takeaway
The ajir mushtarak is defined by a contract for a specific work, not for his time, which permits him to work for multiple clients, whereas the ajir khas's contract for his time prohibits working for others.

Liability of the Common Hireling and Condition of Guarantee
Explains the liability of the ajir mushtarak and the disagreement on his guarantee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the liability of the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) and distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The common hireling is a trustee, not a guarantor—he is only liable for his own negligence.

This passage addresses a critical question in the law of hire (ijara): who bears the risk when goods in the care of a common hireling are lost or destroyed? The Hanafi school, through its founder Imam Abu Hanifa, established the principle that the ajir mushtarak is a trustee and thus not liable for loss in the absence of negligence. However, his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, held a different view. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and the conditions under which a guarantee can be validly stipulated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what legal ruling is being stated. Here, it is about whether the common hireling is liable for goods that perish in his possession.
The text explicitly says 'he does not guarantee what perishes in his hand'.
2
State the Hanafi default position
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the hireling is not liable for any loss, whether preventable or unpreventable.
This is the starting point of the analysis.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani differ: they hold the hireling liable for preventable losses but not for unpreventable ones.
This is a key point of internal debate within the school.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, if goods are stolen, the hireling is not liable; under the Sahibayn, he is liable because theft is preventable.
This shows how the difference matters in real cases.
5
Analyze the stipulation of guarantee
If the contract includes a condition that the hireling will guarantee all losses, such a condition is invalid for unpreventable losses by consensus, and corrupts the contract.
This is a separate but related rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولا يضمن ما هلك في يده...الخ ؛ سواء هلك بأمر يمكن التحرز عنه كالسرقة والغصب، أو بأمر لا يمكن التحرُّزُ عنه كالموت حتف الأنف، والحريق الغالب والغارة الغالبة، وهذا عند الإمام، وأحمد وإسحاق، والمزني، والشافعي ه في قول. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : إن هلك بأمر لا يمكن التحرز عنه فلا ضمان عليه، وإن هلك بأمر يمكن التحرز عنه فعليه الضمان، والمالك بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه محمولاً وأعطاه الأجر، وإن شاء ضمنه غير معمول ولا أجر له، وبالتضمين قال مالك والشافعي له في قول.
[٢] قوله : وإن شرط عليه الضمان ؛ قال الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «شرح الكنز»(۲) : إن شرط الضمان على الأجير المشترك في العقد، فإن شرط عليه فيما لا يمكن التحرُّزُ عنه لا يجوز بالإجماع ؛ لأنه شرط لا يقتضيه العقد، وفيه منفعة لأحدهما ففسدت.
(۱) في «التبيين»(٥ : ١٣٣).
(۲) تبيين الحقائق (٥ : ١٣٥).
His saying: "And he does not guarantee what perishes in his hand...etc."; whether it perishes due to something preventable like theft or usurpation, or due to something unpreventable like natural death, overwhelming fire, and overpowering raid. And this is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), and Ahmad, and Ishaq, and al-Muzani, and al-Shafi'i in one of his opinions. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: If it perishes due to something unpreventable, there is no liability on him; but if it perishes due to something preventable, then he is liable. The owner (the consignor) has the option: if he wishes, he may hold him liable as a carrier (i.e., one who carried the goods) and give him the wage, or if he wishes, he may hold him liable as one who did not work and give no wage. And liability (tadmin) is held by Malik and al-Shafi'i in one opinion. [2] His saying: "And if he stipulated guarantee upon him." Al-Zayla'i said in "Sharh al-Kanz": If guarantee is stipulated on the common hireling in the contract, then if it is stipulated regarding something that cannot be prevented, it is not permissible by consensus because it is a condition not required by the contract and contains a benefit for one of them, thus it corrupts (the contract).
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage deals with the liability of the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) for goods in his possession. The ruling stated is that the ajir mushtarak does not guarantee loss (daman) regardless of whether the loss is preventable (like theft) or unpreventable (like fire). This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa, and it is also attributed to Ahmad, Ishaq, al-Muzani, and al-Shafi'i in one of his opinions. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differentiate: if the loss is unpreventable, the hireling is not liable; if preventable, he is liable. This disagreement is practical: under Abu Hanifa's view, the hireling is a trustee (amin) and is not liable unless he is negligent. Under the Sahibayn, the hireling is a guarantor for preventable losses. The text also mentions that the consignor has an option: if the goods are lost due to a preventable cause, he can either hold the hireling liable as a carrier (and still pay the wage) or hold him liable as not having done the work (and not pay the wage). Finally, the text discusses stipulating a guarantee in the contract. According to al-Zayla'i, if the condition is for unpreventable losses, it is invalid by consensus because it is a condition that does not conform to the contract and benefits one party unfairly, thus rendering the contract corrupt.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability for loss of property; here, whether the hireling is financially responsible for goods that perish in his possession.
شرط الضمان (shart al-daman): A condition in the contract that the hireling will guarantee (i.e., be liable for) any loss. Its validity depends on the type of loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view (Imam Abu Hanifa), when is the ajir mushtarak liable for goods that perish in his hand?
A) Only if the loss is due to his negligence
B) Always, even if the loss is unpreventable
C) Only if the loss is preventable
D) Never, in any case

Key Takeaway
The common hireling (ajir mushtarak) is a trustee and is not liable for loss in his custody without negligence, a principle affirmed by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Distinguishing Common and Special Hire in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines and distinguishes the two types of hire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ajir mushtarak and ajir khas, explain the legal basis for their different treatment regarding liability and multiple contracts, and apply the distinction to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Common hire is a debt; special hire is a specific object – that changes everything.

In Hanafi law, hired workers are classified into two fundamental types: common (ajir mushtarak) and special (ajir khas). This classification does not depend on the trade (tailor, carpenter, guard) but on the structure of the contract – whether it is for a specific task or for services over a period. This passage from a classical sharh clarifies the definitions using the elegant analogy of salam versus sale of a specific object.

Guided Path
1
Extract the core definitions
Locate the definitions in the text: ajir mushtarak is contracted on a specific task (work), while ajir khas is contracted on his services (manafi) typically over a period or distance.
The definitions are announced after 'الأجير المشترك' and 'الأجير الخاص'.
2
Identify the legal consequences
Notice the key outcomes: common hire does not guarantee loss (unless negligence) and can accept work from multiple principals; special hire's services become like a specific object, preventing him from contracting with others for the same period.
These consequences flow from the nature of what is contracted.
3
Understand the salam analogy
The text likens common hire entitlement to a debt (dayn) – like a salam seller who can accept multiple salam contracts. In contrast, special hire is like a seller of a specific object who cannot sell again.
This analogy illuminates why a common hire can serve many clients.
4
Apply to everyday scenarios
Consider a freelancer vs. employee. A freelancer (task-based) is common hire; a full-time employee (service-based) is special hire. This determines liability and exclusivity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كالخياط ونحوه، ولا يضمن ما هلك في يده ، وإن شرط عليه الضمان كالخياط ونحوه، ولا يضمن ما هلك في يده ، وإن شرط عليه الضمان) ويمكن أن يجاب عنه : بأنه قد عُلِمَ مما سبق في باب الأجر متى يستحق : إنّ بعض الأجر يستحق بالعمل ، فلم يتوقف معرفته على معرفة المعـرف فالأولى ما قاله الأوجه أن يقال : الأجير المشترك من يكون عقده وارداً على عمل معلوم ببيان محله؛ ليسلم من النقض. والأجير الخاص من يكون العقد وارداً على منافعه ولا يصير. منافعه معلومة إلا بذكر المدة أو بذكر المسافة، ومنافعه في حكم العين ، فإذا صارت مستحقة بعقد المعاوضة لإنسان لا يتمكن من إيجابها لغيره بخلاف الأجير المشترك ؛ لأنّ المعقود عليه فيه هو الوصف الذي يحدث في العين بعمله، فلا يحتاجُ إلى ذكر المدة، ولا يمتنع تقبل مثل ذلك العمل مع غيره ؛ لأنّ ما استحقه الأول في حكم الدين في ذمته. وهو نظير السلم مع بيع العين، فإن المُسَلّم فيه لما كان ديناً في ذمته لا يتعذر عليه بسببه قبول السلم من غيره، والبيع لما كان يلاقي العين لا يملك بيعه من غيره بعدما باعه ؛ ولهذا كان مشتركاً، والأول أجير واحد، وأجير خاص. انتهى.
Like the tailor and the like, and he does not guarantee what perishes in his hand, even if he stipulates a guarantee like the tailor and like, and he does not guarantee what perishes in his hand, even if he stipulates a guarantee. And it can be answered: It has been learned from what preceded in the chapter on wages when they are due: some wages are due for work, so knowing it does not depend on knowing the definition. So the best what the most authoritative said is to say: The common hire (ajir mushtarak) is one whose contract is entered upon a specific task, defined by specifying its location, to avoid criticism. The special hire (ajir khas) is one whose contract is entered upon his services, and his services are not known except by mentioning the period or the distance, and his services are in the status of a specific object. So when they become due through a compensatory contract for a person, he is not able to assign them to another, unlike the common hire, because what is contracted upon in him is the attribute that is produced in the object by his work, so it does not need mention of the period, and it is not impossible to accept similar work along with someone else, because what the first person is entitled to is in the status of a debt (dayn) in his liability. And it is analogous to salam with sale of a specific object: for the salam commodity, since it is a debt in his liability, he is not prevented by it from accepting salam from another, and sale, since it concerns a specific object, he does not own selling it to another after selling it. Therefore, the first is common (mushtarak), and the former is a single hire, and a special hire. End.
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage defines the two categories of hired workers (ajir) in Hanafi fiqh. The starting point is the matn's ruling that a common hire like a tailor does not guarantee (daman) for loss. The commentator (sharh) explains the underlying definition. A common hire (ajir mushtarak) is contracted for a specific work or task, defined by its location (e.g., sewing a garment). The contract is on the attribute (wasf) that the worker produces in the object. Such a worker can take work from multiple people because his entitlement is a debt (dayn) in his liability, similar to salam. A special hire (ajir khas) is contracted for his services (manafi) over a period of time (duration or distance). His services are treated like a specific object ('ayn), so once he is contracted for a period, he cannot assign those services to another. This distinction governs liability and the validity of stipulating guarantees.

Key Terms
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A hired worker whose contract is for a specific task or work, not for a period of time.
الأجير الخاص (al-ajir al-khas): A hired worker whose contract is for his services over a specified period or distance.
المنافع (al-manafi): The services or benefits of the worker, which in the case of special hire are considered in the status of an 'ayn (specific object).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can a common hire (ajir mushtarak) accept work from multiple principals simultaneously?
A) Because his work is not divisible.
B) Because his entitlement is a debt (dayn) in his liability, similar to salam.
C) Because he does not guarantee the property.
D) Because the contract is for a specific period.

Key Takeaway
The classification of a hire depends on whether the contract is for a specific task (debt-like) or for services over time (ayn-like), determining liability and the possibility of multiple engagements.

Liability of Common Hire for Loss and Stipulated Guarantee
Intra-Hanafi dispute on daman of ajir mushtarak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether a common hire (ajir mushtarak) is liable for loss and apply the mufta bihi ruling in practical scenarios.

Core Idea
A common hire does not guarantee loss; his hand is a trust, not a guarantee.

This lesson explores a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: is a common hire (ajir mushtarak) liable for property that perishes in his possession? You will learn the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and the final mufta bihi ruling, along with the effect of stipulating a guarantee in the contract. Understanding this dispute helps clarify how Hanafi scholars balance trust and liability in service contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is the common hire (ajir mushtarak) holding property for work. The dispute: does he guarantee loss?
Focus on the term 'daman' (guarantee/liability).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa: no guarantee unless transgression (ta'addi). His proof: the property is an amanah (trust), analogous to a deposit (wadi'ah). Also cites practice of Shurayh and narrations from 'Umar and 'Ali.
Trust (amanah) shifts only with transgression.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: guarantee for preventable loss, not for unpreventable. Their proof: the contract requires safekeeping; the hire benefits from wage, so he must guarantee if negligent.
They distinguish based on whether loss could be prevented.
4
Examine the effect of stipulating guarantee
If the contract stipulates guarantee for unpreventable loss: invalid by consensus. For preventable loss: Abu Hanifa says the condition invalidates the contract; Sahibayn say it is valid because the contract requires guarantee.
The difference hinges on whether the condition is 'required by the contract' (muqtada al-aqd).
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its authority
Later authorities (Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, authors of matns) upheld no guarantee even with stipulation. Fatwa is given accordingly. The authority weight is from mutakhkhirin.
This is the operative ruling for practice today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱] قوله : ولا يضمن ما هلك في يده...الخ ؛ سواء هلك بأمر يمكن التحرز عنه كالسرقة والغصب، أو بأمر لا يمكن التحرُّزُ عنه كالموت حتف الأنف، والحريق الغالب والغارة الغالبة، وهذا عند الإمام، وأحمد وإسحاق، والمزني، والشافعي في قول. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد : إن هلك بأمر لا يمكن التحرز عنه فلا ضمان عليه، وإن هلك بأمر يمكن التحرز عنه فعليه الضمان، والمالك بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه محمولاً وأعطاه الأجر، وإن شاء ضمنه غير معمول ولا أجر له، وبالتضمين قال مالك والشافعي له في قول.
[٢] قوله : وإن شرط عليه الضمان ؛ قال الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «شرح الكنز» : إن شرط الضمان على الأجير المشترك في العقد، فإن شرط عليه فيما لا يمكن التحرُّزُ عنه لا يجوز بالإجماع ؛ لأنه شرط لا يقتضيه العقد، وفيه منفعة لأحدهما ففسدت.
وبه يفتي (۱) ) . اعلم أن المتاعَ في يده أمانة عند أبي حنيفة ، ولا يضمن إلا بالتعدي كما في الوديعة، وعندهما يضمن إلا إذا هلك بسبب لا يمكن الاحتراز وإن شرط عليه فيما يمكن الاحتراز عنه، فعلى الخلاف، فعندهما يجوز؛ لأنه يقتضيه العقد عندهما، وعنده يفسد ؛ لأن العقد لا يقتضيه، فيكون اشترطه فيه مفسداً. انتهى.
[11 ] قوله : وبه يقتى ؛ أي يفتى بعدم وجوب الضمان، وإن شرط عليه الضمان وهو مروي عن عمر وعلي له ، وهو قول إبراهيمُ النَّخَعي له، كما روى عنهما مثل قولهما، وذكر الإتقاني عن «شرح الكافي»: «إنّ عليّاً لله كان يضمن الخياط والقصار ومثل ذلك من الصناع احتياطاً للنَّاس أن يضيعوا من أموالهم»، وهذا كان من رأيه بدأ ثم رجع. انتهى. وروى محمد ه من «الآثار»: عن أبي حنيفة عن حماد عن إبراهيم أن شريحاً لم يضمن أجيراً قط. انتهى. وكان حكم شريح بحضرة من الصحابة والتابعين من غير نكير، فحل محل الإجماع. وذكر في «الذخيرة» : كان الفقيه أبو جعفر سوى بين شرط الضمان وعدم الشرط، وكان يقول بعدم الضمان ؛ لأنَّ شرط الضمان في الأمانة مخالف لقضية الشرع فيكون باطلاً، وقال الفقيه أبو الليث : وبه نأخذ، وبه يفتى، وبه جزم أصحاب المتون، فكان هو المذهب خلافاً لما في «الأشباه» من أنه إن شرط ضمانه ضمن إجماعاً. انتهى. كما ذكرناه نقلا عن «التبيين».
.
وذكر في «الـعـدة»: إذا هلك العين عند الأجير المشترك نحو القصار والصباغ بعد الفراغ من العمل لا أجر له ؛ لأنه لم يُسَلّم العمل، ولا يضمن الثوب عند أبي حنيفة
[1] His statement: "And he does not guarantee what perishes in his hand...etc"; whether it perishes by an event that can be guarded against, like theft and usurpation, or by an event that cannot be guarded against, like natural death, overwhelming fire, and overwhelming attack. This is according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), Ahmad, Ishaq, al-Muzani, and al-Shafi'i in one view. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: If it perishes by an event that cannot be guarded against, there is no guarantee on him; if it perishes by an event that can be guarded against, then he is liable for guarantee. And the owner has the option: if he wishes, he may guarantee it as worked and give him the wage, or if he wishes, he may guarantee it as unworked and no wage for him. Malik and al-Shafi'i in one view held that he is liable. [2] His statement: "And if he stipulates a guarantee on him" – al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz said: If he stipulates a guarantee on the common hire in the contract, then if he stipulates it for what cannot be guarded against, it is not permissible by consensus, because it is a condition not required by the contract and contains benefit for one of them, so it becomes corrupt. And according to this, the fatwa is given. Know that the property in his hand is an amanah (trust) according to Abu Hanifa, and he does not guarantee except by transgression (ta'addi), as in the case of a deposit (wadi'ah). According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he guarantees unless it perishes due to a cause that cannot be guarded against. And if he stipulates a guarantee for what can be guarded against, then the difference applies: according to them it is valid because it is required by the contract in their view; according to him (Abu Hanifa) it corrupts the contract because the contract does not require it, so stipulating it would invalidate it. End. [11] His statement: "And by it the fatwa is given" – i.e., the fatwa is given that there is no obligation of guarantee, even if he stipulates a guarantee. And this is narrated from 'Umar and 'Ali, and it is the saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, as narrated from them like their saying. And al-Itqani mentioned from Sharh al-Kafi: 'Ali used to hold the tailor and the washer and similar artisans liable as a precaution for the people so that they would not waste their wealth.' This was his initial view, then he retracted. End. And Muhammad narrated in al-Athar from Abu Hanifa from Hammad from Ibrahim that Shurayh never held a hireling liable. End. And the judgment of Shurayh was in the presence of the Companions and Successors without any disapproval, so it took the place of consensus. And it is mentioned in al-Dhakhirah: The faqih Abu Ja'far made no distinction between stipulating guarantee and not stipulating, and he held that there is no guarantee, because stipulating a guarantee on a trust is contrary to the ruling of the Shari'ah, so it is invalid. And al-faqih Abu al-Layth said: We adopt this, and by it the fatwa is given, and the authors of the matns affirmed it, so it is the madhhab, contrary to what is in al-Ashbah that if he stipulates a guarantee, he is liable by consensus. End. As we have mentioned quoting from al-Tabyin. And it is mentioned in al-'Uddah: If the object perishes with the common hire like the washer and dyer after finishing the work, he has no wage because he did not deliver the work, and he does not guarantee the garment according to Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on the liability (daman) of a common hire (ajir mushtarak) for loss of the entrusted property. The matn states that the hire does not guarantee loss; the commentator expands by detailing the positions. According to Abu Hanifa (Imam), the hire does not guarantee at all, whether the loss is preventable or not, because the property is an amanah (trust) in his hand, like a deposit (wadi'ah). He only guarantees if he transgresses (ta'addi). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn) distinguish: if the loss is from an unpreventable cause, no guarantee; if preventable, he guarantees. The owner then has an option to take the item as worked (with wage) or unworked (no wage). The passage also discusses stipulating guarantee (shart al-daman). If stipulated for unpreventable loss, it is invalid by consensus. For preventable loss, Abu Hanifa says the contract is corrupted because the condition is not required by the contract; Sahibayn say it is valid because the contract requires guarantee in such cases. Later authorities (mutakhkhirin) like Abu Ja'far and Abu al-Layth upheld the position of no guarantee even with stipulation, and the fatwa is given accordingly. The passage also cites practice of Shurayh and narrations from 'Umar and 'Ali to support the no-guarantee position. A secondary point: if the object perishes after work completion but before delivery, the hire has no wage because he did not deliver, and he does not guarantee (at Abu Hanifa).

Key Terms
الضمان (al-daman): Legal liability for compensation when property is lost or damaged in one's possession.
التعدي (al-ta'addi): Transgression or negligence beyond normal care, e.g., using the item for other than intended purpose.
الأمانة (al-amanah): Property held in trust, where the holder is not liable for loss unless negligent.
الشرط (al-shart): A condition stipulated in the contract; if it contradicts the nature of the contract, it may invalidate it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative fatwa) position in this passage, what is the ruling on a common hire if the property perishes due to theft?
A) He guarantees if theft was preventable.
B) He does not guarantee at all.
C) He guarantees only if he stipulated so.
D) He guarantees but the owner has no option.

Key Takeaway
The common hire does not guarantee loss unless he transgresses, and this is the mufta bihi Hanafi position, even if guarantee is stipulated in the contract.

Liability of the Common Artisan (Ajir Mushtarak) – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining Hanafi dispute on liability of common artisan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the liability of the common artisan and evaluate the proofs and later fatwa preferences.

Core Idea
A common artisan is a trustee (amin) according to Abu Hanifa, but liable according to the Sahibayn; later Hanafi fatwas vary.

This lesson explores the Hanafi dispute over whether a common artisan (tailor, dyer, fuller) is liable for goods lost in his possession. The answer affects everyday transactions and balances trust in the artisan with protection of people's property. We will examine the core disagreement, the proof from the practice of Shuraih, and the subsequent diversity of fatwa among later Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their positions
First, locate the two main positions: Abu Hanifa holds the artisan is a trustee (amin) with no liability unless he transgresses; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold he is liable except for unavoidable loss.
2
Examine the proof from Shuraih
Read the narration that Shuraih never held an artisan liable, and note that this ruling occurred in the presence of Companions and Followers without disapproval, constituting a tacit consensus (ijma sukuti).
This is the key dalil for Abu Hanifa's position.
3
Analyze the logical reasoning behind each view
Consider the contractual logic: Abu Hanifa compares the artisan to a depositary (wadi'), so no liability; the Sahibayn argue that the contract of hire implies a guarantee of safekeeping, so liability follows unless the loss is unavoidable.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on stipulating guarantee
Understand the further disagreement: if the customer stipulates that the artisan guarantees the goods, Abu Hanifa says this invalidates the contract, while the Sahibayn say it is valid and enforceable.
5
Understand the later fatwa diversity and the exception for non-worked items
Survey the various fatwa positions: some follow Abu Hanifa absolutely, some follow the Sahibayn, some adopt compromise (sulh) on half value, and some distinguish based on the artisan's character. Also note the consensus that if the hired item is not worked upon (e.g., a raw material), there is no liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة / باب من الإجارة
وبه يفتي (۱) ). اعلم أن المتاعَ في يده أمانة عند أبي حنيفة ، ولا يضمن إلا بالتعدي كما في الوديعة، وعندهما يضمن إلا إذا هلك بسبب لا يمكن الاحتراز وإن شرط عليه فيما يمكن الاحتراز عنه، فعلى الخلاف، فعندهما يجوز؛ لأنه يقتضيه العقد عندهما، وعنده يفسد ؛ لأن العقد لا يقتضيه، فيكون اشترطه فيه مفسداً.
انتهى.
11 ] قوله : وبه يقتى ؛ أي يفتى بعدم وجوب الضمان، وإن شرط عليه الضمان وهو مروي عن عمر وعلي له ، وهو قول إبراهيمُ النَّخَعي له، كما روى عنهما مثل قولهما، وذكر الإتقاني عن «شرح الكافي»: «إنّ عليّاً لله كان يضمن الخياط والقصار ومثل ذلك من الصناع احتياطاً للنَّاس أن يضيعوا من أموالهم»، وهذا كان من رأيه بدأ ثم رجع. انتهى. وروى محمد ه من «الآثار»: عن أبي حنيفة عن حماد عن إبراهيم أن شريحاً لم يضمن أجيراً قط. انتهى. وكان حكم شريح بحضرة من الصحابة والتابعين من غير نكير، فحل محل الإجماع. وذكر في «الذخيرة» : كان الفقيه أبو جعفر سوى بين شرط الضمان وعدم الشرط، وكان يقول بعدم الضمان ؛ لأنَّ شرط الضمان في الأمانة مخالف لقضية الشرع فيكون باطلاً، وقال الفقيه أبو الليث : وبه نأخذ، وبه يفتى، وبه جزم أصحاب المتون، فكان هو المذهب خلافاً لما في «الأشباه» من أنه إن شرط ضمانه ضمن إجماعاً. انتهى. كما ذكرناه نقلا عن «التبيين».
.
وذكر في «الـعـدة»: إذا هلك العين عند الأجير المشترك نحو القصار والصباغ بعد الفراغ من العمل لا أجر له ؛ لأنه لم يُسَلّم العمل، ولا يضمن الثوب عند أبي حنيفة كالخاص، وعندهما يضمن صيانة لأموال الناس، وهذا مذهب عمر و ومذهب أبي حنيفة مذهب عطاء وطاؤوس ، وهما من كبار التابعين. وبعض العلماء أخذوا بقول أبي يوسف ومحمد احتشاماً لقول عمر وعلي ، وبعضهم أفتوا بالصلح عملاً بالقولين منهم شمس الأئمة الأُوزْجَنْدِي (1) وأئمة فرغانة على هذا ، وشيخ الإسلام عزّ الدين الكنديه وأئمة سمرقند كانوا يقولون بالصلح، والشيخ الإمام ظهير الدين أفتى بقول أبي حنيفة . قال صاحب «العدة» : فقلت لهم يوماً من قال منهم بالصلح هل يجب إجبار الخصم لو امتنع قال : كنت أفتي بالصلح بالجبر في الابتداء فرجعت عن هذا، وكان القاضي الإمام فخر الدين يفتي بقول أبي حنيفة .
وفي «فوائد» صاحب «المحيط»، وفتوى القاضي الإمام جلال الدين الريغدموني : أنه ينظر إن كان الأجير مصلحاً لا يجب الضمان ، وإن كان بخلافه يجب الضمان كما هو مذهبهما، وإن كان مستور الحال يؤمر بالصلح كذا في «الفصول العمادية». وقال الزيلعي في «شرح الكنز (۳) : وبقولهما يفتى اليوم لتغير أحوال الناس، وبه يحصل صيانة أموالهم. انتهى.
فقد عرفت أن أكثرهم يفتي بقول الإمام ، وهو عدم ا الضمان مطلقاً، وبعضهم : يفتي بقولهما مطلقاً، وبعضُهم : يفتى بالصلح على نصف القيمة مطلقاً، وبعضُهم يفتي بقولهما إن كان الأجير مصلحاً، وبقولهما إن كان غير مصلح، وبالصلح إن كان مستور الحال فقد اختلفت الافتاء. ثم اعلم أن محل الخلاف إذا كان المتاع المستأجر عليه محدثاً فيه عمل أما لو أعطاء مصحفاً ليعمل له غلافاً ، أو سيفاً ليعمل له جهازاً أو سكيناً ليعمل له نصاباً، فضاع المصحف أو السيف أو السكين فإنّه لا يضمن بالإجماع ؛ لأنه لم يستأجره على إيقاع العمل في ذلك، وإنّما استأجره على غيره، وفي الحقيقة هذا مما هلك في يده لا بعمله.
Book of Ijarah / Chapter from Ijarah. And with it is given fatwa. Know that the property in his hand is a trust according to Abu Hanifa, and he does not guarantee except by transgression as in the case of a deposit. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he guarantees except if it perishes due to a cause that cannot be avoided, even if he stipulated guarantee regarding what can be avoided. So it is based on the disagreement: according to them it is permissible because the contract necessitates it according to them; according to him (Abu Hanifa) it invalidates because the contract does not necessitate it, so stipulating it in the contract invalidates it. End. // His saying: 'And with it is given fatwa' means fatwa is given with non-obligation of guarantee, even if he stipulated guarantee upon him, and it is narrated from Umar and Ali, and it is the saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, as it is narrated from them like their saying. And al-Iqani mentioned from Sharh al-Kafi: 'Ali used to guarantee the tailor, the fuller, and the like of such craftsmen as a precaution for the people so that they not waste their wealth.' And this was his opinion, then he retracted. End. And Muhammad narrated from al-Athar: from Abu Hanifa from Hammad from Ibrahim that Shuraih never held an artisan liable. End. And the ruling of Shuraih was in the presence of the Companions and the Followers without any disapproval, so it took the place of consensus. And it is mentioned in al-Dhakhirah: the Faqih Abu Ja'far equated the condition of guarantee and the absence of condition, and he used to say non-liability because stipulating guarantee in a trust opposes the requirement of the Sharia, so it is void. And the Faqih Abu al-Layth said: we adopt this, and with it fatwa is given, and the authors of the texts affirmed it, so it is the madhhab contrary to what is in al-Ashbah that if he stipulates his guarantee, he guarantees by consensus. End. As we mentioned quoting from al-Tabyin. // And it is mentioned in al-Iddah: if the item perishes in the possession of the common artisan like the fuller and dyer after finishing the work, there is no wage for him because he did not deliver the work, and he does not guarantee the garment according to Abu Hanifa like the private artisan, and according to them he guarantees as a safeguard for the wealth of the people. And this is the madhhab of Umar, and the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is the madhhab of Ata and Tawus, and they are among the great Followers. And some scholars adopted the saying of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad out of respect for the saying of Umar and Ali, and some gave fatwa with compromise (sulh) acting on both sayings, among them Shams al-A'imma al-Ūzjandī and the scholars of Farghana upon this, and Shaykh al-Islam Izz al-Din al-Kindi and the scholars of Samarqand used to say with compromise, and al-Shaykh al-Imam Zahir al-Din gave fatwa with the saying of Abu Hanifa. The author of al-Iddah said: I said to them one day, 'Those among them who said with compromise, is it obligatory to force the opponent if he refuses?' He said: 'I used to give fatwa with compromise by force initially, then I retracted from this.' And al-Qadi al-Imam Fakhr al-Din used to give fatwa with the saying of Abu Hanifa. // And in Fawa'id of the author of al-Muhit, and the fatwa of al-Qadi al-Imam Jalal al-Din al-Righdamuni: that he looks: if the artisan is righteous, no guarantee is obligatory; and if contrary, guarantee is obligatory as per their madhhab; and if his state is unknown, he is ordered to compromise. Likewise in al-Fusul al-Imadiyyah. And al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz said: by their saying fatwa is given today due to changing circumstances of the people, and by it their wealth is safeguarded. End. // So you have known that most of them give fatwa with the saying of the Imam, which is absolute non-liability; and some give fatwa with their saying absolutely; and some give fatwa with compromise on half the value absolutely; and some give fatwa with their saying if the artisan is righteous, and with their saying if not righteous, and with compromise if his state is unknown. Thus the fatwas differed. Then know that the place of disagreement is if the hired property has work performed in it. As for if he gave him a mus'haf to make a cover for it, or a sword to make a scabbard, or a knife to make a handle, and the mus'haf, sword, or knife are lost, then he does not guarantee by consensus, because he did not hire him to perform work in it; rather, he hired him for something else, and in reality this is perished in his hand not due to his work.
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah discusses the liability (daman) of a common artisan (ajir mushtarak) such as a tailor, dyer, or fuller for goods in his possession. The text begins by stating the fatwa position: the artisan is considered a trustee (amin) according to Abu Hanifa, meaning he is not liable for loss unless he transgresses (ta'addi). This is similar to a deposit (wadi'ah). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that he is liable for loss except if the loss occurs from an unavoidable cause. The disagreement extends to stipulating guarantee: according to the Sahibayn, such a condition is valid because the contract implies liability; according to Abu Hanifa, it invalidates the contract because the contract does not imply liability. The text then cites the practice of Shuraih, who never held an artisan liable, and this was known to the Companions without disapproval, constituting a tacit consensus (ijma sukuti). The narration from Imam Muhammad's 'al-Athar' supports this. Later scholars differed: some upheld Abu Hanifa's view, some preferred the Sahibayn's view for public welfare, and many opted for compromise (sulh) to reconcile the two positions. The text notes that the disagreement is limited to cases where the hired item undergoes work directly; if the item is not worked upon (e.g., a raw material), there is consensus on no liability. This shows the nuanced application of Hanafi principles to protect both the artisan and the public.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A common artisan (e.g., tailor, dyer, fuller) who works for multiple customers, not exclusively for one.
ضمان (daman): Legal liability to compensate for loss or damage of property in one's possession.
أمانة (amanah): Trust; property in the artisan's hand is considered a trust, so no liability unless transgression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Abu Hanifa's ruling that the common artisan is not liable for loss without transgression?
A) A verse from the Quran
B) A hadith of the Prophet
C) The practice of Shuraih, accepted by the Companions
D) A consensus of the four schools

Key Takeaway
The liability of the common artisan is a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute; while Abu Hanifa's view treats the artisan as a trustee, the Sahibayn's view holds him liable for public welfare, and later fatwas often adopt the latter due to changing circumstances.

Liability of a Hired Worker: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Fatwa Variations
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ajir's liability with fatwa variations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three positions (Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, sulh) regarding the liability of a hired worker (ajir) and determine which fatwa applies under different conditions based on the text.

Core Idea
A hired worker's liability is disputed: no liability (Abu Hanifa), liability for negligence (Sahibayn), or half-compromise (sulh).

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when a worker hired to perform a specific job (ajir khas) loses or damages the item, is he liable? Abu Hanifa, following earlier tabi'un, says no, unless he directly destroys it. His disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, citing the practice of Caliphs Umar and Ali, hold him liable for negligence. Later Hanafi scholars differed on which view to adopt, with some ordering a compromise payment of half the value. The text also clarifies an important consensus: if the item was given for a different purpose (e.g., making a cover for a Quran), the worker is not liable at all.

Guided Path
1
State the three positions
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa (no liability), Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (liability if negligent), and the compromise view (sulh: pay half).
The text also mentions a consensus exception for items given for a different purpose.
2
Map the fatwa variations
Note that later scholars adopted different positions: some followed Abu Hanifa (e.g., Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani), some followed the Sahibayn (e.g., al-Zaylai), and some ordered sulh across the board or conditionally based on the worker's character.
Al-Zaylai argued that changing times require following the Sahibayn to protect people's wealth.
3
Identify the consensus exception
The dispute only applies when the worker performs work on the specific hired item. If the item is given for a different purpose (e.g., giving a Quran for a cover), the worker is a mere trustee and no liability attaches by consensus.
This is a key condition for the dispute's application.

Source Text

زبدة النهاية لعمدة الرعاية كالخاص، وعندهما يضمن صيانة لأموال الناس، وهذا مذهب عمر و ومذهب أبي حنيفة مذهب عطاء وطاؤوس ، وهما من كبار التابعين. وبعض العلماء أخذوا بقول أبي يوسف ومحمد احتشاماً لقول عمر وعلي ، وبعضهم أفتوا بالصلح عملاً بالقولين منهم شمس الأئمة الأُوزْجَنْدِي (1) وأئمة فرغانة على هذا ، وشيخ الإسلام عزّ الدين الكنديه وأئمة سمرقند كانوا يقولون بالصلح، والشيخ الإمام ظهير الدين أفتى بقول أبي حنيفة . قال صاحب «العدة» : فقلت لهم يوماً من قال منهم بالصلح هل يجب إجبار الخصم لو امتنع قال : كنت أفتي بالصلح بالجبر في الابتداء فرجعت عن هذا، وكان القاضي الإمام فخر الدين يفتي بقول أبي حنيفة . وفي «فوائد» صاحب «المحيط»، وفتوى القاضي الإمام جلال الدين الريغدموني : أنه ينظر إن كان الأجير مصلحاً لا يجب الضمان ، وإن كان بخلافه يجب الضمان كما هو مذهبهما، وإن كان مستور الحال يؤمر بالصلح كذا في «الفصول العمادية». وقال الزيلعي في «شرح الكنز (۳) : وبقولهما يفتى اليوم لتغير أحوال الناس، وبه يحصل صيانة أموالهم. انتهى. فقد عرفت أن أكثرهم يفتي بقول الإمام ، وهو عدم الضمان مطلقاً، وبعضهم : يفتي بقولهما مطلقاً، وبعضُهم : يفتى بالصلح على نصف القيمة مطلقاً، وبعضُهم يفتي بقولهما إن كان الأجير مصلحاً، وبقولهما إن كان غير مصلح، وبالصلح إن كان مستور الحال فقد اختلفت الافتاء. ثم اعلم أن محل الخلاف إذا كان المتاع المستأجر عليه محدثاً فيه عمل أما لو أعطاء مصحفاً ليعمل له غلافاً ، أو سيفاً ليعمل له جهازاً أو سكيناً ليعمل له نصاباً، فضاع المصحف أو السيف أو السكين فإنّه لا يضمن بالإجماع ؛ لأنه لم يستأجره على إيقاع العمل في ذلك، وإنّما استأجره على غيره، وفي الحقيقة هذا مما هلك في يده لا بعمله.
Cream of the outcome for the foundation of the care: Like the special (ajir), and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he guarantees to protect people's wealth. This is the madhhab of Umar and Ali, and the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is the madhhab of Ata and Tawus, and they are from the great tabi'un. Some scholars took the saying of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad out of respect for the saying of Umar and Ali, and some gave fatwa of compromise (sulh) acting on both sayings, among them Shams al-A'imma al-Uzjandi and the imams of Farghana are upon this, and Shaykh al-Islam Izz al-Din al-Kindi and the imams of Samarqand used to say with compromise, and Shaykh Imam Zahir al-Din gave fatwa with the saying of Abu Hanifa. And in Fawa'id by the author of al-Muhit, and the fatwa of Qadi Imam Jalal al-Din al-Righdamuni: that he looks: if the worker is righteous, no liability; and if contrary, liability as is their madhhab; and if his state is unknown, he is ordered to compromise, as in al-Fusul al-Imadiyya. And al-Zaylai said in Sharh al-Kanz: and with their saying fatwa is given today due to change of people's conditions, and by it protection of their wealth is achieved. End. So you have known that most of them give fatwa with the saying of the Imam, which is absolute non-liability; and some give fatwa with their saying absolutely; and some give fatwa with compromise on half the value absolutely; and some give fatwa with their saying if the worker is righteous, and with their saying if he is otherwise, and with compromise if his state is unknown—so the fatwas differed. Then know that the place of dispute is when the hired item has work done on it. As for if he gave him a mushaf to make a cover for it, or a sword to make a sheath for it, or a knife to make a handle for it, and the mushaf, sword, or knife is lost, then there is no liability by consensus, because he did not hire him to perform work on it, but rather he hired him for something else, and in reality this is something that perished in his hand not by his work.
Source pages p. 584

Commentary
This passage discusses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: the liability (daman) of a hired worker (ajir) when the item he is working on is lost or damaged. Abu Hanifa holds that the worker is not liable at all, likening him to a trustee (amin) unless he directly destroys the item. His view follows the early tabi'un Ata and Tawus. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold the worker liable if he fails to safeguard the item, drawing an analogy to a paid deposit (wadee'a bi-ujr) where the depositary is responsible. They also cite the practice of Caliphs Umar and Ali. The text then shows how later scholars differed: some followed Abu Hanifa (e.g., Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani), some followed the Sahibayn (e.g., al-Zaylai, citing changed social conditions), and some adopted a compromise (sulh) ordering the worker to pay half the value, especially when the worker's reliability is unknown. Important clarifications: the dispute only applies when the worker performs work on the specific hired item (e.g., tailoring cloth). If the item is given for a different purpose (e.g., making a cover for a Quran), the item is merely an amanah (trust) in his hands, and loss does not entail liability by consensus. Also, the dispute is limited to valid (sahih) hire contracts; if the hire is void (fasid), there is no liability by agreement because the item becomes a trust.

Key Terms
أجير (ajir): A worker hired to perform a specific task on a specific item (ajir khas)
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage
صلح (sulh): Compromise; here meaning a settlement ordering the worker to pay half the value of the lost item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the condition for the dispute on the ajir's liability to apply?
A) The worker is hired to work on a specific item and performs work on it.
B) The worker is hired for any task without specification.
C) The item is given to the worker for a different purpose than working on it.
D) The hire contract is void (fasid).

Key Takeaway
The liability of a hired worker (ajir khas) is disputed in the Hanafi school, with three possible rulings: no liability (Abu Hanifa), liability (Sahibayn), or compromise (sulh), and the fatwa applied depends on the worker's reliability and societal conditions.
