Owner's Option When a Common Carrier Breaks Goods
Explaining the option given to the owner when a carrier breaks a jar in transit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two compensation options available to an owner when a common carrier breaks goods by his fault, and identify the difference in liability between Abu Hanifa and the two students.

Core Idea
An owner can claim full value at loading (no wages) or value at breakage (with wages) if the carrier caused the breakage.

When a common carrier (ajir mushtarak) accidentally breaks goods he is transporting, the owner is not left without recourse. This lesson explains the option the owner has to claim compensation, and also highlights an internal Hanafi disagreement on whether the goods are a trust or guaranteed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the incident
The scenario involves a jar (denn) being carried by a common carrier (hammal) on the Euphrates road. The jar breaks.
2
State the two compensation options
If the breakage is due to the carrier's action (e.g., slipping), the owner can either: (1) claim the jar's value at the place of loading and pay no wages, or (2) claim the value at the place of breakage and pay wages proportionally.
3
Determine the condition for these options
These options apply only when the carrier caused the breakage by his own action. If it was due to external factors, different rules apply.
The condition is the carrier's fault (bi-sun'ihi).
4
Note the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two students
When breakage is not by the carrier's action, Abu Hanifa holds the goods are a trust (amanah) so no liability. The two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold the carrier liable but without giving the owner a choice—the owner must claim value at breakage and pay wages.
The mufta bihi position is that of the two students.
5
Understand the reasoning behind the option
The option exists because the carrying act is considered a single continuous action. The owner may regard the whole transport as transgression from the start (so full value, no wages) or as initially permitted but becoming transgression at breakage (so breakage value, with wages).
This is a legal interpretation of the nature of the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : فإن انكسر...الخ ; يعني فلو انكسر دنّ في طريق الفرات، فللمالك أن يضمن الحمّال قيمة ذلك الدنّ التي تقوم في مكان حمله ، ولا أجر له، أو ضَمِنَ قيمته في مكان كسره ، وللحمال الأجر بحسابه. وهذا إذا كان الكسرُ بصنعه بأن زَلِق أو عَثِر ، وإن كان من غير صنعه بأن زحمه الناس فانكسر فلا يضمن عند الإمام ; لأنَّ المتاع أمانة عنده ، وعندهما يضمن قيمته في موضع انكسر ; لأنه سليم العمل بإيصاله بملكه، فيعطيه أجره، ولا يخير في هذه الصورة عندهما ; لأن العين مضمونة على الأجير المشترك عندهما. كما صرحوا به. في طريق الفراتِ ضَمِنَ الحمّالُ قيمتَهُ في مكانٍ حَمْلِه بلا أجر، أو في موضع كُسِرَ مع حصة أجره ) ; لأنه لما وجب الضمان فله وجهان : . أحدهما : أن يجعل فعله تعدياً من الإبتداء، فإنّ الحمل شيء واحد. ٢. أو يجعل الأول بإذنِه ، ثُمَّ صارَ تعدِّياً عند الكسر فيختار أياً شاء. الأجير الخاص [١]قوله : في طريق الفرات ; ذكر الفرات للشهرة ، فإنّ الدنان تباع هناك، فذكره ليس بقيد احتراز [٢] قوله : لأنه لما وجب الضمان ; ووجه : وجوب الضمان : أنه تلف بفعله، فإنّ الداخل تحت العقدِ إنّما هو عمل سليم، والعمل المفسد غير داخل تحته فيضمن. فله وجهان ; تقرير وجه الخيار : إنّ الدنَّ إذا انكسر في الطريق، والحالُ [٣] قوله : أن الحمل شيء واحد حكماً، إذ الحملُ المستحق بالعقـد مـا ينتفع به، وهو أن يجعله محمولاً إلى موضع عينه ، فظهر أنّ الإنكسار وقع تعدياً من الابتداء، فيكون انكساره في الطريق كانكساره ابتداء. وله وجه آخر : وهو أنّ ابتداء الحمل حصل بأمره ، فلم يكن تعدياً، وإنما صار تعدياً عند الكسر ، ولما كان جهة الضمان دائرة بين الأمرين فيميل إلى أيهما شاء، فإن مال إلى كونِهِ متعدِّياً ضمن قيمته في الابتداء ، ولا يجب الأجر ; لأنه تبين أنه كان متعدِّياً من الابتداء، وإن مال إلى كونه مأذوناً فيه في الابتداء، وإنما صار متعدياً عند الكسر ، ضمنه قيمته في موضع الكسر وأعطاه أجرته بحسابه.
His saying: 'for if it breaks... etc.' means: if a jar breaks on the Euphrates road, the owner may hold the carrier liable for the value of that jar as valued at the place of loading, and no wages for him, or he may hold him liable for its value at the place of breakage, and for the carrier wages proportionally. This is when the breakage was by his action, such as he slipped or stumbled. But if it was not by his action, such as people crowding him and it broke, then he is not liable according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because the goods are a trust with him. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he guarantees its value at the place of breakage, because he is performing the work soundly by delivering it by his ownership, so he gives him his wages, and he is not given a choice in this case according to them, because the article is guaranteed upon the common carrier according to them, as they have clarified. 'On the Euphrates road, the carrier guarantees its value at the place of loading without wages, or at the place of breakage with a portion of his wages.' Because when liability is established, he has two aspects: one is to consider his action as transgression from the beginning, because the carrying is one thing; or to consider the initial act as permitted, then it became transgression at the breakage, so he chooses whichever he wishes. The specific employee... His saying: 'on the Euphrates road' – he mentioned Euphrates for fame, since jars are sold there, so mentioning it is not a restrictive condition. His saying: 'because when liability is established' – the reason for liability: it was destroyed by his action, because what is included under the contract is only sound work, and corrupting work is not included under it, so he is liable. So he has two aspects. Explanation of the choice: if the jar breaks on the road, and the situation... His saying: 'the carrying is one thing legally' because the carrying owed by the contract is what benefits, which is to make it transported to a specific place. So it appears that the breakage occurred as a transgression from the beginning, so its breakage on the road is like its breakage at the beginning. And he has another aspect: the beginning of the carrying occurred by his order, so it was not transgression, but it became transgression at the breakage. Since the direction of liability revolves between the two, he may incline to whichever he wishes. If he inclines to it being transgression, he guarantees its value at the beginning, and wages are not due, because it becomes clear that he was transgressor from the beginning. If he inclines to it being permitted at the beginning and became transgression at the breakage, he guarantees its value at the place of breakage and gives him his wages proportionally.
Source pages p. 590

Commentary
This passage deals with the liability of a common carrier (ajir mushtarak) when the goods he carries are broken. The scholar explains that the owner has an option: either to claim full value of the goods as at the place of loading (without paying any wages), or to claim the value at the place of breakage (and pay wages proportionally). This applies if the breakage was caused by the carrier's own negligence (e.g., slipping). If it was due to external factors (e.g., crowd pressure), Abu Hanifa holds the goods are a trust, so no liability; the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold the carrier liable because he is a common carrier, but they do not give the owner a choice – he must claim at the breakage value and pay wages. The reason for the option when the carrier is at fault is that the act of carrying is one continuous action; one can view the whole transport as a single act of transgression from the start, or as initially permitted but becoming transgressive at the moment of breakage. The owner may choose whichever interpretation benefits him.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A common carrier who works for multiple people, not exclusively for one.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Claim double the value
D) No choice, only the carrier decides

Key Takeaway
The owner of damaged goods has the right to choose how to claim compensation from a common carrier who caused the damage by his own action.

Definition of the Specific Employee (Ajir Khas)
Defining the specific employee and his characteristics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the specific employee and identify which hiring arrangements fall under this category.

Core Idea
A specific employee is dedicated to one employer for a fixed time, even if jointly hired.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between a specific employee (ajir khas) and a common employee (ajir mushtarak). This lesson clarifies the definition from Tanwir al-Absar and al-Hamawi, including a key nuance about joint hiring that prevents misclassification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
From Tanwir al-Absar: the ajir khas is one who works for a single person for a specified period by assignment. Note the elements: exclusivity to one employer, fixed period, and assignment.
2
Refine with al-Hamawi's addition
Al-Hamawi notes that later scholars added 'or what is in its ruling' to cover cases where multiple persons jointly hire a worker.
3
Understand the joint hiring exception
The phrase prevents an objection: if two or three people hire a slave for their service or to graze their sheep, the slave is still an ajir khas because the employers act as a single unit.
The employers are treated as one entity for the purpose of exclusivity.
4
Apply the definition
Given a scenario, determine whether the worker is an ajir khas by checking: is there a single employer (or a group acting jointly) and a fixed period?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأجير الخاص ; قال في تنوير الأبصار: هو من يعمل لواحد عملاً مؤقتاً بالتخصيص. انتهى. وقال الحَمَوِيّ : عرَّفه بعض المتأخرين بأنه من يعمل لواحد أو ما في حكمه عملاً مؤقتا بالتخصيص، وإنّما قال : أو ما في حكمه ; لئلا يرد عليه ما لو استأجر اثنان أو ثلاثة عبداً لخدمتهم مدة أو لرعي غنمهم ، فإنّ الظاهر أنه أجير خاص.
The specific employee. He said in Tanwir al-Absar: He is one who works for a single person for a specified period by assignment. End. And al-Hamawi said: Some later scholars defined him as one who works for one person or what is in its ruling, for a specified period by assignment. He said 'or what is in its ruling' to avoid objection regarding the case where two or three people hire a slave for their service for a period or for grazing their sheep, for it is apparent that he is a specific employee.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage defines the 'ajir khas' (specific employee). According to the definition from Tanwir al-Absar, he is someone who works exclusively for one employer for a specified period. Al-Hamawi adds that the definition includes working for more than one person if they are jointly hiring, because the arrangement is essentially the same – the employee is dedicated to their service for a fixed time.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A specific employee who is hired exclusively by one employer (or joint employers) for a fixed period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hamawi's refinement, which of the following is considered an ajir khas?
A) A worker hired by three unrelated individuals, each for independent tasks.
B) A worker hired by two brothers jointly to care for their shared property for a month.
C) A worker who works for a daily wage for different clients each day.
D) A worker who is hired without a fixed period.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of ajir khas includes joint hiring by multiple parties acting as one, preserving the characteristic of exclusivity that determines liability as a trustee.

Porter's Liability for Broken Jars on the Euphrates
States the ruling on porter's liability and two legal analyses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a porter's liability for a broken jar and explain the two legal analyses that give the hirer an option.

Core Idea
A porter's liability depends on whether the trespass occurred at the start or only at the break; the hirer may choose.

In Hanafi contract law, a hired porter who breaks a jar during transport is liable for compensation, but the amount and wage adjustment depend on a nuanced legal analysis. The passage from al-Hidayah presents the ruling and two ways to view the porter's act, giving the hirer an option. This lesson unpacks that ruling and the reasoning behind the option.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the hukm (ruling) stated in the passage? The porter is liable (yadman) for the value of the jar. Two options exist for the hirer.
The ruling is a daman obligation.
2
Understand the two options
The hirer may demand (a) the full value at the loading place without paying any wage, or (b) the value at the break place while paying a proportional wage.
These correspond to two legal analyses.
3
Analyze the first wajh
The first analysis: the entire act of carrying is treated as a single undertaking. If the break occurred, the porter was trespassory (mut'a'ddin) from the start, so no wage is due.
This view treats the break as evidence that the whole act was unauthorized.
4
Analyze the second wajh
The second analysis: the initial lifting was permitted, but trespass occurred only at the moment of break. Thus the porter is entitled to wage up to that point, and liability is limited to the break location.
This view segregates the act.
5
Note the practical consequence
The hirer may choose whichever analysis benefits him. The mention of Euphrates is for illustration, not a restriction.
This flexibility is a distinctive Hanafi feature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في طريق الفراتِ ضَمِنَ الحمّالُ قيمتَهُ في مكانٍ حَمْلِه بلا أجر، أو في موضع كُسِرَ مع حصة أجره، الأجير الخاص
[۱]
في طريق الفراتِ ضَمِنَ الحمّالُ قيمتَهُ في مكانٍ حَمْلِه بلا أجر، أو في موضع كُسِرَ مع حصة أجره ) ؛ لأنه لما وجب الضمان فله وجهان :
[Y]
. أحدهما : أن يجعل فعله تعدياً من الإبتداء، فإنّ الحمل شيء واحد. ٢. أو يجعل الأول بإذنِه ، ثُمَّ صارَ تعدِّياً عند الكسر فيختار أياً شاء.
الأجير الخاص [١]قوله : في طريق الفرات ؛ ذكر الفرات للشهرة ، فإنّ الدنان تباع هناك، فذكره
ليس بقيد احتراز
[٢] قوله : لأنه لما وجب الضمان ؛ ووجه : وجوب الضمان : أنه تلف بفعله، فإنّ
الداخل تحت العقدِ إنّما هو عمل سليم، والعمل المفسد غير داخل تحته فيضمن. فله وجهان ؛ تقرير وجه الخيار : إنّ الدنَّ إذا انكسر في الطريق، والحالُ [٣] قوله : أن الحمل شيء واحد حكماً، إذ الحملُ المستحق بالعقـد مـا ينتفع به، وهو أن يجعله محمولاً إلى موضع عينه ، فظهر أنّ الإنكسار وقع تعدياً من الابتداء، فيكون انكساره في
الطريق كانكساره ابتداء. وله وجه آخر : وهو أنّ ابتداء الحمل حصل بأمره ، فلم يكن تعدياً، وإنما صار تعدياً عند الكسر ، ولما كان جهة الضمان دائرة بين الأمرين فيميل إلى أيهما شاء، فإن مال إلى كونِهِ متعدِّياً ضمن قيمته في الابتداء ، ولا يجب الأجر ؛ لأنه تبين أنه كان متعدِّياً من الابتداء، وإن مال إلى كونه مأذوناً فيه في الابتداء، وإنما صار متعدياً عند الكسر ، ضمنه قيمته في موضع الكسر وأعطاه أجرته بحسابه.
On the Euphrates road, the porter is liable for its value at the place of loading without wage, or at the place where it broke with a portion of his wage. This is because once liability is established, there are two aspects: One: that his act is considered trespassory from the beginning, for carrying is one thing. Two: or the first part is considered permissible by his permission, then it became trespassory at the break, so he may choose whichever he wishes.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding a porter hired to carry jars along the Euphrates. If the jar breaks, the hirer has an option. He can demand the full value of the jar from the porter without paying any wage, because the entire act of carrying is treated as trespassory from the start. Alternatively, he can demand the value at the point of break, but must pay the proportional wage. The reason for this option is that the porter's act can be analyzed in two ways: either the whole carrying is one integral act that became trespassory at inception, or the initial lifting was lawful and the trespass occurred only at the moment of break. The hirer may choose whichever analysis benefits him. The commentary explains that the mention of the Euphrates is not a restriction but due to common practice where jars are sold there. Liability arises because the contract only covers sound work, not defective work that destroys the object.

Key Terms
تعدي (ta'di): Transgression beyond the limits of permission; in contract, acting contrary to the agreed terms causing damage.
ضمان (daman): Liability to pay compensation for damage or loss caused by one's action.
دن (dann): A large jar used for storing liquids, commonly carried by porters in the Euphrates region.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The jar's value is always estimated at the place of loading.
D) The porter has a choice to pay or not.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives the hirer an option in porter liability cases, reflecting a flexible approach to assessing ta'di and wage compensation.

The Special Hireling (Ajir Khas): Wage Entitlement by Self-Surrender
Defines ajir khas and states his wage entitlement upon self-surrender

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ajir khas, state the condition for his wage entitlement, and distinguish him from ajir mushtarak.

Core Idea
A special hireling earns his wage simply by making himself available – actual work is not required.

In Hanafi fiqh, hire contracts (ijara) distinguish between two types of hirelings: the special hireling (ajir khas) and the common hireling (ajir mushtarak). This lesson defines the ajir khas and explains the crucial ruling that his wage is earned upon self-surrender (taslim al-nafs), even if no work is performed. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying ijara rulings in practice.

Guided Path
1
Define the special hireling
From the text, extract the definition from Tanwir al-Absar and the refinement by later scholars: one who works exclusively for a single person (or its like) for a specified time by assignment.
Exclusivity is the key element.
2
Identify the feature of exclusivity
The ajir khas cannot work for others because his benefits (manafi‘) are dedicated to the hirer.
This makes the wage in exchange for availability, not output.
3
State the ruling on wage entitlement
The special hireling is entitled to the full wage by surrendering himself for the period, whether he works or not.
Self-surrender means making oneself available and able to work.
4
Note exceptions: impediments
If an impediment (e.g., illness, rain) prevents the hireling from working or he refuses, there is no effective self-surrender, so no wage.
Al-Ayni confirms this condition.
5
Contrast with the common hireling
The ajir mushtarak must actually deliver the work to earn his wage; the contract ends upon completion.
Example: a tailor who sews but a third party tears the garment loses his wage because delivery did not occur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأجير الخاص [١]قوله : في طريق الفرات ؛ ذكر الفرات للشهرة ، فإنّ الدنان تباع هناك، فذكره ليس بقيد احتراز
[٤]قوله : الأجير الخاص ؛ قال في تنوير الأبصار» (۱) : هو من يعمل لواحد عملاً مؤقتاً بالتخصيص. انتهى. وقال الحَمَوِيّ : عرَّفه بعض المتأخرين بأنه من يعمل لواحد أو ما في حكمه عملاً مؤقتا بالتخصيص، وإنّما قال : أو ما في حكمه ؛ لئلا يرد عليه ما لو استأجر اثنان أو ثلاثة عبداً لخدمتهم مدة أو لرعي غنمهم ، فإنّ الظاهر أنه أجير خاص.
[١] قوله : يستحق ... الخ ؛ يعني إنّ الأجير الخاص يستحق الأجرة بتسليم نفسه للعمل في مدة الإجارة سواء عمل أو لم يعمل ، كمَن استؤجر سنة للخدمة أو لرعي الغنم، ويسمّى ذلك الأجير الخاص أجير وحد ؛ لأنه يختص به الواحد، وهو المستأجر، وليس له أن يعمل لغيره ؛ لأن منافعه صارت مستحقة له، والأجر مقابل بها، ولما كان الأجر مقابلاً بالمنافع يبقى الأجر مستحقاً، وإن نقض العمل.

[٣]قوله : كالأجير للخدمة...الخ ; قال في «الدرر » ) : اعلم أن الأجير للخدمة أو
The special hireling: his saying: on the Euphrates road; he mentioned the Euphrates for notoriety, for jars are sold there, so its mention is not a restrictive condition. His saying: the special hireling; said in Tanwir al-Absar: he is one who works for one person for a specified time by assignment. End. And al-Hamawi said: some later scholars defined him as one who works for one person or its like for a specified time by assignment; they said 'or its like' to avoid including cases where two or three hire a slave for their service for a period or for grazing their sheep, for apparently he is a special hireling. His saying: He is entitled... meaning that the special hireling is entitled to the wage by surrendering himself for work during the hire period, whether he works or not, such as one hired for a year for service or for grazing sheep. He is called a special hireling (ajir wahd) because he is exclusive to one, the hirer, and he may not work for others because his benefits have become due to the hirer, and the wage is in exchange for them. Since the wage is in exchange for the benefits, the wage remains due even if the work is undone. Unlike the common hireling, for it is related from Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) concerning a tailor who sewed a man's garment for a wage, then a person tore it before the owner took possession; there is no wage for the tailor because he did not deliver the work to the owner, and the tailor is not compelled to redo the work because if compelled, it would be by the contract that occurred between them, and that contract ended with the completion of the work. But if the tailor himself tore it, he must redo the work because he undid his work, so it becomes as if he did not sew. Unlike the stranger, for if he tore it, it cannot be considered that the tailor did not work at all. His saying: even if he does not work; meaning he surrendered himself and did not work while able; but if he refrained from work and the period passed, or was unable to work due to an excuse and the period passed, he is not entitled to the wage because there was no surrender of self. Thus in al-Kifaya. And al-Ayni said: he is entitled as long as no impediment prevents him from work, like illness, rain, and the like that prevent ability to work. End. His saying: like the hireling for service; said in al-Durar: know that the hireling for service or...
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage defines the 'ajir khas' (special hireling) and explains his wage entitlement. The definition from Tanwir al-Absar states that a special hireling is one who works exclusively for a single person for a specified time period. The definition is refined to include cases where multiple persons jointly hire a slave for their collective service, as he is still considered a special hireling since he cannot work for outsiders. The key ruling is that a special hireling becomes entitled to the full wage merely by making himself available for work during the contracted period, regardless of whether actual work is performed. This is because the wage is in exchange for the availability of his benefits (manafi'), which are exclusively dedicated to the hirer. The text contrasts with the 'ajir mushtarak' (common hireling), who is only paid upon actual delivery of the work. An example is given from Imam Muhammad: if a tailor sews a garment but a third party tears it before delivery, the tailor loses his wage because he did not deliver the completed work. However, if the tailor himself tears it, he must redo the work. The passage also clarifies that the wage entitlement for the special hireling is contingent on genuine surrender of self; if he refuses to work or is unable to work due to an excuse (e.g., illness, rain), he does not deserve the wage because effective surrender did not occur.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A person hired to work exclusively for one employer (or its like) for a specified period, dedicated personal service.
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A person hired for a specific task, not dedicated exclusively; wage is due upon completion and delivery of work.
تسليم النفس (taslim al-nafs): Surrendering oneself for service; making oneself available to work during the hire period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) If he surrenders himself but is prevented from work by an impediment like illness or rain.
C) If he works but the work is defective.
D) If he works for another person without permission.

Key Takeaway
An ajir khas earns his wage by making himself available; actual performance is irrelevant unless an impediment prevents availability.

Specific Hireling's Entitlement to Wages
Explaining that a specific hireling earns wages by surrendering himself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a specific hireling (ajir khas) earns wages by surrendering himself, distinguish this from a common hireling (ajir mushtarak), and apply the condition of ability to work.

Core Idea
A specific hireling is paid for his availability, not his work.

Have you ever wondered if a worker must actually perform the job to be paid? In the Hanafi school, a specific hireling – one who works exclusively for a single employer – is entitled to his wages simply by making himself available. This lesson unpacks that rule, its rationale, and the crucial exception when work is impossible due to an excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening statement: the specific hireling deserves wages by surrendering himself for the contract period, whether he works or not.
Focus on 'yastahiqq' and 'taslim nafs'.
2
Understand the rationale
The wage is in exchange for the hireling's benefits (manafi'), which are dedicated to the hirer upon surrender.
This is a key principle: benefits, not output, are the consideration.
3
Contrast with the common hireling
The tailor example shows that a common hireling only earns wages by delivering the completed work.
Note the different outcome if the tailor himself tears the garment vs. a stranger.
4
Analyze the condition of ability
The passage clarifies that surrender requires ability to work. If the hireling refrains or is unable (e.g., illness), surrender is incomplete and no wage is due.
Quotes from Al-Kifayah and Al-Ayni on excuses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : يستحق ... الخ ; يعني إنّ الأجير الخاص يستحق الأجرة بتسليم نفسه للعمل في مدة الإجارة سواء عمل أو لم يعمل ، كمَن استؤجر سنة للخدمة أو لرعي الغنم، ويسمّى ذلك الأجير الخاص أجير وحد ; لأنه يختص به الواحد، وهو المستأجر، وليس له أن يعمل لغيره ; لأن منافعه صارت مستحقة له، والأجر مقابل بها، ولما كان الأجر مقابلاً بالمنافع يبقى الأجر مستحقاً، وإن نقض العمل.

بخلاف الأجير المشترك، فإنه روي عن محمد الله في خياط خاط ثوب رجل بأجرٍ ففتقه رجل قبل أن يقبض ربُّ الثوب فلا أجر للخياط ; لأنه لم يُسلّم العمل إلى ربِّ الثوب، ولا يجبر الخياط على إعادة العمل ; لأنه لو أجبر عليه إنما يجبر بحكم العقدِ الذي جرى بينهما، وذلك العقد قد انتهى بتمام العمل ، وإن كان الخياط هو الذي فتق فعليه إعادة العمل ; لأنه نقض عمله فصار كأن لم يخط ، بخلاف الأجنبي فإنّه إذا فتقه لم يمكن أن يجعل كأن الخياط لم يعمل أصلاً.

قوله : وإن لم يعمل ; أي سلّم نفسه ولم يعمل مع التمكن أما إذا امتنع من العمل ومضت المدة أو لم يتمكن من العمل لعذر ، ومضت المدة لم يستحق الأجر ; لأنه لم يوجد تسليم النفس. كذا في «الكفاية» ; ولذا قال العيني : فيستحقه ما لم يمنعه من العمل مانع ، كالمرض والمطر ونحو ذلك مما يمنع التمكن من العمل. انتهى.

قوله : كالأجير للخدمة...الخ ; قال في «الدرر » : اعلم أن الأجير للخدمة أو لرعي الغنم، وسمي أجير وحد. انتهى.
His statement: 'He deserves the wage... etc.' Means the specific hireling deserves the wage by surrendering himself for work during the hire period, whether he works or not, like one hired for a year for service or herding sheep. And that specific hireling is called 'ajir wahd' because he is exclusively for one (the hirer), and he may not work for others because his benefits have become due to him, and the wage is in exchange for them. Since the wage corresponds to benefits, the wage remains due even if the work is undone. Unlike the common hireling: it is narrated from Muhammad al-Shaybani concerning a tailor who sewed a man's garment for a wage, then a person tore it before the garment's owner took possession—the tailor has no wage because he did not deliver the work to the owner, and the tailor is not compelled to redo the work because if compelled it would be by the contract, but the contract ended with completion of the work. If the tailor himself tore it, he must redo it because he undid his work, making it as if he never sewed. If a stranger tore it, he cannot be treated as if the tailor never worked at all. His statement: 'And if he did not work' i.e., he surrendered himself but did not work while able. If he refrained from work and the period passed, or was unable due to an excuse and the period passed, he does not deserve the wage because surrender of self did not occur. Thus in al-Kifayah. Al-Ayni said: He deserves it as long as no preventing factor like illness or rain prevents him from ability to work. End. His statement: 'Like the hireling for service.. etc.' He said in al-Durar: Know that the hireling for service or herding sheep is only a specific hireling if it is stipulated that he not serve others or herd for others, or if the period is mentioned first, like hiring a shepherd for a month to herd named sheep for a known wage—he is a specific hireling from the start of the statement. End.
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the ruling that a specific hireling (ajir khas, also called ajir wahd) is entitled to his wage simply by making himself available for work during the contract period, whether he actually works or not. The reason is that the wage is in exchange for the hireling's benefits (manafi'), and once he surrenders his time and availability, the wage becomes due. He cannot work for others because his benefits are exclusively for the hirer. The passage contrasts this with a common hireling (ajir mushtarak), using the example of a tailor: if a stranger tears the garment after the work is complete but before delivery, the tailor has no wage because he hasn't delivered the work, but he is not forced to redo it. If the tailor himself tears it, he must redo it. The passage then clarifies the condition of 'working' meaning ability to work: if the hireling refrains from work despite ability, or if he is genuinely unable due to an excuse (like illness or rain), he still deserves the wage as long as the inability is not due to his own refusal. Finally, it quotes al-Durar to define when an ajir becomes specific: either by a stipulation of exclusivity or by mentioning the period first in the contract.

Key Terms
الأجير الخاص (al-ajīr al-khāṣṣ): A hireling exclusively for one employer, whose benefits are dedicated to that employer for the contract period.
الأجير المشترك (al-ajīr al-mushtarak): A hireling who works for multiple employers, earning wage by delivering the work, not by time.
أجير وحد (ajīr waḥd): Another term for the specific hireling, emphasizing his exclusivity to one hirer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because he surrendered his time.
B) No, because he was unable to work and so surrender is incomplete.
C) He gets partial wages for the days he was well before falling ill.
D) The contract is void.

Key Takeaway
A specific hireling is entitled to wages by making himself available and able to work, not by actually performing the work.

Ajir Wahd: Definition and the Role of Contract Wording
Defining ajir wahd and explaining how contract wording determines the type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of ajir wahd and apply the Hanafi rule that the placement of the period or work in the contract wording determines whether the hireling is specific or common.

Core Idea
The contract wording determines the hireling's type: if the period comes first, it's specific; if the work comes first, it's common.

In Hanafi fiqh, the classification of a hireling as 'specific' (ajir wahd) or 'common' (ajir mushtarak) has important legal consequences. This lesson explains the definition of ajir wahd and the critical rule that the order of mentioning the period (muddah) and the work (amal) in the contract decisively determines the hireling's status.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of ajir wahd
Understand that ajir wahd (also called ajir khas) is a hireling who works exclusively for one employer during a specified period. The linguistic root 'wahd' means 'one' or 'unique'.
The term is derived from 'al-wahd' meaning uniqueness, emphasizing one hirer.
2
Identify the two key elements in an ijara contract
The two elements are the period (muddah) and the work (amal). The order of mentioning these in the contract determines the hireling's classification.
These are the essential components that the fuqaha analyze.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule: first mention dominates
If the period is mentioned first, the contract is based on time, making the hireling specific; if the work is mentioned first, the contract is based on the work, making the hireling common. Ambiguity is resolved by the apparent wording.
The rule is based on the principle that the first element establishes the nature of the contract.
4
Analyze sample contract wordings
Work through examples: (a) 'I hire you for a month to herd my sheep' → period first → ajir wahd. (b) 'I hire you to herd my sheep for a month' → work first → ajir mushtarak. Note that even for ajir wahd, the type of work must be specified for the contract to be valid.
The passage emphasizes that the ruling is not changed by mere probability; clear wording is required.

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'ajir wahd' (also 'ajir khas') and explains the critical role of contract wording in determining whether a hireling is specific or common. The key principle is that if the period (muddah) is mentioned first in the contract, the hireling becomes specific (ajir wahd), because the contract is based on time, and the hirer owns the hireling's benefits for that duration. If the work (e.g., 'to herd my sheep') is mentioned first, the contract is based on the work itself, making the hireling common (ajir mushtarak). The commentator clarifies that mentioning the period first establishes the hireling's exclusivity even if the type of work is specified later. Conversely, if the work is mentioned first and the period next, the hireling is common unless the wording clearly indicates otherwise. Then the linguistic origin of 'ajir wahd' is discussed: it means 'unique' or 'alone,' emphasizing one hirer. The passage concludes with a quotation from al-Mughrib explaining that 'ajir al-wahd' is a construct term meaning the hireling of one hirer.

Key Terms
أجير وحد (ajīr waḥd): A hireling who is exclusive to one employer, derived from 'wahd' meaning 'unique' or 'one'.
المدة (al-muddah): The time period of the hire; mentioning it first in the contract makes the hireling specific.
العمل (al-`amal): The work to be performed; mentioning it first makes the hireling common.

Liability of the Special Hireling (Ajir Khas)
Defines ajir khas vs. mushtarak and rules on his liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a special hireling (ajir khas) and a common hireling (ajir mushtarak), and state the Hanafi ruling on the liability of each, including the reasoning based on trust and istihsan.

Core Idea
A special hireling is not liable for accidental loss or damage; he is a trustee, not a guarantor.

In Hanafi fiqh, the distinction between a special hireling (ajir khas) and a common hireling (ajir mushtarak) is crucial for determining liability. The special hireling works exclusively for one hirer, while the common hireling works for multiple parties. This lesson explores the ruling that the special hireling does not guarantee loss or damage unless he intentionally causes it, and the reasoning behind this rule.

Guided Path
1
Define and contrast the two hireling types
Identify the key features: ajir khas (special) is hired for a period and works exclusively for one hirer; ajir mushtarak (common) is hired for a specific task and may work for multiple hirers. The definition hinges on whether the contract is on the period or the work.
The text gives the example of a shepherd for specified sheep.
2
State the ruling for the special hireling
The special hireling does not guarantee (i.e., is not liable) for loss or damage to the hired property in his possession or arising from his work, provided he did not intentionally cause the damage.
This is the agreed position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
3
Analyze the reasoning for the ruling
Two rationales: (1) For loss in his hand: the property is a trust (amanah) because he took it with permission, analogous to a depositary. (2) For loss due to his work: the hireling is a deputy (na'ib) of the hirer; the wage is for making the benefit available, not for the work itself.
The contrast with the common hireling, who is liable by istihsan, clarifies the Hanafi position.
4
Identify the exception for intentional damage
If the hireling intentionally causes corruption (ta'ammada al-fasad), he becomes liable, like a depositary who transgresses.
This preserves accountability while protecting the hireling from unforeseen accidents.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Example: A man hires a driver exclusively for a month. While driving, the car gets a flat tire due to a pothole. The driver is not liable, as he is a special hireling. But if he deliberately runs the car into a wall, he is liable.
This illustrates the distinction between non-liability for accidents and liability for misconduct.

(And he does not guarantee what is lost in his hand or due to his work.) [1] His statement: 'And he does not guarantee...' etc.; meaning the special hireling does not guarantee what is lost in his hand, e.g., it is stolen or usurped from him, nor what is lost due to his work, e.g., the garment is torn, or the cooking is spoiled, or the bread is burnt, and the like. And this is if he did not intentionally cause corruption. But if he intentionally did that, then he guarantees, like the depositary if he transgresses, as they have clearly stated. As for the non-obligation of guarantee for what is lost in his hand, it is because the object is a trust in his hand, because he took possession with the hirer's permission. And this is apparent according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and likewise according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because making the common hireling liable is a type of istihsan to protect people's property, for he accepts many objects desiring abundant wages, and he may be unable to fulfill the right of preservation therein, so he is liable so that he does not neglect their preservation and does not take except what he can preserve. And the special hireling does not accept work from others; rather, he surrenders himself, so safety is predominant, so qiyas is applied in his case. As for the non-obligation of guarantee for what is lost due to his work, it is because when the benefits become owned by the hirer due to the surrender of the self, his disposition in them is valid, and the command to dispose in them. So when he commands him to dispose in his property, it is valid, and the commanded person (i.e., the hireling) becomes a deputy representing him. Thus his action is transferred to him, as if he did it himself. Hence he does not guarantee, and the wage is not in exchange for the work, as evidenced by the fact that he is entitled to the wage even if he does not work, as you have learned. And this is because the sold item is the benefit, and it is safe; the damage occurs in the work which is the delivery of the benefit, and that is not contracted upon. So if it is not guaranteed upon him, then its safety is not required, so he is not liable for what is lost through it.
Source pages p. 593

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah addresses the liability of the special hireling (ajir khas) in the chapter on ijarah. The text begins by defining when a shepherd becomes a special hireling: either by stipulating exclusivity, mentioning the period first, or specifying the type of work. The distinction between special and common hireling hinges on whether the contract is on the period (making him special) or on the work (making him common). The commentary clarifies that the primary ruling is that a special hireling does not guarantee (i.e., is not liable) for loss or damage to the hired property while in his possession or arising from his work, provided he did not intentionally cause the damage. The reasoning is twofold: (1) For loss in his hand: the property is an amanah (trust) because he took it with permission. This is agreed upon by Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The common hireling, by contrast, is liable by istihsan to protect public interest. (2) For loss due to his work: the benefits belong to the hirer; the hireling is merely an agent. The wage is not in exchange for the specific work but for making the benefit available. Therefore, if damage occurs in the process of delivering the benefit, it is not the hireling's responsibility. The passage also notes that if the hireling intentionally causes damage, he becomes liable, analogous to a depositary who transgresses.

Key Terms
أجير وحد (ajir wahd): A hireling who works exclusively for one hirer. Also called ajir khas (special hireling). The term 'wahd' indicates singularity or exclusivity.
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A hireling who works for multiple hirers or whose contract is based on the work itself rather than a period. He is liable for loss or damage due to istihsan.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage. In this context, it refers to the hireling's financial responsibility for the hired property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does a special hireling (ajir khas) become liable for loss or damage to the hired property?
A) If the loss occurs due to theft by a third party.
B) If the hireling intentionally causes the damage.
C) If the hireling is not paid his wages.
D) If the hirer did not specify the type of work.

Key Takeaway
The special hireling is not liable for unintentional loss or damage because the hired property is a trust in his hands; liability only arises from intentional misconduct.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Liability of the Special Hireling (Ajir Khas)
Rationale for non-liability of special hireling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the special hireling's liability for accidental loss and explain the rationale based on trust and agency.

Core Idea
The special hireling is a trustee, not a guarantor, so he is not liable for accidental loss.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a key distinction in Hanafi Ijara law: the special hireling (ajir khas) who works exclusively for one employer is not liable for damage or loss to the property unless he deliberately causes it. This stands in contrast to the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) who is made liable by istihsan to protect public interest. The commentator elaborates the reasoning behind this rule, grounding it in the principles of trust (amanah) and agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening statement: the special hireling does not guarantee loss in his hand or from his work. This is the core ruling.
The ruling applies only to accidental loss; deliberate damage triggers liability.
2
Understand the exceptions
The text then clarifies that if the hireling intentionally causes damage, he is liable, like a depositary who transgresses.
Intentional damage (ta'addi) removes the protection of trust.
3
Analyze rationale for loss in hand
The item is a trust (amanah) because he took possession with the lessee's permission. All Hanafi imams agree on this.
Trustees (amin) are not liable for accidental loss without negligence.
4
Analyze rationale for loss from work
When the hireling surrenders his person, the benefits become owned by the lessee. The hireling acts as the lessee's deputy, so his actions are attributed to the lessee. Thus, any damage from the work is not the hireling's responsibility.
Also, the wage is for the benefit itself, not for the specific work outcome.
5
Compare with common hireling
The common hireling (ajir mushtarak) is made liable by istihsan to prevent negligence, as he takes many items. The special hireling, by contrast, is judged by qiyas (analogy) as a trustee.
This distinction is a classic application of istihsan overriding qiyas for public interest.

قوله : ولا يضمن.... الخ ؛ يعني ولا يضمن الأجير الخاص ما تلف في يده بأن سرق منه أو غصب، ولا ما تلف من عمله بأن تخرّق الثوب أو انفسد الطبيخ أو احترق الخبز، ونحو ذلك، وهذا إذا لم يتعمد الفساد. أما إذا تعمد ذلك فضمن كالمودع إذا تعدّى . كما صرحوا به، أما عدم وجوب الضمان فيما تلف في يده ؛ فلأنّ العين أمانة في يده ؛ لأنه قبضها بإذن المستأجر، وهذا ظاهر عند الإمام، وكذا عندهما ؛ لأنّ تضمين الأجير المشترك نوع استحسان صيانة لأموال الناس، فإنه يتقبل أعياناً كثيرة رغبة في كثرة الأجرة، وقد يعجز عن قضاء حق الحفظ فيهما فيضمن حتى لا يقصِّرُ في حفظها، ولا يأخذ إلا ما يقدر على حفظه. وأجير الوحد لا يتقبل العمل من غيره بل يُسَلّم نفسه، فتكون السلامة غالبة، فيؤخذ فيه بالقياس، وأما عدم جوب الضمان فيما تلف من عمله ؛ فلأن المنافع متى صارت مملوكة للمستأجر بتسليم النفس صح تصرفه فيها، والأمر بالتصرف فيها، فإذا أمره بالتصرف في ملكه صح. ويصير المأمور : أي الأجير نائباً ،منابه، فصار فعله منقولاً إليه، كأنه فعله بنفسه ؛ فلذا لا يضمن، على أنّ البدل ليس بمقابلة العمل، بدليل أنه يستحق الأجر وإن لم يعمل كما عرفت ؛ وهذا لأنّ المبيع ،منفعة، وهي سليمة، وإنما الخرق في العمل الذي هو تسليم المنفعة ؛ وذلك غير معقود عليه ، فإذا لم يكن مضموناً عليه، فلا يشترط فيه سلامته، فلا يتضمن ما تلف به.
His statement: 'And he does not guarantee' etc.; meaning: the special hireling does not guarantee what is lost in his hand, such as by theft or usurpation, nor what is lost from his work, such as the garment tearing, the cooking spoiling, or the bread burning, and the like. This is when he did not intentionally cause damage. But if he intentionally does that, then he guarantees like a depositary if he transgresses, as they have explicitly stated. As for the absence of liability for what is lost in his hand: because the object is a trust in his hand, since he took possession with the lessee's permission. This is apparent according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and likewise according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Because making the common hireling liable is a type of istihsan to protect people's property, since he accepts many objects in hopes of greater wages, and he might be unable to fulfill the duty of safeguarding them, so he is made liable so that he does not fall short in preserving them and only takes what he can preserve. The special hireling does not accept work from others but rather surrenders his own person, so safety is predominant, and he is judged by analogy. As for the absence of liability for what is lost from his work: because once the benefits become owned by the lessee through the surrender of his person, his (the lessee's) disposal of them is valid, and the command to dispose of them is valid. When he commands him (the hireling) to dispose of his property, it is valid. The commanded one, i.e., the hireling, becomes his deputy, so his action is attributed to him as if he did it himself. Therefore he does not guarantee, and also because the compensation is not in exchange for the work, as evidenced by the fact that he deserves wages even if he did not work, as you have learned. This is because the sold item is a benefit, and it is safe; the flaw is in the work which is the delivery of the benefit, and that is not contracted upon. So when it is not guaranteed against him, safety is not required of it, and thus he does not guarantee what is lost by it.
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling that the special hireling (ajir khas) is not liable for damage or loss occurring to the hired item while in his possession or through his work, unless he deliberately causes the damage. The commentator explains the reasoning behind this ruling. First, regarding loss in his hand: the item is an amanah (trust) because he took possession with the owner's permission. Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions agree on this, but the two companions make the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) liable as an istihsan to protect people's property, since he takes many items. The special hireling does not take items from others, so trust is predominant. Second, regarding loss from his work: once the hireling surrenders his person, the benefits become owned by the lessee. The hireling acts as the lessee's agent, so his actions are attributed to the lessee. Thus, any damage from the work is not the hireling's responsibility. Also, the wage is not in exchange for the specific work but for the benefit itself, so the hireling is not a guarantor of the work's perfection.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A special hireling who works exclusively for one employer and does not accept work from others.
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A common hireling who accepts work from multiple people, like a tailor or baker.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a special hireling (ajir khas) liable for damage to the hired item?
A) When the damage occurs through his work.
B) When the damage is caused deliberately.
C) When the item is stolen from his hand.
D) When the damage is accidental.

Key Takeaway
The special hireling is a trustee, not a guarantor, so accidental loss does not make him liable; only deliberate damage triggers liability.

Conditional Wages in Hire Contracts: Hanafi Validity and the Dispute
Dispute over conditional wages in ijara with examples and istihsan reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates hire contracts with conditional wages and evaluate the opposing schools' objection.

Core Idea
In ijara, wage becomes known at performance, so uncertainty at contract doesn't invalidate.

Hire contracts often involve specifying a wage. The classical question: can the wage be left conditional on the type of work? The Hanafi school says yes, citing istihsan. This lesson explores the reasoning and the inter-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
State Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: the hire contract is valid (sahih) despite the conditional wage.
This is based on istihsan, not qiyas.
2
Identify opponents and their view
The opposing schools (Malik, Shafi'i, etc.) hold that such a contract is invalid due to jahalah (uncertainty) in the wage at contract time.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their proof is qiyas to a sale with uncertain price, which is invalid because the countervalue is unspecified at formation.
Sale: price due immediately; hire: wage due on work.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response (istihsan) distinguishes hire from sale: in hire, the wage is only due upon work completion; at that point, the wage is known. Thus no harmful uncertainty remains.
This distinction is the core of the dispute.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi contract valid, specified wage paid; opponents' contract invalid, fair wage (ajr al-mithl) owed.
This affects the parties' obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الإجارة على أحد الشرطين [1] وصح ترديد الأجر بالترديد في خياطةِ النُّوبِ فارسيّاً أو رومياً [١]قوله : صح ترديد الأجر ... الخ ؛ يعني صح جعل الأجر متردداً بين التسميتين ، بسبب الترديد بين نوعي عمل ، كأن يقول : إن خطته رومياً فبدرهم، وإن خطته فارسيّاً فبدرهمين، أو يقول : إن صبغته بعصفر ،فبدرهم، وإن خطته بزعفران فبدرهمين، أو بين إسكان البيت عطاراً وحداداً بأن يقول : إن أسكنتُ في هذا البيت عطاراً فبدرهم، وإن أسكنت فيه حداداً فبدرهمين. أو بين مسافتين بأن يقول : إن حملتُ الدّابة إلى كوفة فبدرهم، وإن حملتها إلى واسطة فبدرهمين، أو بين دارين بأن يقول : إن سكنت هذه الدار شهراً فبدرهم، وإن سكنت الأخرى شهراً ،فبدرهمين، أو بين حملين بأن يقول : إن حملت على هذه الدابة إلى كذا كراً من بر فبعشرة دراهم ، وإن حملت عليها إلى كذا كُراً من شعير فبدرهمين ، وأيهما وجدَ لَزِمَ ما سمّى له. وقال مالك والشافعي والثوري وأبو ثور وإسحاق : لا يصح العقد، ويجب أجر المثل إذا عمل، وهو القياس؛ لأنه عقد معاوضة يتعيّن فيه العوض ولا المعوض فلم يصح، كما لو قال : بعتك بدرهم أو هذا بدرهمين. وجه الاستحسان : إنّ الإجارة يجب فيها الأجر بالعمل، وعند العمل ما يلزم من البدل معلوم، فلا تبقى جهالة لا في المعقود عليه ولا في بدله بخلاف البيع، فإنّ الثمن فيه يجب بنفس العقد، فإذا لم يكن معلوماً عند العقد يفسد.
Chapter: Hire on one of two conditions. It is valid to make the wage conditional on the type of work, such as stitching the garment in Persian style or Roman style. His statement: 'It is valid to make the wage conditional' etc. Meaning: it is valid to make the wage contingent on the type of work, e.g., he says: if you stitch it in Roman style, then one dirham; if you stitch it in Persian style, then two dirhams. Or he says: if you dye it with safflower, then one dirham; if you stitch it with saffron, then two dirhams. Or between housing a perfumer or a blacksmith by saying: if I house a perfumer in this house, then one dirham; if I house a blacksmith, then two dirhams. Or between two distances by saying: if I transport the animal to Kufa, then one dirham; if I transport it to Wasit, then two dirhams. Or between two houses by saying: if I occupy this house for a month, then one dirham; if I occupy the other for a month, then two dirhams. Or between two loads by saying: if I transport on this animal to such a place a kur of wheat, then ten dirhams; if I transport a kur of barley, then two dirhams. Whichever occurs, the wage specified is binding. Malik, al-Shafi'i, al-Thawri, Abu Thawr, and Ishaq said: the contract is invalid, and the fair wage is obligatory if the work is done. That is the analogy because it is a commutative contract where the consideration is specified but the countervalue is not, so it is invalid, like if he said: I sell to you for one dirham or this for two dirhams. The basis of istihsan: in hire, the wage becomes due upon work, and at the time of work, what is due of the consideration is known, so there is no uncertainty in the object of contract or its substitute, unlike sale where the price becomes due upon the contract itself, so if it is not known at the time of contract, it is invalid.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage discusses a chapter on hire contracts where the wage is conditional on which of two types of work is performed. The Hanafi position is that such a contract is valid, citing istihsan. The author gives examples: different wages for different stitching styles, dyeing, housing different tenants, transporting to different distances, occupying different houses, or carrying different loads. Whichever condition occurs, the corresponding wage is binding. The opposing schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, etc.) say the contract is invalid because of uncertainty (jahalah) in the countervalue at the time of contract, analogous to an invalid sale. The Hanafi response (istihsan) is that in hire, the wage becomes due only upon performance of the work; at that moment, the wage is known. There is no uncertainty in the subject matter or its substitute. This differs from sale, where the price is due immediately upon contract.

Key Terms
ترديد الأجر (tardid al-ajr): Making the wage conditional on which of two types of work is performed.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market wage for the work, payable when no valid wage is specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis consider a hire contract with conditional wages valid?
A) Because the wage is determined at contract formation.
B) Because uncertainty in hire is always permissible.
C) Because the wage becomes known when the work is performed.
D) Because it is a sale contract.

Key Takeaway
A hire contract with wage conditional on work type is valid in the Hanafi school because uncertainty is resolved at performance.

Valid Contingent Wages in Ijara
Ruling statement on contingent wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on contingent wages in ijara and distinguish it from cases that involve prohibited gharar.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, an ijara contract is valid even if the wage varies based on the type of work performed.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding contingent wages in hiring contracts. The source passage states that it is valid to specify two different wages depending on the type of work done, such as stitching a garment in Persian or Roman style. The commentator provides numerous examples to illustrate the scope of this ruling, highlighting that the wage becomes determinable upon performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an ijara (hire) contract with a wage that depends on the type of work. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih).
The wage is not fixed at contract formation but becomes determined when the work is performed.
2
Understand the structure of the contract
The contract includes two possible wages, each tied to a specific work type. Once the work is done, the corresponding wage becomes binding.
The uncertainty is temporary and resolved by performance.
3
Review the examples
The commentary lists multiple scenarios: stitching (Roman vs. Persian), dyeing (safflower vs. saffron), renting to different tenants, transporting to different destinations, occupying different houses, and carrying different loads.
In each case, a different wage is specified for each option.
4
Distinguish from prohibited gharar
The Hanafi school permits this because the wage becomes known upon performance. It is not the type of extreme uncertainty that invalidates a contract.
This is an application of istihsan, which overrides the general prohibition of gharar in this context.

Chapter: Ijara on one of two conditions. It is valid to make the wage contingent on the variation in stitching the garment, Persian or Roman. [Commentary: It means it is valid to make the wage contingent between the two mentions due to the variation between two types of work, such as saying: If you stitch it Roman-style, then one dirham; if you stitch it Persian-style, then two dirhams. Or: If you dye it with safflower, then one dirham; if you stitch it with saffron, then two dirhams. Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the Hanafi matn. The author states that it is valid in an ijara contract to make the wage contingent on which type of work is performed. The commentary provides several examples: stitching (Roman vs. Persian), dyeing (safflower vs. saffron), renting a house to a perfume seller vs. a blacksmith, carrying goods to Kufa vs. Wasit, occupying one of two houses, and carrying wheat vs. barley. In each case, a different wage is specified for each option, and whichever option actually occurs determines the wage due. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
ترديد الأجر (tardid al-ujr): Making the wage contingent upon which of two specified types of work is performed

Contingent Wage in Ijara: Hanafi vs. Majority
Dispute: Hanafi position vs. other schools on contingent wage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on contingent wages in ijara, state the opposing view, and identify the qiyas-istihsan distinction that underpins the dispute.

Core Idea
In ijara, the wage is earned by the work; in sale, the price is fixed at contract — so contingent wage is valid by istihsan.

This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of a wage that is contingent on the type of work in an ijara contract. The majority of scholars (Malik, Shafi'i, Thawri, Abu Thawr, Ishaq) argue that such a contract is invalid based on qiyas with sale, where a contingent price would void the contract. The Hanafi school, however, uses istihsan to distinguish ijara from sale, arguing that the wage becomes known at the time of work. This lesson unpacks their arguments and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the contested ruling: validity of ijara with wage contingent on type of work. State that Hanafis say valid, majority says invalid.
The majority includes Malik, Shafi'i, Thawri, Abu Thawr, and Ishaq.
2
Examine the majority's qiyas argument
Understand their analogy: in sale, contingent price invalidates; similarly, in ijara, contingent wage should invalidate. This is based on the need for certainty in commutative contracts.
3
Analyze the Hanafi istihsan response
Hanafis argue that in ijara, the wage is due by the work, not by the contract. At the time of work, the wage is known, so there is no uncertainty.
This is an override of the qiyas via istihsan.
4
Identify the key distinction between sale and ijara
In sale, the price is fixed at the contract moment; in ijara, the wage is earned by actual work. Hence the timing of obligation differs.
5
Note the practical consequence
Hanafis permit contingent wage contracts; the majority requires a fixed wage from the start or else ujrat al-mithl (fair wage) is due.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال مالك والشافعي والثوري وأبو ثور وإسحاق : لا يصح العقد، ويجب أجر المثل إذا عمل، وهو القياس؛ لأنه عقد معاوضة يتعيّن فيه العوض ولا المعوض فلم يصح، كما لو قال : بعتك بدرهم أو هذا بدرهمين. وجه الاستحسان : إنّ الإجارة يجب فيها الأجر بالعمل، وعند العمل ما يلزم من البدل معلوم، فلا تبقى جهالة لا في المعقود عليه ولا في بدله بخلاف البيع، فإنّ الثمن فيه يجب بنفس العقد، فإذا لم يكن معلوماً عند العقد يفسد
Malik, al-Shafi'i, al-Thawri, Abu Thawr, and Ishaq said: The contract is not valid, and the fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) is due when work is done, and this is the qiyas; because it is a commutative contract where the consideration and the counter-value must be specified, so it is not valid, just as if one says: 'I sell to you for a dirham or this for two dirhams.' The istihsan justification: In ijara, the wage is due by the work, and at the time of work, what is owed of the substitute is known, so there is no ignorance regarding the subject matter nor its substitute, unlike sale, where the price is determined by the contract itself, and if it is not known at the time of contract, it is invalid.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of contingent wages in ijara. The majority of scholars (Malik, Shafi'i, Thawri, Abu Thawr, Ishaq) argue that such a contract is invalid based on qiyas (analogy) with sale: in a sale, if the price is contingent (e.g., 'I sell to you for a dirham or for two dirhams'), the contract is invalid due to uncertainty (gharar). Similarly, in ijara, if the wage is contingent on the type of work, it is invalid. Their proof: it is a commutative contract requiring certainty of both substitutes. The Hanafi school responds by invoking istihsan (juristic preference). They argue that ijara differs from sale because in ijara, the wage is not fixed at the moment of contract; rather, it becomes due upon the performance of the work. At the time of work, the wage is known. Thus, there is no debilitating uncertainty. This distinction is based on the nature of ijara: the wage is earned by the work, not by the contract alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between sale and ijara that Hanafis use to justify valid contingent wage?
A) In sale, price is due at contract; in ijara, wage is due at work
B) Ijara is not a commutative contract
C) Hanafis reject qiyas in this case
D) The opposing school agrees

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates contingent wages in ijara because the wage is determined by the work performed, not by the contract alone — a distinction that overrides the qiyas with sale via istihsan.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Contingent Benefit in Ijara
Intra-Hanafi dispute on contingent benefit in ijara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on contingent ijara and explain how the timing of wage obligation (taslim vs. 'amal) determines the dispute.

Core Idea
When wage is due at surrender, contingency invalidates ijara; when due by work, it does not.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi disagreement about leasing when the precise benefit is not fixed at contract. Abu Hanifa allows a house to be rented to either a perfume seller or a blacksmith—the lessee chooses later. The Sahibayn reject this because for a specific hireling, the wage becomes due before the work is known. We will trace their arguments and see how a key distinction in hireling types drives the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the case and the Hanafi positions
First, identify the factual scenario: renting a house to an attar or a blacksmith (or carrying goods to Kufa or Wasit). Note that Abu Hanifa declares the ijara valid, while the Sahibayn declare it invalid.
This is an agreement between three early Hanafi masters: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's principle
The Sahibayn reason: for a specific hireling (ajir khas), the wage is due upon surrender (taslim) without any work. At the moment of surrender, it is unknown which benefit will be chosen and which wage is due. This double uncertainty (jahalah) invalidates the contract. They contrast with Roman vs. Persian stitching, where wage is due only after work, removing uncertainty.
Their principle: if wage is due by taslim, it cannot be contingent between two things.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa argues that the two options are similar (mutanasaib) and each has a known wage. He draws an analogy to the stitching case, where the wage is known even though the style is chosen later. He emphasizes that ijara is contracted for benefit (intifa'), and this flexibility accommodates the lessee's needs.
For Abu Hanifa, the wage is due by work, not by mere surrender, so the uncertainty is resolved when the choice is made.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, such contracts are enforceable; under the Sahibayn, they are void. A mufti would need to know which view is operative, though the text does not specify tarjih.
Both positions are recorded in zahir al-riwayah, so they are authoritative.

[٢]قوله : وفي إسكان البيت... الخ؛ هذا قول أبي حنيفة له، وعندهما : لا يجوز الإجارة، وعلى هذا الخلاف مسألة الحمل إلى كوفة أو إلى واسطة. لهما : إن الأجرة والمنفعة مجهولان؛ لأنّ الأجر في الأجير الخاص يجب بالتسليم من غير عمل، ولا يدري أي العملين تقرّر، وأي التسميتين تجب وقت التسليم، بخلاف الخياطة الرومية أو الفارسيّة؛ لأنَّ الأجر لا يجب فيه إلا بالعمل، وبه يرتفع الجهالة. فالقاعدة لهما أن الأجر متى وجب بالتسليم لا يجوز أن يكون متردداً بين شيئين. عند التسليم؛ لأنه لا يدري أيهما يجب، والإجارة تفسد. ولأبي حنيفة : إنه خيره بين شيئين متقاربين وجعل لكل واحد منهما أجرةً معلومة، فوجب أن يجوز كما في مسألة الخياطة الروميّة أو الفارسية، والإجارة تعقد للانتفاع.
His saying: 'And in renting the house to a perfume seller or a blacksmith...' — this is the view of Abu Hanifa; with him (the Sahibayn) the ijara is not valid. And upon this difference is the case of carrying to Kufa or to Wasit. For them (the Sahibayn): the wage and the benefit are unknown, because for a specific hireling, the wage is due by surrender without work, and it is not known which work will be determined and which wage is due at the time of surrender, unlike Roman or Persian stitching; because the wage is only due by work, and thereby the ignorance is removed. Their principle: whenever the wage is due by surrender, it is not permissible for it to be contingent between two things at surrender, because it is not known which is due, and the ijara is invalid. For Abu Hanifa: he gave a choice between two similar things and assigned each a known wage, so it should be valid, as in the case of Roman or Persian stitching, and ijara is contracted for benefit.
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The issue concerns cases where the type of benefit differs—for example, renting a house to either a perfume seller or a blacksmith, or carrying goods to Kufa or Wasit. In such cases, Abu Hanifa allows the ijara with a contingent wage, whereas the Sahibayn invalidate it. The Sahibayn argue that for a specific hireling (ajir khas), the wage becomes due upon surrender (taslim) without any work performed. At the moment of surrender, it is not known which work will be done or which wage is due, leading to uncertainty in both wage and benefit. This is unlike the stitching case (Roman vs. Persian) where the wage is only due after work, so the uncertainty is removed by the work itself. Therefore, their principle is: if the wage is due at surrender, it cannot be contingent. Abu Hanifa responds that the two options are similar (mutanasa'ib) and each has a known wage, so the contract should be valid by analogy with the stitching case. He emphasizes that ijara is fundamentally a contract for benefit (intifa'), and this flexibility serves the purpose of the contract.

Key Terms
الأجير الخاص (al-ajir al-khass): A specific hireling whose services are exclusively hired for a period; the wage becomes due upon surrender (taslim) without work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the wage is unknown at the time of contract
B) Because the wage becomes due upon surrender and it is not known which wage is due
C) Because the benefit is too different
D) Because Abu Hanifa said so

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute on contingent ijara, the Sahibayn invalidate because wage due at surrender creates uncertainty, while Abu Hanifa validates by analogy to stitching and the purpose of contract for benefit.

Ijarah with Alternative Tasks: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute over ijarah with alternative tasks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ijarah contracts with alternative tasks, explain the Sahibayn's objection, and apply the rule to scenarios with two, three, or four alternatives.

Core Idea
An ijarah contract with two or three similar alternative tasks is valid under Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn invalidate it due to wage uncertainty at the moment of taslīm.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of ijarah contracts where the employee is given a choice between two or more specific tasks, each with a predetermined wage. Imam Abu Hanifa validates such contracts, analogizing them to the accepted case of tailoring, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), invalidate them due to gharar in the wage obligation. Understanding this dispute is crucial for constructing valid hire contracts in daily transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an ijarah contract where the employee may choose between two tasks (e.g., dyeing with safflower or saffron, or sewing Persian or Roman style). State Abu Hanifa's ruling (valid) and the Sahibayn's (invalid).
2
Locate the dalil
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to the tailoring case; the Sahibayn rely on the principle that in ajīr khāṣṣ, wage is due upon taslīm, creating uncertainty.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For Abu Hanifa, the analogy is that both cases involve choice between similar tasks with known wages; for the Sahibayn, the key difference is when wage becomes due.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the contract is valid and the named wage is due; under the Sahibayn, the contract is fasid and only ujrat al-mithl is due.
5
Evaluate the extension to three or four alternatives
For three alternatives, the ruling follows Abu Hanifa's permissibility; for four or more, the contract is invalid by analogy to sale with khiyar al-ta'yin.

And upon this difference is the issue of carrying to Kufa or to Wasit. Page 597: ...so with two dirhams, and I rented this house to you for a month for one dirham, or this house for a month for two dirhams, and likewise if it is in three things, and in four things... not like in sale, except that the option of specification is required in sale but not in ijarah, because in ijarah the wage becomes obligatory with work, and upon work it becomes specified, unlike sale, where the price becomes obligatory by the contract itself and the sold item is unknown. So it is apparent that he receives the benefits, and upon receipt the ignorance is removed. And if it is necessary to make it obligatory simply upon delivery, when there is no receipt after delivery, half of each of the two alternatives is obligatory according to some mashayikh, since neither is more deserving than the other, so delivery is made with both. And the correct view is that the lesser of the two alternatives is obligatory, because it is not more harmful than benefiting from the lesser harm. Mentioned by al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz. [1] His statement: 'and likewise... etc.'; meaning likewise the ruling is the permissibility of the contract and the obligation of the wage for what he did when the alternation is in three things, as when he says: if you sew it Persian-style then for one dirham, if you sew it Roman-style then for two dirhams, if you sew it Turkish-style then for three dirhams, or if he says: if you dye it with safflower then for one dirham, if you dye it with saffron then for two dirhams, if you dye it with woad and the like then for three dirhams, and compare to this; whichever work he performs, he is entitled to the named wage. [2] His statement: 'and in four things... etc.'; meaning if the alternation is in four things, such that he says: if you sew it Persian-style then for one dirham, if you sew it Roman-style then for two dirhams, if you sew it Turkish-style then for three dirhams, if you sew it Indian-style then for four dirhams, the contract is not valid, as in sale, because if he sells one of two garments on the condition that he takes whichever he wishes, it is permissible. Likewise if he says: I have sold one of these three garments on the condition that he takes whichever he wishes; but if he says: I have sold one of these four or five or more garments on the condition that he takes whichever he wishes, it is not permissible. And the common point in joining ijarah to sale in these cases is the fulfillment of need, because need is fulfilled by three (alternatives), as they include the good, the medium, and the poor, and there is no need for four or more.
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary that expands on a ruling from al-Wiqayah regarding ijarah (hiring) when the contract specifies alternative tasks with distinct wages. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The core issue is the validity of an ijarah contract that gives the hirer (or employee) a choice between two (or more) tasks, each with a predetermined wage. Imam Abu Hanifa validates such contracts, analogizing them to the case of tailoring where the tailor chooses between Roman or Persian stitching – a case already accepted as valid. He argues that as long as the alternatives are similar (mutqāribān) and each has a known wage, the contract is valid because ijarah is inherently for benefit, and the uncertainty (jahālah) is removed upon actual performance. The Sahibayn, however, invalidate the contract because, in their view, the wage in a specific hire (ajīr khāṣṣ) becomes obligatory upon mere delivery of self (taslīm) to work, not upon actual work. Thus, at the moment the contract is formed, both the exact wage and the exact service are uncertain, leading to gharar (excessive uncertainty), which renders the contract fasid (invalid). They distinguish the accepted tailoring case where the wage is only due upon completion of work, thus removing uncertainty. The commentary then extends the discussion to contracts involving three alternatives – which are valid – and four or more – which are invalid, by analogy to sale with khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification). The rationale is that three options (good, medium, poor) fulfill the typical need, whereas more create excessive uncertainty. The passage also touches on a subsidiary issue: if the employee does nothing after delivery, the correct view is that the lesser of the two wages is owed, based on minimizing harm.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajīr khāṣṣ): A specific hireling who is contracted to work exclusively for the hirer during the contract term, and whose wage is due upon delivery of self (taslīm) even if no work is performed.
خيار التعيين (khiyār al-ta'yīn): The option of specification in a contract of sale, allowing the buyer to choose one of several items at a later time.
تسليم (taslīm): Delivery of the self or the subject matter; in ijarah context, the employee's placing oneself at the disposal of the hirer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is an ijarah contract invalid if the employee has a choice between two tasks with different wages?
A) Because the wage is unknown until the work is done.
B) Because the wage in a specific hire becomes obligatory upon delivery (taslīm), creating uncertainty at the time of contract.
C) Because ijarah does not permit choice; only sale does.
D) Because the employee must work for free if no wage is specified.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ijarah contracts with two or three similar alternative tasks are valid according to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn invalidate them due to wage uncertainty at the moment of delivery.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
