Ijarah on Alternating Conditions: Validity and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on the ruling and dispute regarding ijarah with alternative conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on ijarah with alternative conditions, state the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the ruling to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
In ijarah, uncertainty (jahalah) is excused if resolved at performance; Abu Hanifa permits up to three alternatives, while the Sahibayn require certainty at contract formation when wage is due upon delivery.

This lesson examines the validity of hire contracts (ijarah) where the wage or work is specified in the alternative, such as 'If I sew it Persian style, 1 dirham; if Roman, 2 dirhams.' The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: Abu Hanifa deems such contracts valid for up to three alternatives, while his two main disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold them invalid due to excessive uncertainty when the wage becomes due upon delivery (takhliya) rather than upon performance. Understanding this dispute clarifies the school's criteria for permissible uncertainty in contracts and its application to modern service agreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and alternatives
Examine the contract type (ijarah) and the specific alternative conditions (e.g., work style, occupant, destination). Note whether the alternatives are in the work or the wage.
The passage covers both work-based alternatives (sewing styles) and use-based alternatives (shop occupancy, donkey route).
2
Check the number of alternatives
According to the Hanafi school, if the alternatives are three or fewer, the contract is generally valid under Abu Hanifa. For four or more, the contract is invalid by analogy with sale (bay').
The rationale is that need is satisfied with three options (good, medium, poor).
3
Compare with sale and the role of khiyar al-ta'yin
Note that in ijarah, khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification) is not required because the wage becomes due only upon performance, at which point uncertainty is resolved. In sale, the price is due at contract, so khiyar al-ta'yin is needed.
This distinction is crucial for understanding why ijarah with alternatives is treated differently from sale with alternatives.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of wage obligation
Focus on the core disagreement: Abu Hanifa holds that uncertainty is removed upon actual use/performance, making the contract valid. The Sahibayn argue that when the wage is due upon delivery (takhliya) rather than performance, uncertainty persists, invalidating the contract.
The sewing case is agreed upon because wage is due upon work; the shop/donkey cases are disputed because wage is due upon delivery.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the contract is valid (Abu Hanifa), the agreed wage corresponding to the actual work is due. If invalid (Sahibayn), the worker receives ujrat al-mithl (proper wage) for the work performed. The text states that the correct view is to give the lesser wage if payment is due without performance.
The mufta bihi appears to be Abu Hanifa's view, as indicated by the phrase 'الصحيح أنه يجب أقل البدلين'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة / الإجارة على أحد الشرطين
فبدرهمين، وأجرتُك هذه الدَّارَ شهراً ،بدرهم، أو هـذه الـدار شهراً بدرهمين، وهكذا إذا كان في ثلاثة أشياء ، وفي أربعة أشياء" لا كما في البيع غير أنه يشترط خيار التعيين في البيع دون الإجارة، لأن في الإجارة الأجرة تجب بالعمل، وعند العمل يتعين بخلاف البيع، فإنَّ الثَّمن يجب بنفس العقد والمبيع مجهول.
فالظاهر أنه يستوفي المنافع، وعند الاستيفاء يرتفع الجهالة، ولو احتيج إلى الإيجاب بمجرد التسليم . عند عدم الاستيفاء بعد التسليم يجب نصف كل واحد من البدلين عند بعض المشايخ ، إذ ليس أحدهما بأولى من الآخر، فيجعل التسليم بهما، والصحيح أنه يجب أقل البدلين ؛ لأنه لا يكون أكثر ضرراً من الانتفاع بأقلهما ضرراً. ذكره الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «شرح الكنز) (۱)
[1]قوله : وهكذا ...الخ ؛ أي وهكذا الحكم وهو جواز العقد ووجوب أجر ما عمل إذا كان الترديد في ثلاثة أشياء ، كما إذا قال : إن خطته فارسيّاً فبدرهم، وإن خطته رومياً فبدرهمين، وإن خطته تركيّاً فبثلاثة دراهم ، أو قال : إن صبغته بعصفمر فبدرهم، وإن صبغته بزعفران فبدرهمين، وإن صبغته بورث ونحوه فبثلاثة دراهم ، وقس على هذا فأي الأعمال عمل استحق الأجر المسمّى.
[٢] قوله : وفي أربعة أشياء... الخ ؛ يعني إن كان الترديد في أربعة أشياء بأن قال : إن خطته فارسيّاً ،فبدرهم، وإن خطته روميّاً فبدرهمين، وإن خطته تركياً فبثلاثة دراهم، وإن خطته هنديّاً فبأربعة دراهم لا يصح العقد كما في البيع، فإنه إذا باع أحد الثوبين على أن يأخذ أيهما شاء جاز.
وكذا إذا قال : بعت أحد هذه الأثواب الثلاثة على أن يأخذ أيهما شاء، وإذا قال : بعت أحد هذه الأثواب الأربعة أو الخمسة فصاعداً على أن يأخذ أيهما شاء لا يجوز.
والجامع في إلحاق الإجارة بالبيع في هذه الصور دفع الحاجة، فإنّها تندفع بالثلاثة ؛ لاشتمالها على الجيد والوسط والرديء ، ولا حاجة إلى الأربعة فصاعداً ؛
وذَكَرَ في «الهداية" في مسألة العطّار، والحدّاد ، وكُرّ البر والشعير خلاف أبى يوسف ، وفي الدابة إلى كوفة ، أو واسط
لاندفاعها بما دونها ، إلا أنه يشترط خيار التعيين في البيع، فإنه إذا خيره بين ثوبين على أن يأخذ أيهما شاء يكون للمشتري الخيار.
وكذا إذا خيره بين ثلاثة أثواب، ولا يشترط ذلك الخيار في الإجارة، فإنّ الأجر لا يجب إلا بالعمل، وعند ذلك يصير المعقود عليه وهو العمل متعيناً، وفي البيع يجب الثمن بنفس العقد، فيتحقق الجهالة على وجه لا يرتفع بإثبات الخيار.
[١]قوله : وذكر في «الهداية...الخ ؛ قال في «الهداية») : ولو قال : إن أسكنتُ في هذا الدكان عطاراً فبدرهم في شهر ، وإن أسكنت حداداً فبدرهمين جاز، وأي الأمرين فعل استحق المسمى فيه عند أبي حنيفة ، وقالا : الإجارة فاسدة. . له، وكذا إذا استأجر بيتاً على أنه إن سكن فيه فبدرهم، وإن أسكن فيه حداداً فبدرهمين، فهو جائز عند أبي حنيفة ، وقالا : لا يجوز. ومن استأجر دابة إلى الحيرة بدرهم ، وإن جاوز بها إلى القادسية فبدرهمين فهو جائز، ويحتمل الخلاف، وإن استأجرها إلى الحيرة على أنه إن حمل عليها كُرّ شعير فبنصف درهم، وإن حمل عليها كُرَّ حنطة فبدرهم، فهو جائز في قول أبي حنيفة له وقالا : لا يجوز. وجه قولهما : إنَّ المعقود عليه مجهول، وكذا الأجر أحد الشيئين وهو مجهول، والجهالة توجب الفساد ، بخلاف الخياطة الروميّة والفارسيّة ؛ لأنَّ الأجر يجب بالعمل، وعنده يرتفع الجهالة، أما في هذه المسائل يجب الأجرُ بالتخلية والتسليم، فيبقى الجهالة، وهذا الحرفُ هو الأصل عندهما.
ولأبي حنيفة الله إنه خيره بين عقدين صحيحين مختلفين فيصح، كما في مسألة الرومية والفارسية ؛ وهذا لأنّ سكناه بنفسه يخالف إسكانه الحداد، ألا تری أنه لا يدخلُ ذلك في مطلق العقد، وكذا في أخواتها، والإجارة تعقد للانتفاع ، وعنده يرتفعُ الجهالة، ولو احتيج إلى الإيجاب بمجرد التسليم يجب أقل الأجرين المتيقن به. انتهى.
Book of Ijarah / Ijarah on One of Two Conditions: ... (then the full passage is translated literally following the Arabic).
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the ruling of ijarah (hire) where the consideration (ujrah) is specified based on which of alternative tasks or conditions is performed. The author first states the general rule: if a person says 'I hired you for this house for a month for one dirham, or this house for a month for two dirhams,' it is valid, and similarly for three alternatives, but not for four or more, analogous to sale (bay') but with a key difference: in ijarah, when the work is performed, the uncertainty is removed, whereas in sale the price is due immediately and the object may remain uncertain. The commentary then discusses the opinion of some mashayikh that if delivery is made without performance, half of each alternative is due, but the correct view is that the lesser of the two is due. The passage then addresses the case of three alternatives, giving examples of sewing in Persian (1 dirham), Roman (2 dirhams), Turkish (3 dirhams), or dyeing with safflower (1), saffron (2), and woad (3). It states that for four or more alternatives, the contract is invalid, as in sale, because need is satisfied with three (good, medium, poor). The exception for khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification) in sale but not in ijarah is explained: in ijarah, the wage is only due upon work, at which point the subject matter becomes specific; in sale, the price is due at contract, so uncertainty remains. The passage then quotes Al-Hidayah on the case of renting a shop to an 'attar (perfumer) or haddad (blacksmith), and a house for residence or housing a blacksmith, and a donkey to Hira or Qadisiyya, and carrying a load of barley or wheat. Abu Hanifa says all these are valid; the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say they are invalid, arguing that both the subject matter and the wage are uncertain, which causes invalidity, unlike the sewing case because there the wage is due upon work and uncertainty is removed. Here, the wage is due upon delivery (takhliya) and remains uncertain. Abu Hanifa's response is that the contract offers a choice between two valid contracts, both of which are different and permissible, and that uncertainty is removed upon actual use. If payment were required merely upon delivery, the lesser of the two wages is due as a certainty.

Key Terms
الإجارة على أحد الشرطين (al-ijarah 'ala ahad al-sharatayn): A hire contract where the consideration (ujrah) is determined by which of two or more conditions is fulfilled (e.g., 'if I sew it Persian, 1 dirham; if Roman, 2 dirhams').
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yeen): The option of specification: in a sale, the buyer may choose which of multiple items to take. Required in sale with alternatives, but not in ijarah.
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Uncertainty or ignorance about the subject matter or price, which can invalidate a contract if excessive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct view regarding the amount due if delivery (takhliya) occurs without performance (the work not yet done)?
A) Half of each alternative wage is due.
B) The lesser of the two wages is due.
C) The higher wage is due.
D) Ujrat al-mithl (proper wage) is due.

Key Takeaway
In ijarah with alternative conditions, the contract is valid for up to three alternatives, and the wage is determined by actual performance; when payment is due upon delivery without performance, the lesser wage is paid, reflecting the Hanafi principle of minimizing harm.

Ijarah on One of Two Conditions: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional rent in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the validity of ijarah with conditional rent and apply the Hanafi position to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
When the rent depends on a choice between two permissible options, the contract remains valid under Abu Hanifa, as uncertainty is resolved through performance.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute over the validity of ijarah when the rent is specified based on one of two possible conditions. The examples given by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah illustrate the practical implications of the disagreement. Understanding the reasoning behind each position is essential for correctly applying the school's relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and examples
Read the passage and list the four examples of conditional ijarah. Note the different conditions (occupation, destination, load).
The common thread: rent varies based on which of two alternatives occurs.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa rules the contract valid (sahih). His proof: the contract gives a choice between two valid contracts, analogous to Roman and Persian tailoring where uncertainty is removed by performance.
If uncertainty remains, the lesser known rent is due.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule the contract void (fasid) due to jahalah in both the subject matter and the rent. They argue that rent is due at delivery (takhliya), so uncertainty persists.
They distinguish tailoring because rent there is due by work, not delivery.
4
Analyze the key difference: timing of rent obligation
The crux is when the rent becomes owed. For Sahibayn, it is at takhliya, so jahalah is fatal. For Abu Hanifa, the rent is not fixed until performance, so the contract is initially a choice between two valid forms.
This reflects different views on the nature of ijarah's obligation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical effect
The relied-upon view in the school is Abu Hanifa's. Thus, such conditional leases are enforceable. Under the Sahibayn's view, the contract would be void and a new contract with a fixed rent required.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the enforceability of the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His words: 'And he mentioned in al-Hidayah... etc.' He said in al-Hidayah: 'If he says: If I seat a perfumer in this shop, then for a dirham per month, and if I seat a blacksmith, then for two dirhams, it is valid, and whichever of the two he does, he deserves the named price according to Abu Hanifa. They (the two) said: The lease is void. Similarly, if he rents a house on condition that if he lives in it himself it is for one dirham, and if he seats a blacksmith it is for two dirhams, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, and they said it is not valid. And if he rents an animal to al-Hira for a dirham, and if he passes with it to al-Qadisiyya for two dirhams, it is valid, and there is potential for disagreement. And if he rents it to al-Hira on condition that if he loads on it a kurr of barley it is for half a dirham, and if he loads on it a kurr of wheat it is for a dirham, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, and they said it is not valid. The basis of their statement: The object of contract is unknown, and also the rent is one of two things and is unknown, and uncertainty necessitates invalidity, unlike Roman and Persian tailoring, because the rent is due by the work, and in his view uncertainty is removed. But in these cases the rent is due by handing over and surrender, so uncertainty remains, and this principle is the foundation in their view. And for Abu Hanifa: He gave him a choice between two valid different contracts, so it is valid, as in the case of Roman and Persian tailoring. This is because his own residence is different from seating the blacksmith; do you not see that the latter does not fall under the absolute contract, and similarly in its analogues. And the lease is contracted for benefit, and in his view uncertainty is removed. And if proof of obligation is needed by mere surrender, the lesser of the two rents which is certain becomes due.' End.
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the validity of an ijarah contract where the rent varies based on one of two specified conditions. The passage presents multiple examples: renting a shop with different rents depending on whether the tenant is a perfumer or a blacksmith; renting a house with different rents if the lessor lives in it vs. if he seats a blacksmith; renting a riding animal to a destination with different rents if he overloads it or goes further; and loading grain of different types with different rents. Abu Hanifa upholds validity in all these cases, while the two companions (the Sahibayn) rule the contract void due to uncertainty (jahalah) in both the subject matter and the rent. Their reasoning is that the rent is due immediately upon delivery of the property (takhliya wa taslim), leaving the uncertainty unresolved. Abu Hanifa counters that the contract gives a choice between two valid contracts, analogous to hiring a tailor for Roman or Persian style stitching, where the rent becomes certain through the work. He also notes that if uncertainty persists, the lesser known rent applies. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the school is Abu Hanifa's view, as it is the stronger argument.

Key Terms
جهالة (jahalah): Uncertainty or ambiguity in the essential terms of a contract (object or price) that leads to invalidity.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The equivalent market rent for similar services or property, used as a fallback when the specified rent is unknown.
تخلية وتسليم (takhliya wa taslim): Handing over the leased property to the lessee, after which the rent becomes due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the lease valid when the rent depends on whether the tenant is a perfumer or a blacksmith?
A) Because the rent is determined at the time of contract.
B) Because it gives a choice between two valid contracts and uncertainty is removed by performance.
C) Because the object is well known in both cases.
D) Because the rent is the same in both cases.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ijarah with rent conditional on one of two permissible alternatives is valid under Abu Hanifa, and this is the relied-upon view.

Conditional Rent in Ijarah: Today vs Tomorrow
Further case of ijarah with conditional rent based on time of performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the three Hanafi positions on conditional ijarah based on time of performance and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A wage conditioned on 'today or tomorrow' creates uncertainty for Zufar but not for Abu Hanifa — intent matters.

In ijarah, the wage must be known at formation. But what if the hirer says: 'If you do it today, I pay a dirham; if tomorrow, half a dirham'? The three major Hanafi authorities disagreed. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the relied-upon ruling. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to identify when a condition introduces prohibited uncertainty versus permissible flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case structure
The case: hiring a tailor, with the wage conditioned on the timing of performance — two possible wages for the same work, alternative based on time.
The work (tailoring) is one, but the wage depends on when it is done.
2
List the three Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: named wage for today, ajr al-mithl for tomorrow (contract valid). Sahibayn: both conditions valid (named wage for each day). Zufar: both conditions void (contract invalid due to uncertainty).
3
Analyze Zufar's reasoning (talil)
Zufar argues that mentioning two alternative prices for one work creates jahalah (uncertainty) — as if saying 'tailor for a dirham or half a dirham', which is void.
The wage is unknown at contract formation because it depends on an uncertain future event (which day).
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
The mention of today is for expediting (ta'jil), not for timing (tawqit). Mentioning tomorrow is for relaxation (tarfiya), not conditioning. Thus the wage is fixed by the actual day of performance.
The work is absolute; the time mention only encourages early work, not a second price specification.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical difference
The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's. Under it, the contract is enforceable; under Zufar's, it would be void and require renegotiation.
The thamarah al-khilaf: validity vs invalidity of the ijarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احتمال الخلاف ، ومسألة الخياطة ، والصَّبْغُ متفق عليهما ) . (ولو ردد" في خياطتِهِ اليوم أو غداً) : أي قال : إن خطته اليوم فبدرهم، وفي غد بنصف درهم، (فله ما سمّى إن خاطه اليوم، وأجر مثلِهِ إن خاطه غدا) : هذا عند أبي حنيفة ، وعندهما الشرطان جائزان ، وعند زُفَر به فاسدان ، لأنَّ ذِكْرَ م للتعجيل، وذكر الغد للترفيه فيجتمع في كل يوم تسميتان [١] قوله : احتمال الخلاف ؛ ووجه ا جه الاحتمال ما ذكره صاحب «العناية»(۲) من أنّ هذه المسألة ذكرت في «الجامع الصغير مطلقاً، فيحتمل أن يكون هذا قول الكل، ويحتمل أن يكون قول أبي حنيفة الله خاصة كما في نظائرها. انتهى. Potential for disagreement, and the issue of tailoring and dyeing are agreed upon. (And if he makes it conditional in terms of his tailoring today or tomorrow): i.e., he said: If you tailor it today, then for a dirham; tomorrow, for half a dirham. (Then he gets what he named if he tailors it today, and the equivalent wage if he tailors it tomorrow): This according to Abu Hanifa. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), both conditions are valid, and according to Zufar, both are void, because mentioning today is for expediting, and mentioning tomorrow is for relaxation, so in each day two price specifications come together. [1] His words: 'Potential for disagreement': The reason for this possibility is what the author of al-'Inayah mentioned: that this issue was reported in al-Jami' al-Saghir in absolute terms, so it could be that this is the consensus opinion, or it could be the opinion of Abu Hanifa alone as in analogous cases. [2] His words: 'And if he makes it conditional...': i.e., if he makes the tailoring of the garment conditional on two price specifications by hesitation between two times, saying: If you tailor it today then for a dirham, and if you tailor it tomorrow then for half a dirham, then if he tailors it today, he gets a dirham, which is the named wage; if he tailors it tomorrow, he gets the equivalent wage. [3] His words: 'Because mentioning today...': Its explanation: Tailoring is one action because he hired him for tailoring absolutely, so the action is not different, it differs only by time, and two alternative prices were mentioned against the tailoring, so the price becomes unknown, as if he said: I stitch it for a dirham or half a dirham, which is void, and so is this. The inner meaning: Mentioning today is for expediting, not for timing; otherwise, the combination of work and time in ijarah would be invalidating. As established in its place. So when mentioning today is for expediting, the wage is in exchange for the tailoring itself on that day, and mentioning tomorrow is for relaxation, not for addition and conditioning. Do you not see that if he isolated the contract for tomorrow, saying: I tailor it tomorrow for half a dirham, this contract would be established today, so that if he tailors it today he would deserve half a dirham, thus in each day two price specifications come together, because the price for tomorrow is also the price for today, and the price for today is also the price for tomorrow.

Commentary
This passage continues the intra-Hanafi discussion on conditional ijarah, now focusing on a specific case: hiring a tailor with different pay depending on whether the work is done today or tomorrow. The text explains that according to Abu Hanifa, if the tailor works today, he gets the named price (a dirham); if he works tomorrow, he gets the equivalent market wage (ajr al-mithl). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider both conditions valid. Zufar holds that both conditions are void. The reasoning for Zufar's position is that mentioning 'today' is for expediting the work, and mentioning 'tomorrow' is for giving relief (tarfiya), so the same tailoring action is associated with two different prices, leading to uncertainty. The commentary from al-'Inayah notes ambiguity in whether the ruling in al-Jami' al-Saghir is consensus or only Abu Hanifa's view. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as it is supported by the analogy with the earlier cases.

Key Terms
تسميتان (tasmiyatan): Two price specifications for the same service, leading to uncertainty in the contract.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): Equivalent market wage for similar work, used when the named wage is not applicable due to the condition.
ترفيه (tarfiya): Relaxation or ease given to the worker by allowing a later deadline with a lower wage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The named wage (half a dirham).
B) The equivalent market wage (ajr al-mithl).
C) Nothing, because the contract is void.
D) Double the named wage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, a conditional wage based on timing is valid per Abu Hanifa if the time mention is interpreted as expediting or relaxation, not as a binding alternative price.

Ijarah with Two Wages Depending on Time of Work
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hiring with two conditional wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an ijarah contract with two conditional wages and explain the reasoning behind interpreting the time mention as expediting rather than fixing.

Core Idea
When the wage depends on the day of work, the contract is saved by interpreting time mention as expediting, not binding.

This passage addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an ijarah contract where the hirer promises different wages depending on whether the work is done today or tomorrow. The core issue is whether such a condition creates fatal ignorance (jahalah) in the wage or whether it can be interpreted in a way that preserves the contract's validity. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the Hanafi principle of preferring validity over invalidity and interpreting potentially ambiguous stipulations figuratively.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling of Abu Hanifa on this contract: what wage is due if the tailor works today, and what if he works tomorrow.
Note the cap on ujr al-mithl: it cannot exceed the named wage for the alternate day.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Examine the positions of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Zufar. The Sahibayn hold both conditions valid; Zufar holds both corrupt the contract.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not an inter-madhhab one.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the Sahibayn's argument: each time is an independent formation with a known wage and a known time, analogous to two different types of sewing.
They rely on the literal meaning of the hirer's statement.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Trace Abu Hanifa's reasoning: mentioning 'today' is for ta'jeel (expediting), not ta'weeq (time-fixing), because combining time-fixing with work would spoil the contract. Similarly, 'tomorrow' is for tarwih (ease).
The Hanafi response uses the principle that the contract should be saved from invalidity wherever possible.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical difference: if the tailor works tomorrow, under Abu Hanifa he gets ujr al-mithl capped at half dirham; under Sahibayn he gets half dirham directly; under Zufar the contract is void.
This shows how the same facts yield different financial outcomes based on legal interpretation.

[1] Possibility of disagreement; the issue of sewing and dyeing are agreed upon. - (And if he vacillated in its sewing today or tomorrow): meaning he said: if you sew it today then a dirham, and tomorrow half a dirham, (then he gets what he named if he sewed it today, and the wage of the like if he sewed it tomorrow): this according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two (Sahibayn) both conditions are valid, and according to Zufar both are corrupt, because the mention of today is for expediting and the mention of tomorrow is for giving ease, so two named wages come together in each day. [1] He said: possibility of disagreement; and the face of its possibility is what the author of al-‘Inayah mentioned: that this issue is mentioned in al-Jami‘ al-Saghir in absolute terms, so it is possible that this is the opinion of all, and possible that it is the opinion of Abu Hanifa specifically as in its parallels. End. [2] He said: and if he vacillated... etc.; meaning if he vacillated in sewing the garment between the two namings by vacillating between the two times, such that he said: if you sew it today then a dirham, and if you sew it tomorrow then half a dirham, then if he sewed it today he gets a dirham, which is the named wage, and if he sewed it tomorrow he gets the wage of the like. [3] He said: because mentioning today... etc.; its exposition: the sewing is one thing because he hired him for sewing in absolute terms, so the action is not different; it only differs by time, and he has mentioned against the sewing two compensations in the manner of substitution, so the compensation becomes unknown, so it is as if he said: I sewed it for a dirham or half a dirham, which is invalid, and so is this. And the secret in it: that mentioning today is for expediting, not for fixing time, otherwise the combination of work and time in ijarah would be necessary, and that is corrupting, as established in its place. So if mentioning today is for expediting, the wage is in exchange for the sewing itself on the day, and mentioning tomorrow is for giving ease, not for addition and attachment; do you not see that if he isolated the contract for tomorrow and said: I sewed it tomorrow for half a dirham, this contract is established today, so that if he sewed it today he would deserve half a dirham, so two named wages come together in each day; because that which is named for tomorrow is also that which is named for today, and that which is named for today is also that which is named for tomorrow. And it does not exceed the named wage. [2] For them: that each one is intended, so it is like the difference of types. And for him: that mentioning today is not for fixing time because combination of time and work is corrupting as previously mentioned; rather his mentioning today is for expediting, and mentioning tomorrow is not for giving ease but his mentioning is for attachment, so two named wages come together in tomorrow. (And it does not exceed the named wage): meaning the wage of the like if it is more than half a dirham no; if each of them is named in both times, then the ijarah is corrupt because mentioning two compensations against one exchanged thing is corrupting, so it becomes analogous to his saying: I sold you spot for a thousand and deferred for two thousand, and the answer to this inference is that the ignorance is removed by the occurrence of the work, because by it the wage is determined for its binding at the time of work, as previously mentioned, so remember. [ ] He said: for them... etc.; this is an inference for what Abu Yusuf and Muhammad went to, and its exposition: that each of expediting and delaying is intended for purposes, and the contracted thing is the work, so it becomes like the difference of types, like Roman and Persian sewing. And it may be inferred upon it that mentioning today is for fixing time, and mentioning tomorrow is for addition, so this is the literal meaning, and using them for giving ease and expediting is figurative, and speech is upon its literal meaning until evidence for the figurative is established, especially if carrying it upon the figurative leads to corruption; and each one of them is known, and their compensations are also known, so it becomes like Roman and Persian sewing. 2 He said: and for him... etc.; this is an inference for what the Imam went to. And its analysis: that mentioning today is for expediting, and mentioning tomorrow is for attachment and addition, and speech is upon its literal meaning until evidence for its figurative meaning is established; and indeed evidence has been established for the figurative meaning in mentioning today, which is expediting; because their intent is the desire for validity, and it is determined in the figurative; because specifying the work with fixing time is corrupting; for specifying the work necessitates him being a common hired worker, and specifying the time does not necessitate him being a common hired worker, and there is incompatibility between them, so they do not combine and it becomes corrupt; so the figurative is determined lest it become corrupt, so we carried it upon expediting.
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an ijarah contract where the hirer stipulates two different wages depending on the day the work is performed: a dirham if sewn today, half a dirham if sewn tomorrow. The core question is whether such a condition renders the contract valid or invalid, and what wage is owed. 

Imam Abu Hanifa rules that if the tailor sews today, he receives the named wage (one dirham). If he sews tomorrow, he receives the wage of the like (ujr al-mithl), but capped at the named wage for tomorrow (half a dirham) — it does not exceed that amount. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that both conditions are valid, so the tailor receives the specifically named wage for whichever day he works. Zufar holds that both conditions are corrupt, rendering the contract invalid. 

The reasoning revolves around whether mentioning 'today' and 'tomorrow' is for ta'jeel (expediting) or for ta'weeq (fixing a time). Abu Hanifa argues that mentioning 'today' is merely an exhortation to sew quickly, not a binding temporal condition; combining a fixed time with the work would spoil the contract because the worker would become an ajir mushtarak (common worker) while time-fixing requires exclusivity. Similarly, mentioning 'tomorrow' grants ease (tarwih) and does not attach the wage to that time. If it did, both wages would be named for both times, causing confusion. In contrast, the Sahibayn contend that each time is an independent formation with its own intended wage, akin to two different types of work (e.g., Roman vs. Persian sewing). They argue that both time and wage are known, so no ignorance (jahalah) exists. The author of the sharh also addresses an objection: that the contract is like selling spot for one price and deferred for another — but the answer is that ignorance is removed once the work is performed, because the wage is determined at that moment. 

The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of reconciling textual interpretation with legal principles: Abu Hanifa's approach preserves the validity of the contract by interpreting potentially corrupting conditions as non-binding exhortations, while the Sahibayn uphold the literal wording. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is generally Abu Hanifa's view, as it is presented first and supported by the principle that the contract should be saved from invalidity whenever possible.

Key Terms
ترديد (tardid): Vacillation between two options; here, the hirer's statement offering two different wages depending on the day of work.
تعجيل (ta'jeel): Expediting; interpreting the mention of 'today' as a prompt to work quickly, not as a binding time condition.
أجر مثل (ujr al-mithl): The wage of the like; the market rate for similar work when the named wage is not applicable (due to unfulfilled condition).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the ijarah contract where the hirer says 'if you sew today, I give you a dirham; if tomorrow, half a dirham', and the tailor sews tomorrow, what does Abu Hanifa rule?
A) The tailor gets half a dirham as named.
B) The tailor gets the wage of the like (ujr al-mithl), capped at half a dirham.
C) The contract is invalid and the tailor gets nothing.
D) The tailor gets either half a dirham or the full dirham at his choice.

Key Takeaway
When a hirer stipulates different wages for different days, Abu Hanifa interprets the time mention as non-binding to preserve contract validity, awarding ujr al-mithl for the alternate day, capped at the named wage.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate

Ijarah with Two Named Wages and the Limitation of the Like Wage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ijarah with two wage conditions and ruling on exceeding named wage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of ijarah with two named wages for different times and apply the rule that the like wage in a corrupt ijarah does not exceed the named wage.

Core Idea
When two named wages appear for different times, Imam Abu Hanifa deems the contract valid by interpreting time as acceleration; the like wage is bounded by the named amounts.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an ijarah contract where two different wages are named for two different times (e.g., today for one dirham and tomorrow for half a dirham). The commentator presents the arguments of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and then explores the related principle that in a corrupt ijarah, the like wage (ajr al-mithl) cannot exceed the named wage. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the Hanafi school balances contractual stipulation with fairness and prevents exploitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed contract scenario
The contract is: 'I hire you to sew today for one dirham and tomorrow for half a dirham.' The dispute is whether naming two different wages for two different times makes the contract valid, corrupt, or something else.
The wages are known and the times are specified.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds the contract is valid if work is done on the first day; the wage for that day is due. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold the contract is corrupt (fasid) because both wages are intended.
The disagreement is about the interpretation of 'today' and 'tomorrow'.
3
Trace the arguments (dalil)
Sahibayn argue that each time reference is literal, like two different types of tailoring (Roman and Persian), so both obligations stand. Imam counters that combining time specification with work type specification creates a contradiction (the worker cannot be both a common worker and a specific worker simultaneously), so 'today' must be metaphorical for acceleration.
Imam's argument relies on the principle that literal interpretation would corrupt the contract.
4
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the worker sews today: according to Imam, one dirham is due; according to Sahibayn, the contract is corrupt and ajr al-mithl is due. If the worker sews on the second day: according to Imam, the contract becomes corrupt due to two namings, so ajr al-mithl between half and one dirham; according to Sahibayn, it is corrupt from the start.
The difference affects the amount owed.
5
Analyze the second ruling: 'لا يجاوز به المسمى'
The principle that the like wage in a corrupt ijarah does not exceed the named amount. When two namings exist (e.g., one dirham and half a dirham), the first naming prevents increase above the higher named amount, and the second naming prevents decrease below the lower named amount, so the like wage is bounded between the two.
This applies when the work is done on a day different from the specified ones.

كتاب الإجارة / الإجارة على أحد الشرطين
درهم
يجب الزيادة، وفي «الجامع الصغير»: لا يزاد على درهم، ولا ينقص عن نصف . لكن الصحيح هو الأول ؛ لأنَّ المسمى في الغد نصف درهم، وفي الإجارة الفاسدة أجر المثلِ لا يزادُ على المسمّى ، وإن خاطه في اليوم الثالث، فأجرُ المثل لا يزاد على نصف درهم. وفي الغد لم يقم الدليل على إرادة المجاز، وهو الترفيه، كما قام الدليل على إرادة الحقيقة، وهو الإضافة والتعليق، فتركناه على حقيقته، فإذا خاطه اليوم وجب عليه الدرهم، فإن جاء الغد فسد لوجود تسميتين فيه ؛ لأنَّ المعلق يترك بمجيء الغد، والتسمية الأولى باقية، فيفسد لاجتماع تسميتين في عمل واحد بخلاف الخياطة الرومية والفارسيّة ؛ لأنه ليس لأحد العقدين موجب في العمل الآخر، فكانا عقدين مختلفين ، كل واحد منهما يبدل مسمّى على الانفراد معلوم فافترقا(۲).
[١]قوله : لا يزاد....الخ ؛ لأنَّ التسمية الأولى لا تنعدم في اليوم الثاني، فيعتبر لمنع الزيادة، وتعتبر التسمية الثانية لمنع النقصان. كذا في «الهداية»(۳).
وأورد عليه : إن التسمية في الإجارة الفاسدة تمنع الزيادة عندنا، كما تقرر في موضعه، فلا تمنع النقصان أصلاً ، بل يجب أجر المثل وإن نقص عن المسمى فما معنى أن يعتبر التسمية الثانية لمنع النقصان.
[٢]قوله : لكن الصحيح هو الأول ؛ وهذا على ما ذهب إليه الإمام، أما عندهما فالصحيح أنه ينقض من نصف درهم، ولا يزاد عليه. صرح به العَيْنِيُّ (4) ، والزَّيْلَعِي ) وغيرهما.

Because if each of them is named in the two times, the hire becomes corrupt; because mentioning two substitutes for one substituted is corrupting, so it becomes like his saying: I sold you immediately for a thousand and deferred for two thousand. And the answer to this inference is that ignorance is removed by the occurrence of the work, for the wage becomes determined by its necessity at the time of work, as previously mentioned. So remember. [ ] His saying: For them...etc.; this is an inference on what Abu Yusuf and Muhammad went to. Its explanation: That each of acceleration and deferral is intended for purposes, and the contracted matter is the work, so it became like differing types, like Roman and Persian tailoring. And it may be inferred by that mentioning 'today' is for specification, and mentioning 'tomorrow' is for addition, so this is literal, and using them for postponement and acceleration is metaphorical, and speech is literal until evidence for metaphor appears, especially if carrying it metaphorically leads to corruption, and each of them is known, and their substitutes are also known, so it became like Roman and Persian tailoring. 2 His saying: And for him...etc.; this is an inference on what the Imam (Abu Hanifa) went to. Its explanation: That mentioning 'today' is for acceleration, and mentioning 'tomorrow' is for suspension, and addition (?) and speech is literal until evidence for its metaphor appears, and evidence has appeared for metaphor in mentioning 'today', which is acceleration; because their desire is for validity, and it is determined in metaphor; because specifying the work with time is corrupting, for specifying the work necessitates him being a common worker, and specifying the time does not necessitate him being a common worker, and there is contradiction between them so they cannot combine, thus it is corrupt, so metaphor is determined to avoid corruption, so we carried it upon acceleration. (1) See: al-Tabyin (5:139). Book of Ijarah / Ijarah on one of the two conditions dirham. The increase is obligatory, and in al-Jami' al-Saghir: It is not increased above a dirham, nor decreased below half. But the correct is the first; because the named on tomorrow is half a dirham, and in corrupt ijarah, the like wage is not increased above the named, and if he sewed it on the third day, then the like wage is not increased above half a dirham. And on tomorrow, evidence for intending metaphor did not stand, which is postponement, as evidence for intending the literal stood, which is addition and suspension, so we left it on its literal. So if he sewed it today, a dirham becomes obligatory. Then if tomorrow comes, it becomes corrupt due to the presence of two namings in it; because the suspended is left with the coming of tomorrow, and the first naming remains, so it becomes corrupt due to the gathering of two namings in one work, unlike Roman and Persian tailoring; because neither contract has a requirement in the other work, so they were two different contracts, each one substitutes a named amount independently known, so they differ. [1] His saying: It is not increased...etc.; because the first naming does not become nonexistent on the second day, so it is considered to prevent increase, and the second naming is considered to prevent decrease. Thus in al-Hidayah (3:247). And an objection is raised against it: The naming in corrupt ijarah prevents increase according to us, as established in its place, so it does not prevent decrease at all, rather the like wage is obligatory even if it is less than the named. So what does it mean that the second naming is considered to prevent decrease? [2] His saying: But the correct is the first; and this is according to what the Imam went to. As for according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the correct is that it is decreased from half a dirham and not increased upon it. This is stated by al-Ayni (2:202) and al-Zayla'i (5:140) and others. (1) End from al-Jami' al-Saghir (p. 443), and the phrasing includes forward and backward, as his phrasing: It is not decreased from half a dirham, nor increased above a dirham. (2) See: al-Tabyin (5:140). (3) Al-Hidayah (3:247). (4) In al-Ramz (2:202). (5) In al-Tabyin (5:140).
Source pages p. 600

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling on ijarah (hire) with two conditions, specifically where the hirer says, 'I hire you to sew today for one dirham and tomorrow for half a dirham.' The commentator first presents the dispute: The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that both acceleration and deferral are intended, so it is like two different types of work (e.g., Roman and Persian tailoring), making the contract valid with two wages. They further argue that mentioning 'today' and 'tomorrow' is literal specification. Imam Abu Hanifa counters that mentioning 'today' is not for specification but for acceleration, and mentioning 'tomorrow' is not for postponement but for suspension, so on tomorrow two namings (the wage for today and the wage for tomorrow) meet, causing corruption. However, the corruption is avoided because the work done on the first day determines the wage; the second wage only applies if work is delayed, thus only one wage actually applies. The commentator then discusses the second ruling: 'It does not exceed the named amount.' This means that in a corrupt ijarah, the like wage (ajr al-mithl) cannot exceed the named wage if the named wage is over half a dirham. For example, if the named wage for sewing tomorrow is half a dirham, and the actual work is done on a different day, the like wage cannot exceed half a dirham. The correct position (according to Imam Abu Hanifa) is that the like wage can be increased above half a dirham up to a full dirham, as indicated in al-Jami' al-Saghir. The commentator notes that according to the Sahibayn, the like wage cannot exceed half a dirham. The passage concludes with an objection: If naming in corrupt ijarah only prevents increase but not decrease, how can the second naming prevent decrease? The answer is that the first naming prevents increase and the second naming prevents decrease, so the wage is capped between half and one dirham. The mufta bihi position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa: the contract is valid if the work is done on the first day, and the wage for that day is due; if work is done on the second day, the contract becomes corrupt due to two namings. The like wage is then between half and one dirham, not exceeding the named amounts.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): The naming or stipulation of a specific wage in a contract.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The comparable market wage for the same type of work in a corrupt or unspecified ijarah.
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): A hire contract that is corrupt due to a defect, such as ambiguity in wage or time, but can be validated by performance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person says, 'I hire you to sew today for 1 dirham and tomorrow for half a dirham' and the worker sews today?
A) The contract is valid, and the worker receives 1 dirham.
B) The contract is valid, and the worker receives half a dirham.
C) The contract is corrupt, and the worker receives the like wage.
D) The contract is void, and the worker receives nothing.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when two wages are named for two different times, the contract is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa because the time references are interpreted as acceleration and suspension, and the like wage in a corrupt ijarah is bounded by the named amounts.

Ijarah with Two Conditional Wages: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ijarah with two conditional wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a hire contract with two conditional wages and apply the mufta bihi (operative ruling) from Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
A hire contract with two alternative wages becomes invalid when the condition triggers a different day; the named wage caps the equivalent wage.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh tradition addresses a specific scenario: hiring a tailor with a conditional wage—1 dirham if today, half dirham if tomorrow. The scholars disagree on the outcome when the work is performed on the different day. We will analyze the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the reasoning behind each, and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the legal issue
Identify the contract: hire with two alternative wages depending on the day the work is performed. The issue is what wage is due when the work is done on the second day.
The contract is conditional: the wage depends on when the work occurs.
2
Present Imam Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that if work is done today, the full dirham is due; if done tomorrow, the contract becomes invalid (fasid) and the equivalent wage is capped at half dirham (the named wage for that day).
His proof: literal interpretation of the condition; the first naming prevents increase, the second prevents decrease.
3
Present the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the wage must be decreased from half dirham and cannot exceed it; the equivalent wage may be less than half.
They argue that naming in an invalid contract only prevents increase, not decrease.
4
Analyze the objection and the Hanafi response
The commentator addresses an objection: if naming only prevents increase, how can it prevent decrease? The response is that the first naming prevents increase, the second prevents decrease—this is consistent with Abu Hanifa's view.
The objection stems from a general rule about naming in invalid contracts.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
The commentator states 'the correct is the first' (Imam Abu Hanifa). The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the worker is guaranteed at least the named wage (half dirham); under Sahibayn, he may receive less.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the amount the worker receives when work is done on the second day.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a hire contract with two conditional wages: one dirham if the work is done today, half a dirham if done tomorrow. The author first states the ruling that the named wage must be paid (increase is required) and cites Al-Jami' al-Saghir which says it cannot exceed a dirham or fall below half. The correct view, according to the commentator, is the first: the wage is determined by the named amount based on the day the work is actually performed. The reasoning is that the contract is valid if the work is done today (the suspended condition does not take effect) but becomes invalid if done tomorrow because two namings exist. In an invalid contract, the equivalent wage is due but cannot exceed the named amount. The commentator then explains the proof: the first naming prevents increase, the second prevents decrease. An objection is raised: in an invalid hire, naming prevents increase but does not prevent decrease; the equivalent wage is due even if less. The commentator responds that this is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the correct view is that the wage must be decreased from half a dirham and cannot exceed it. This difference is practical: under Abu Hanifa, if the work is done tomorrow, the contract is invalid and the lower named wage (half dirham) sets a cap on the equivalent wage; under the Sahibayn, the equivalent wage may be less than half dirham but cannot exceed it. The passage highlights the application of usul principles: literal meaning is preferred, and the effect of conditions on contract validity.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): An invalid hire contract that is not void but defective, requiring the equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl) not exceeding the named wage.
تسمية (tasmiyah): Naming or specifying a wage in the contract.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The equivalent market wage for similar work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The wage is 1/2 dirham because the contract becomes invalid and the equivalent wage cannot exceed the named wage.
B) The wage is 1 dirham because the contract is valid and the higher wage applies.
C) The wage is determined by the market rate, regardless of the named amounts.
D) The contract is void and no wage is due.

Key Takeaway
In an invalid hire contract with two conflicting namings, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the equivalent wage is capped by the lower named wage, while the Sahibayn hold it must be decreased from that amount.

Traveling with a Hired Slave: Custom as a Legal Restriction
Commentary on a matn ruling with analogical proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on traveling with a hired slave without stipulation and explain the role of custom (urf) and analogy (qiyas) in deriving the ruling.

Core Idea
An absolute hire contract for a slave is confined by custom to local service; travel requires a stipulation.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a key rule in hire contracts: a hirer cannot take a hired slave on a journey unless agreed. The commentator uses analogies from hiring horses and houses to show that custom restricts the contract's scope. Understanding this reveals how Hanafi fiqh uses 'urf and qiyas to fill contractual gaps.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is traveling with a hired slave without stipulation. The ruling is that it is prohibited (haram); the hirer becomes a usurper (ghāṣib) and is liable to the master for damages, and if the slave returns safely, the hirer gets no wage.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is based on custom (al-‘urf) and analogy (qiyās). The absolute contract (muṭlaq al-‘aqd) is interpreted according to the predominant custom, which is service in the city (hadar). Travel imposes extra hardship not covered by the contract.
The text explicitly states: 'al-muṭlaq yataqayyad bi-mithli dhālika min al-muta‘ārif'.
3
Understand the role of custom
Custom restricts the absolute contract. Since people commonly hire slaves for local service, the contract is understood to apply only to that. Transferring the slave to travel service is a change in the nature of the work, not covered by the contract.
Al-‘urf al-‘āmm (general custom) is a recognized source of restriction in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Examine the analogies (qiyās)
The commentator draws two analogies: (1) Hiring a horse for riding – you cannot ride a different horse. (2) Hiring a house for dwelling – you cannot house a blacksmith in it. In both, the contract specifies a particular use, and changing it without agreement is not allowed. The common illa (effective cause) is the additional burden or change in service.
These analogies show that the ruling is based on the principle that the contract is limited to what is agreed or customary.
5
Note the exceptions and contrasts
Exception: If travel is stipulated explicitly, or if at the time of contract the context indicated readiness for travel (e.g., the hirer was preparing for a journey), then travel is allowed. Contrast: A slave bequeathed for service (al-‘abd al-mūṣā bi-khidmatihī) – the legatee may travel with the slave unconditionally because the legatee bears the slave's maintenance and no custom restricts the bequest.
The exception 'al-ma‘rūf ka al-mashrūṭ' (the known is like the stipulated) is applied, showing the importance of custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولا يسافر بعبد...الخ ؛ يعني من استأجر عبداً ليخدمه فليس له أن يسافر به إلا أن يشترط ذلك السفر، حتى لو سافر به يضمن لمولاه ؛ لأنه صار غاصباً، ولو رده إلى مولاه سالماً لا أجر له عندنا. صرح به العيني)، وغيره. ووجه امتناع السفر به في هذه الصورة أنّ مطلق العقد يتناولُ الخدمة في الحضر إذ هو الأعم الأغلب، وعليه عرف الناس ، فانصرف إليه ؛ لأنَّ المطلق يتقيد بمثل ذلك من المتعارف ، فلا يكون للمستأجر أن ينقل ذلك العبد إلى خدمة السفر، إذ خدمة السفر اشتملت على زيادة مشقة مفضية الى النزاع، فلا ينتظمها إطلاق العقد. فصار كما لو استأجر فرساً للركوب فليس له أن يركب غيره للتفاوت، وكذا لو استأجر داراً للسكنى فليس له أن يسكن فيه حداداً ؛ لأنه أضر ومطلق العقد لا يتناوله. أما إذا شرط ذلك أو كان وقت الإجارة متهيئاً للسفر وعرف ذلك فيجوز له السفر به؛ لأنّ الشرط أملك عليك أم لك، والمعروف كالمشروط، بخلاف العبد الموصى بخدمته، فإنّ له أن يسافر به مطلقاً، سواء شرط السفر به أو لا ؛ لأنَّ مؤنته عليه، ولم يوجد العرف في حقه(٢).
His saying: 'And he does not travel with a slave... etc.' means: Whoever hires a slave to serve him may not travel with him unless he stipulates that travel. Thus, if he travels with him, he is liable to his master because he becomes a usurper, and if he returns him to his master safe, he has no wage according to us. This is stated by al-‘Ayni and others. The reason for prohibiting travel with him in this case is that the absolute contract encompasses service in the city, as it is the most common and predominant, and people's custom is upon that, so it is restricted to it. Because the absolute is restricted by such customary practice. So the hirer may not transfer the slave to travel service, since travel service involves additional hardship leading to dispute, so the absolute contract does not include it. It is like if one hires a horse for riding, he may not ride another due to difference; similarly, if one hires a house for dwelling, he may not house a blacksmith in it because it is harmful and the absolute contract does not cover it. But if he stipulates that, or if at the time of hire he was ready for travel and that was known, then he may travel with him, because the condition is more binding upon you or for you, and the known is like the stipulated. Contrary to a slave bequeathed for service, for he may travel with him absolutely, whether he stipulates travel or not, because his maintenance is upon the legatee and custom does not exist in his regard.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn ruling that a hirer may not travel with a hired slave unless stipulated. The commentator explains that the default in a hire contract is service in the city (hadar), as that is the common practice (al-‘urf al-‘amm). Travel involves extra hardship and is not covered by the absolute contract. He supports this with analogies: hiring a horse for riding does not permit riding another horse, and hiring a house for dwelling does not permit using it for a blacksmith who causes damage. The underlying principle is that the contract is interpreted according to custom. However, if travel is explicitly stipulated, or if at the time of contract the context indicated travel (e.g., the hirer was preparing to travel), then it is permitted. The commentator contrasts this with a slave bequeathed for service (al-‘abd al-muwsā bi-khidmatihī), where the legatee may travel with the slave unconditionally because the slave's maintenance is on the legatee and no custom restricts it. This distinction shows that the restriction in the hired slave case is based on custom and the nature of the contract, not a general prohibition.

Key Terms
عبد مستأجر (‘abd musta’jar): A slave hired for service, typically for domestic or local work.
مطلق العقد (muṭlaq al-‘aqd): The absolute, unrestricted contract of hire that does not specify travel or other conditions.
العرف (al-‘urf): Customary practice of the people in transactions, used to restrict the absolute contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because travel is inherently prohibited in Islamic law
B) Because the absolute contract is restricted by custom to local service, and travel imposes extra burden
C) Because the slave's master forbids travel
D) Because the hirer must pay extra wage for travel

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule that a hirer cannot travel with a hired slave without stipulation is grounded in custom and analogy, emphasizing that contract terms are interpreted within their customary context.

Hirer Cannot Reclaim Wage Paid to a Restricted Slave
Brief ruling that a hirer cannot recover the wage paid to a restricted slave for work done.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wage payment to a restricted slave and explain why the hirer cannot reclaim it.

Core Idea
The hirer's payment to a restricted slave is valid and irrevocable.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school concerning hire (ijārah) of a restricted slave. Although the slave is under interdiction and cannot independently engage in transactions, the wage earned through his labor is valid and cannot be taken back by the hirer. Understanding this ruling clarifies the school's protection of earned compensation, even when the recipient lacks full legal capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The subject is a hirer who hires a restricted slave (ʿabd maḥjūr) and pays him the wage after the work is done. The ruling is that the hirer cannot reclaim that wage.
The restriction (ḥajr) on the slave does not affect the validity of the wage.
2
Understand the condition of the slave
The slave is maḥjūr ʿalayh – legally restricted, e.g., due to minority or bankruptcy. Normally such a person cannot validly contract. However, the wage here is for actual labor performed.
3
Recognize the legal effect
The payment vests in the slave, and the hirer loses the right to recover it. The wage is considered the slave's rightful compensation.
The ruling protects the slave's right to the fruit of his labor.
4
Contrast with potential objections
One might think the payment to a restricted person is ineffective. The Hanafi position emphasizes that the labor itself is not restricted, so the wage is valid.
This is a feature of Hanafi fiqh: compensation for work is not invalidated by the worker's legal incapacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولا يسترده. ... الخ ؛ يعني من استأجر عبداً محجوراً عليه شهراً مثلاً ، أو أعطاه الأجر بعد عمله فليس للمستأجر أن يسترد الأجر.
His saying: 'And he does not reclaim... etc.' means: Whoever hires a restricted slave ([e.g.] for a month) or gives him the wage after his work, the hirer may not reclaim the wage.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the second part of the matn: 'and the hirer does not reclaim the wage for what a restricted slave has worked.' The commentator clarifies that if a person hires a slave who is legally restricted (mahjūr ‘alayh) — meaning the slave is under interdiction and cannot manage his own affairs — and the slave performs the work, then the hirer pays the wage to the slave. That payment is valid and the hirer cannot later recover it. This applies even if the slave worked for a month or any period. The ruling protects the slave's right to compensation for his labor and prevents the hirer from unjustly taking back what was given. The 'restricted slave' here likely refers to a slave who is interdicted due to bankruptcy or minority, but the text does not elaborate.

Key Terms
عبد محجور (‘abd maḥjūr): A slave who is legally restricted (under interdiction), e.g., due to being a minor or bankrupt, and cannot contract on his own.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when a hirer pays a restricted slave (abd mahjur) for work done?
A) The hirer can reclaim the wage because the slave is restricted
B) The hirer must pay the master instead of the slave
C) The hirer cannot reclaim the wage once paid
D) The contract is invalid and no wage is due

Key Takeaway
Under Hanafi fiqh, compensation for actual labor performed by a restricted person is valid and cannot be reclaimed by the payer.

Ruling on Traveling with a Hired Slave
Commentary on prohibition of traveling with hired slave without stipulation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on traveling with a hired slave and explain the role of custom and stipulation in the contract.

Core Idea
Traveling with a hired slave requires stipulation; otherwise, the hirer becomes a usurper and forfeits wages.

In this passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah, we learn a key principle of Hanafi ijarah: the default scope of a hire contract is determined by common custom. This lesson unpacks the ruling that traveling without stipulation turns the hirer into a guarantor (ghasib) and denies him wages for the journey. We will also explore the exceptions and the underlying reasoning based on custom and analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hiring a slave for service and then traveling with him without stipulating travel. The ruling is that this is prohibited (makruh tahrimi) and the hirer becomes a usurper (ghasib).
The prohibition is not absolute; it depends on the contract's scope.
2
Locate the dalil (proof) based on custom and analogy
The proof is derived from the general custom ('urf) that service is normally in the city, and from analogies to hiring a horse (cannot ride a different horse) and hiring a house (cannot house a blacksmith).
The custom restricts the absolute contract.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The absolute contract (mutlaq) is interpreted according to what is common (a‘amm al-aghallab). Since city service is the norm, the contract is confined to that. Travel service involves extra hardship not covered by the default understanding.
The principle: 'al-mutlaq yuqayyad bi al-muta‘araf' (the absolute is restricted by custom).
4
Note the exceptions and distinction
If travel is stipulated or the known context (e.g., hiring season) implies it, travel is permissible. A slave bequeathed for service is different: the beneficiary may travel even without stipulation because maintenance is on him and no contrary custom exists.
Stipulation is binding ('al-shart amlak'), and the known is like the stipulated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل إجارة العبد ولا يسافر بعبد مستأجر للخدمة إلا بشرطه [1] قوله : ولا يسافر بعبد...الخ ؛ يعني من استأجر عبداً ليخدمه فليس له أن يسافر به إلا أن يشترط ذلك السفر، حتى لو سافر به يضمن لمولاه ؛ لأنه صار غاصباً، ولو رده إلى مولاه سالماً لا أجر له عندنا. صرح به العيني وغيره. ووجه امتناع السفر به في هذه الصورة أنّ مطلق العقد يتناولُ الخدمة في الحضر إذ هو الأعم الأغلب، وعليه عرف الناس ، فانصرف إليه ؛ لأنَّ المطلق يتقيد بمثل ذلك من المتعارف ، فلا يكون للمستأجر أن ينقل ذلك العبد إلى خدمة السفر، إذ خدمة السفر اشتملت على زيادة مشقة مفضية الى النزاع، فلا ينتظمها إطلاق العقد. فصار كما لو استأجر فرساً للركوب فليس له أن يركب غيره للتفاوت، وكذا لو استأجر داراً للسكنى فليس له أن يسكن فيه حداداً ؛ لأنه أضر ومطلق العقد لا يتناوله. أما إذا شرط ذلك أو كان وقت الإجارة متهيئاً للسفر وعرف ذلك فيجوز له السفر به؛ لأنّ الشرط أملك عليك أم لك، والمعروف كالمشروط، بخلاف العبد الموصى بخدمته، فإنّ له أن يسافر به مطلقاً، سواء شرط السفر به أو لا ؛ لأنَّ مؤنته عليه، ولم يوجد العرف في حقه(٢).
Chapter of hiring a slave. One should not travel with a hired slave for service except with a stipulation. [1] His saying: 'and one should not travel with a slave...' etc.; meaning: whoever hires a slave to serve him, he does not have the right to travel with him unless he stipulates that travel; even if he travels with him, he guarantees to his master because he becomes a usurper; and if he returns him to his master safe, he has no hire according to us. Al-Ayni and others stated it explicitly. The reason for prohibiting travel with him in this case is that the absolute contract encompasses service in the city since it is the more common and prevalent, and based on the custom of people, so it is restricted to that; because the absolute is restricted by such customary usage. Thus the hirer cannot transfer that slave to travel service, since traveling service involves additional hardship leading to dispute, so the absolute contract does not cover it. It is similar to if one hires a horse for riding, he cannot ride another because of disparity; similarly, if one hires a house for residence, he cannot house a blacksmith in it because it is more harmful and the absolute contract does not include it. But if he stipulates that, or if at the time of hire the context was prepared for travel and that was known, then it is permissible for him to travel with him; because the stipulation is binding, and the known is like the stipulated. This is unlike a slave bequeathed for service, for whom one may travel with him absolutely, whether travel is stipulated or not, because his maintenance is on [the beneficiary] and no custom exists in his regard.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This is a commentary on the matn of Al-Wiqayah. The author explains the ruling that a person who hires a slave for service in the city cannot take the slave on a journey unless this was explicitly stipulated in the contract. The reason is that the default understanding of a hire contract for service is service in the city, as that is the common practice. If the hirer takes the slave on a journey without stipulation, he becomes a guarantor (mustadmin) for the slave's value to the master, because he is considered a usurper (ghasib). Even if he returns the slave safely, he is not entitled to any wages for the work done during the journey, according to the Hanafi school. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) considering custom (`urf). The author draws an analogy: if one hires a horse for riding, he cannot ride a different horse without permission; similarly, if one hires a house for residence, he cannot use it for a harmful purpose like housing a blacksmith. However, if the travel was stipulated or implied by the known context (e.g., the slave was hired in a traveling season), then travel is permissible. A distinction is made: if the slave is bequeathed for service (in a will), then the beneficiary may travel with him even without stipulation, because the maintenance is on the beneficiary and no contrary custom exists.

Key Terms
إجارة (ijarah): A contract of hiring for service or usufruct.
عبد محجور (abd mahjur): A slave who is legally interdicted from financial transactions.
غاصب (ghasib): One who takes another's property without right.
شرط (shart): A condition stipulated in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person hires a slave for service in the city without stipulating travel. He then takes the slave on a journey. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The hire is valid and the hirer must pay wages for the journey.
B) The hirer is a usurper and must compensate the master; he gets no wages.
C) The hire becomes invalid and the slave is free.
D) The hirer may travel if he pays extra wages.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, custom defines the contract's scope; traveling without stipulation is prohibited and makes the hirer a usurper with no wage claim.

Istihsan in Ijarah: The Case of the Interdicted Slave
Commentary on the rule that the hirer cannot recover wages from a hired slave under interdiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recovery of wages from a hired interdicted slave and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
A contract with an interdicted slave becomes valid after completion by istihsan, so the hirer cannot recover wages.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in ijarah (hiring) where a slave under interdiction (mahjur) performs work for a hirer. The initial contract would be fasid (defective) due to the slave's lack of capacity, but after the work is completed, Hanafi law upholds the contract by istihsan. Understanding this ruling clarifies how istihsan operates to achieve a practical benefit (the master's right to the wage) over strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial ruling
The act is hiring an interdicted slave. Initially, the contract is fasid because the slave cannot contract independently without the master's permission. By qiyas (analogy) with other defective contracts, the contract would be void and wages recoverable.
Fasid means defective but not void; it can become valid under certain conditions.
2
Determine the consequence after work is completed
After the slave has performed the work and received wages, the hirer tries to recover the wages. The ruling says he cannot recover them.
The key point: the ruling changes after the work is done.
3
Locate the dalil and legal reasoning
The proof is istihsan (juristic preference). The author states that after completion, the contract is valid by istihsan. The apparent analogy would declare the contract void, but istihsan overrides this due to a stronger consideration.
Istihsan is a departure from strict analogy for a reason that is stronger in the eyes of the law.
4
Analyze the illa (effective cause)
The invalidity was originally to protect the master's right (since the slave's earnings belong to the master). By upholding the contract after completion, the master receives the wage through the slave, thus protecting his right. The illa for istihsan is the benefit to the master that arises only after the work is done.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy): the hidden cause is the benefit accruing to the master after completion.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider the contract void ab initio because the slave lacked capacity, making the wages recoverable by the hirer. The Hanafi position is based on istihsan, which is not accepted by all schools.
This ikhtilaf highlights the role of istihsan as a distinct Hanafi source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يسترد مستأجر أجر ما عمل عبد محجور [2] قوله : ولا يسترده...الخ ؛ يعني من استأجر عبداً محجوراً عليه شهراً مثلاً ، أو أعطاه الأجر بعد عمله فليس للمستأجر أن يسترد الأجر. لأن هذه الإجارة بعد الفراغ صحيحة استحساناً ، لأن الفساد لرعاية حق المولى، فبعد الفراغ رعاية حقه في الصحة ووجوب الأجرة.
The hirer does not recover the wage of what is done by a slave under interdiction. [2] His saying: 'and he does not recover it'... etc.; meaning: whoever hires a slave who is under interdiction for a month, for example, or gives him the wage after his work, the hirer does not have the right to recover the wage. Because this hiring, after completion, is valid by istihsan; since the invalidity is due to consideration of the master's right, so after completion, the consideration of his right is for validity and obligation of the wage.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This is a commentary on the second part of the matn. The author explains that if a person hires a slave who is legally interdicted (mahjur) for a specified period, and the slave performs the work and receives wages, the hirer cannot reclaim the wages. Despite the contract being potentially invalid initially because the slave is interdicted (disallowing him to contract), once the work is completed, the contract becomes valid by istihsan. The reason is that the invalidity was meant to protect the master's right (since the slave's earnings belong to the master). After the work is done, the master's right is better served by upholding the contract and ensuring the wage is received. Therefore, the wage belongs to the slave (ultimately to the master), and the hirer cannot take it back.

Key Terms
عبد محجور (abd mahjur): A slave under legal interdiction, unable to contract independently.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method to depart from strict analogy for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the Hirer not recover wages after an interdicted slave completes work?
A) Because the hirer was at fault for hiring an interdicted slave.
B) Because the contract becomes valid by istihsan after completion.
C) Because the slave has a right to the wages.
D) Because the master already received the wages.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a hiring contract with an interdicted slave becomes valid after completion by istihsan, protecting the master's right to wages and preventing the hirer from recovering them.
