No Liability for Consuming the Usurped Slave's Earnings
Commentary on the rule that a usurper is not liable for consuming the earnings of a usurped slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a usurper consuming the wages of a usurped slave, explain the reasoning based on the concept of protected property (al-mal al-muhraz), and apply the distinction between beneficial and harmful transactions.

Core Idea
A usurper is not liable for consuming the slave's earnings because the slave's hand does not secure property.

In Hanafi law, the concept of protected property (mal muhraz) is essential for establishing liability. This lesson explores a specific case: a usurper who consumes the wages earned by the usurped slave. You will learn why Abu Hanifa holds that no guarantee is due, based on the principle that the slave's hand is not a preserving hand. We will also examine the istihsan that validates the slave's hire contract after safe completion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Understand the basic facts: a man usurps a slave, the slave hires himself out, the usurper takes and consumes the wage. What is Abu Hanifa's ruling? No guarantee.
The ruling is a hukm wad'i (declaratory): no liability.
2
Grasp the key concept: ihraz (protection)
Liability for destruction of property requires that the property be 'protected' (muhraz), i.e., in a preserving hand (like the owner's or his agent's). The slave’s hand does not count as a preserving hand because the slave himself is not secure.
The slave's earnings follow the usurper's hand, but since the usurper already holds the slave, the earnings are not separately secured.
3
Trace the dalil (reasoning)
The reasoning: guarantee only arises from destroying protected, valuable property. The slave's earnings are not protected because the slave does not secure himself. Hence, no guarantee.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof).
4
Examine the istihsan regarding the contract
The passage also explains why the slave's hire contract is valid after completion (istihsan). The contract is beneficial (wage for the master) and not harmful if the slave finishes safely. The slave is interdicted only from harmful transactions. Thus, the wage leaves the slave's ownership and the hirer cannot recover it.
This distinguishes between the validity of the contract and the liability for consuming the wage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يضمن اكل غلة عبد غصبَهُ فَاجْرَ هو نفسه، رجلٌ غصب عبداً ، فأَجْرَ العبد نفسه، فأخذ الغاصب الأجر فأكله ، فلا ضمان عند أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنَّ العبد لا يحرز نفسه، فكذا ما في يده ، فلا يكون متقوماً. [١]قوله : استحساناً ؛ القياس أن لا يجوز عقد الإجارة ؛ لأنَّ عقد المحجور عليه لا يجوز لانعدام الإذن، وقيام الحجر ، فيصيرُ المستأجر غاصباً بالاستعمال، ولا أجر على الغاصب. [٢] قوله : لأن الفساد.... الخ ؛ تقرير الاستحسان : إنّ التصرف نافع على اعتبار فراغ العبد عن العمل سالماً، وضار على اعتبار هلاك العبد، والنافع مأذون فيه فيجوز فيخرج الأجرة عن ملكه ، فليس له أن يسترده. والسر فيه : إن العبد محجورٌ عن تصرُّف يضرُّ بالمولى، لا عن تصرف ينفعه، ألا ترى أنه يجوز للعبد أن يقبل الهبة من غير أن يأذنه المولى؛ لأنه نافع في حق المولى فالإجارة إذا جازت بعدما سلم من العمل يحصل الأجر للمولى بغيرِ ضرر، ولو حكم بعد جوازها لضاع متاع العبد عليه مجاناً، فتعين القولُ بالجواز. وإذا جازت الإجارة صح قبض العبد الأجرة ؛ لأنه هو العاقد، ومتى صح قبضه لا يكون للمستأجر أن يسترده منه، بخلاف ما إذا هلك العبد في حالة الاستعمال، فإنّه يجب على المستأجر قيمته، وإذا ضمن صار مالكاً من وقت الاستعمال فيصير مستوفياً عبد نفسه، فلا يجب عليه الأجر [٣] قوله : لأن العبد...الخ ؛ تقريره : إن الضمان لا يجب إلا بإتلاف مال محرز متقوم، وهذا ليس بمحرز؛ لأنّ الإحراز إنّما يثبتُ بيد حافظة كيد المالك، أو بيد نائبه ، ويد المالك لم يثبت عليه، ويد العبد ليست يد المولى ؛ لأنّ العبد في يد الغاصب، وما في يده يكون في يد الغاصب تبعاً لنفسه.
And one does not guarantee the consumption of the produce of a slave whom he usurped and the slave hired himself. A man usurped a slave, then the slave hired himself, then the usurper took the wage and consumed it; there is no guarantee according to Abu Hanifa because the slave does not secure himself, and likewise what is in his hand is not secured property. [1] His saying: 'by istihsan'; the analogy that the hire contract is not valid because the contract of an interdicted person is not valid due to lack of permission and existence of interdiction, so the hirer becomes a usurper by use, and there is no wage on the usurper. [2] His saying: 'because the invalidity...' etc.; the explanation of istihsan: the transaction is beneficial on the consideration of the slave finishing work safely, and harmful on the consideration of the slave perishing; the beneficial is permitted, so it is valid, and the wage leaves his ownership, so he cannot recover it. The secret in it: the slave is interdicted from transactions that harm the master, not from transactions that benefit him. Do you not see that the slave may accept a gift without the master's permission? Because it is beneficial for the master. So hire, when it is valid after safety from work, yields the wage for the master without harm. And if it were judged invalid, the slave's labor would be wasted for nothing, so the view of validity is determined. And when the hire is valid, the slave's taking of the wage is valid because he is the contractor; and when his taking is valid, the hirer cannot recover it from him. This differs from if the slave perishes during use, where the hirer must pay his value; and if he guarantees, he becomes owner from the time of use, so he becomes a user of his own slave, and no wage is due. [3] His saying: 'because the slave...' etc.; its explanation: guarantee is only obligatory for destroying protected, valuable property; this is not protected because protection is established by a preserving hand like the hand of the owner or his agent; the owner's hand is not established over it, and the hand of the slave is not the hand of the master because the slave is in the hand of the usurper, and what is in his hand is in the hand of the usurper as a consequence of himself.
Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This is a commentary on the third part of the matn. The author explains the ruling that if a person usurps a slave, and the slave hires himself out, and the usurper consumes the wages, the usurper is not liable for damages according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The reasoning is that the slave's earnings do not constitute protected property (mal muhraz) because the slave himself is not in a position to secure his own property; his hand is not a preserving hand. The commentary also discusses the istihsan that makes the slave's hire contract valid after completion, distinguishing between beneficial and harmful transactions. The slave is interdicted only from harmful transactions. Once the work is done safely, the contract is valid, and the wage belongs to the master. The hirer cannot recover it. However, if the slave dies during use, the hirer must pay his value, and then becomes owner retroactively, so no wage is due.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee for damages.
غلة (ghullah): Produce or earnings, here the wage of the slave.
إحراز (ihraz): Securing or protecting property in one's possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because he is a usurper.
B) No, because the slave's earnings are not secured property.
C) Yes, because the slave's earnings belong to the master.
D) No, because the contract was invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, liability for consuming the earnings of a usurped slave does not arise because the earnings are not considered protected property (muhraz) in the slave's hand.

Usurper's Liability for Slave's Wage: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on daman of consumed wage from slave's hire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether a usurper guarantees the wage of a wrongfully seized slave, and explain the rationale based on the concepts of ihraz (safeguarding) and mutaqawwam (legal value).

Core Idea
A usurper's liability for a slave's wage hinges on whether the wage is 'safeguarded' (muhraz); Abu Hanifa says no, the Sahibayn say yes.

In this lesson, we explore a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: If a usurper consumes the wage earned by a slave he wrongfully seized, is he liable to the master? Abu Hanifa argues no because the wage in the slave's hand is not safeguarded, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue yes because it remains the master's property. This case reveals the subtle interplay between property concepts of ihraz and mutaqawwam in Hanafi fiqh, and how istihsan (juristic preference) validates the slave's hire contract for the master's benefit.

Guided Path
1
State the case
Describe the scenario: a man usurps a slave, the slave hires himself out, earns a wage, and the usurper takes and consumes that wage. The question is whether the usurper must compensate the master for the wage.
The slave is under the usurper's physical control throughout.
2
Identify the positions
State the two Hanafi rulings: Abu Hanifa holds that the usurper is not liable (la daman); the Sahibayn hold that he is liable (yadman). This is a recorded intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
Both positions are from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Trace Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that liability only arises for destroying property that is muhraz (safeguarded) and mutaqawwam (valuable). The wage in the slave's hand is not muhraz because the slave himself is not safeguarding against the usurper; the slave's hand is not the master's hand. Hence, the wage is not mutaqawwam and no guarantee.
Key principle: the usurper's hand over the slave prevents the slave from acting as a safe custodian for the wage.
4
Trace the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn counter that the wage is the property of the master (mal al-mawla). The usurper's consumption is an act of transgression (ta'addi) against the master's property, so he must guarantee it regardless of whether the wage was physically safeguarded.
They focus on ownership (milk) rather than physical custody (ihraz).
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the master cannot claim compensation from the usurper; under the Sahibayn, the usurper must pay the wage amount to the master. This affects who bears the loss if the usurper spends the wage.
The passage notes consensus that the slave's receipt is valid and the master may take the wage from the slave if still extant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يضمن أكل غلة عبد غصبه فأجر هو نفسه لأن هذه الإجارة بعد الفراغ صحيحة استحساناً، لأن الفساد لرعاية حق المولى، فبعد الفراغ رعاية حقه في الصحة ووجوب الأجرة.
(ولا يضمن أكل غلّة عبدِ غصبَهُ فَأَجْرَ هو نفسه)، رجلٌ غصب عبداً، فأَجْرَ العبد نفسه، فأخذ الغاصب الأجر فأكله، فلا ضمان عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنَّ العبد لا يحرز نفسه، فكذا ما في يده، فلا يكون متقوماً.
[١]قوله: استحساناً؛ القياس أن لا يجوز عقد الإجارة؛ لأنَّ عقد المحجور عليه لا يجوز لانعدام الإذن، وقيام الحجر، فيصيرُ المستأجر غاصباً بالاستعمال، ولا أجر على الغاصب.
[٢] قوله: لأن الفساد.... الخ؛ تقرير الاستحسان: إنّ التصرف نافع على اعتبار فراغ العبد عن العمل سالماً، وضار على اعتبار هلاك العبد، والنافع مأذون فيه فيجوز فيخرج الأجرة عن ملكه، فليس له أن يسترده.
والسر فيه: إن العبد محجورٌ عن تصرُّف يضرُّ بالمولى، لا عن تصرف ينفعه، ألا ترى أنه يجوز للعبد أن يقبل الهبة من غير أن يأذنه المولى؛ لأنه نافع في حق المولى فالإجارة إذا جازت بعدما سلم من العمل يحصل الأجر للمولى بغيرِ ضرر، ولو حكم بعد جوازها لضاع متاع العبد عليه مجاناً، فتعين القولُ بالجواز.
منفعة .
(1)
وإذا جازت الإجارة صح قبض العبد الأجرة؛ لأنه هو العاقد، ومتى صح قبضه لا يكون للمستأجر أن يسترده منه، بخلاف ما إذا هلك العبد في حالة الاستعمال، فإنّه يجب على المستأجر قيمته، وإذا ضمن صار مالكاً من وقت الاستعمال فيصير مستوفياً عبد نفسه، فلا يجب عليه الأجر " [٣] قوله: لأن العبد...الخ؛ تقريره: إن الضمان لا يجب إلا بإتلاف مال محرز متقوم، وهذا ليس بمحرز؛ لأنّ الإحراز إنّما يثبتُ بيد حافظة كيد المالك، أو بيد نائبه، ويد المالك لم يثبت عليه، ويد العبد ليست يد المولى؛ لأنّ العبد في يد الغاصب، وما في يده يكون في يد الغاصب تبعاً لنفسه.
وقالا: يضمن؛ لأنَّه مالُ المولى".
(وصح للعبد قبضها، ويأخذها مولاه قائمةً)، هذا بالاتفاق؛ لأنَّ بعد الفراغ يعتبر مأذونا كما مرّ.
فلا يتصور أن يكون محرزاً بحرزه، إذ هو لا يحرز نفسه عن الغاصب، فكيف يحرزُ ما في يده عنه، وما لم يقع في يد المولى حقيقة أو حكماً بالاستنابة لا يكون معصوماً له، فإن اختلج في قلبك أنّ الغاصب إذا استهلك ولد المغصوبة ضمنه، ولا إحراز فيه، فازحه بأنه تابع للأم؛ لكونه جزءاً منها، وهي محرزة، بخلاف الأجر، فإنّه حصل من المنافع، وهي غير محرزة. هكذا قالوا).
١ ] قوله: لأنه مالُ المولى؛ فإنّ إجارة العبدِ نفسه جائزة على تقدير السلامة كما تقدم، وسلب العبد يكون للمولى؛ لأنه تبع لرقبته، فيكون الغاصب متعدّياً بالأخذ منه والإتلاف، فلا جرم أن يضمن). [٢]قوله: وصح للعبد...الخ؛ أي وجاز للعبد قبض الأجرة في قولهم جميعاً؛ لأنه مأذون في التصرُّف على اعتبار الفراغ، كما تقدّم، فبعد الفراغ رعاية حقه في الصحة، فإنّ التصرُّفَ النَّافع مأذون فيه، وهو العاقد، فترجع الحقوق إليه، فيكون له القبض. وفائدته تظهر في خروج المستأجر عن عهدة الأجرة، فإنه يحصل بالأداء إليه، وإنّما وضع المسألة فيما إذا أجرَ العبد المغصوب نفسه؛ لأنه إن أجره الغاصب كان له الأجر لا للمالك، ولا ضمان عليه بالاتفاق، وإن أجره المولى فليس للعبد أن يقبض الأجرة إلا بوكالة المولى؛ لأنه هو العاقد. كذا في «العناية»، وغيرها. [٣] قوله: ويأخذها مولاه قائمة؛ يعني لو وجد مولى العبد ما في يد العبد من الأجرة قائمة أخذه؛ لأنه وجد عين ماله ولا يلزم من بطلان التقوم بطلان الملك كما القطع، فإنه لم يبقَ متقوماً حتى لا يضمن بالإتلاف، ويبقى الملك في د فيه في المسروق بعد حتى يأخذه المالك.
And he does not guarantee the consumption of the produce of a slave whom he usurped, and then the slave hired himself out, because this hire is valid after completion by istihsan, since the invalidity is for the sake of protecting the master's right, so after completion, protection of his right is in validity and in the obligation of the wage. (And he does not guarantee the consumption of the produce of a slave whom he usurped, and then the slave hired himself out): a man usurped a slave, then the slave hired himself out, so the usurper took the wage and consumed it—there is no guarantee according to Abu Hanifa, because the slave does not safeguard himself, and likewise what is in his hand, so it is not considered valuable. [1] His saying 'by istihsan': the qiyas is that the contract of hire is not valid because the contract of a person under interdiction is not valid due to the absence of permission and the existence of interdiction, so the lessee becomes a usurper by use, and there is no wage upon the usurper. [2] His saying 'because the invalidity... etc.': the explanation of istihsan: the transaction is beneficial regarding the slave's completion of work safely, and harmful regarding the slave's destruction, and the beneficial is permitted, so it is valid, and the wage leaves his ownership, so he cannot reclaim it. And the secret in it is: the slave is interdicted from transactions that harm the master, not from transactions that benefit him. Do you not see that it is permissible for the slave to accept a gift without the master's permission, because it is beneficial for the master? So if the hire is valid after he is safe from work, the wage is obtained for the master without harm, and if it were ruled invalid, the slave's labor would be wasted, so the ruling of validity is determined. (1) And when the hire is valid, the slave's receipt of the wage is valid, because he is the contracting party, and whenever his receipt is valid, the lessee cannot reclaim it from him, unlike if the slave perishes during work, then the lessee must pay his value, and when he guarantees, he becomes owner from the time of use, so he becomes a user of his own slave, so the wage is not obligatory upon him. [3] His saying 'because the slave... etc.': its explanation: guarantee is only obligatory for destroying property that is safeguarded and valuable, and this is not safeguarded, because safeguarding is established by a protecting hand like the hand of the owner or his agent, and the hand of the owner is not established over it, and the hand of the slave is not the hand of the master, because the slave is in the hand of the usurper, and what is in his hand is in the hand of the usurper as a consequence of himself. And they both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he guarantees, because it is the property of the master. (And it is valid for the slave to receive it, and his master takes it as it stands), this is by agreement, because after completion he is considered permitted as previously. So it cannot be conceived that it is safeguarded by his guarding, since he does not guard himself from the usurper, so how can he guard what is in his hand from him? And what has not come into the hand of the master actually or virtually by deputyship is not protected for him. If it occurs to your mind that if the usurper consumes the offspring of the usurped animal, he guarantees it, and there is no safeguarding in it, then remove it by saying it is a follow of the mother, being part of her, and she is safeguarded, unlike the wage, which is obtained from benefits, and they are not safeguarded. Thus they said. 1] His saying 'because it is the property of the master': the hire of the slave himself is valid on the condition of safety as previously, and the earnings of the slave belong to the master, because they are subsidiary to his status as property, so the usurper is transgressing by taking and destroying it, so he must guarantee. [2] His saying 'and it is valid for the slave to receive it... etc.': meaning it is permissible for the slave to receive the wage in all their sayings, because he is permitted in the transaction based on completion, as previously. So after completion, his right is considered in validity, for the beneficial transaction is permitted, and he is the contracting party, so rights return to him, so he has the right to receive. Its benefit appears in releasing the lessee from the responsibility for the wage, because it is fulfilled by paying to him. And the case is placed where the usurped slave hired himself out, because if the usurper hired him out, the wage is for him, not for the master, and there is no guarantee by agreement. And if the master hired him out, the slave cannot receive the wage except by the master's agency, because he (the master) is the contracting party. Thus in al-'Inayah and others. [3] His saying 'and his master takes it as it stands': meaning if the master of the slave finds the wage in the slave's hand as it stands, he takes it, because he found his own property in kind, and the invalidity of being considered valuable does not necessitate the invalidity of ownership—just as with the thief, it does not remain valuable so that he guarantees by destroying it, but ownership remains in it until the owner takes it.
Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, discusses the liability of a usurper (ghasib) who consumes the wage earned by a wrongfully seized slave who hired himself out. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute, with Abu Hanifa holding that the usurper is not liable, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that he is. The commentary first explains that the slave's contract of hire is valid by istihsan (juridical preference) rather than by qiyas, because it benefits the master if the slave completes the work safely. However, the invalidity (if ruled) would protect the master from harm. After completion, the hire is valid, and the slave's receipt of the wage is valid. The dispute on liability hinges on whether the wage in the slave's hand is considered 'muhraz' (safeguarded) and thus subject to guarantee upon destruction. Abu Hanifa argues that since the slave does not safeguard himself against the usurper, he cannot safeguard the wage; it is not 'mutaqawwam' (valuable for liability). The Sahibayn argue that the wage is the master's property, and the usurper's consumption is destruction of that property, thus he must guarantee. The passage then notes a consensus (ittifaq) that the slave's receipt of the wage is valid and the master may take it from him as it stands, because after completion the slave is considered permitted. The master's right to take the wage is compared to a thief's ownership of stolen goods until the owner reclaims them—ownership remains despite the item not being considered valuable for liability purposes.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference that departs from strict qiyas (analogy) for a stronger reason, here to validate the slave's hire after safe completion to benefit the master.
محرز (muhraz): Something that is effectively safeguarded or protected, typically under someone's actual control. The wage in the slave's hand is not muhraz because the slave himself is under the usurper's control.
متقوم (mutaqawwam): Valuable property recognized by Islamic law as having financial worth and thus subject to guarantee upon destruction. The wage is not mutaqawwam in the slave's hand due to lack of ihraz.
غصب (ghasb): Wrongful seizure and control of another's property without right; the usurper (ghasib) is liable for the property while in his possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a usurper who consumes the wage earned by a wrongfully seized slave who hired himself out?
A) He is not liable according to Abu Hanifa, but liable according to the Sahibayn.
B) He is liable according to all Hanafi imams.
C) He is not liable according to all Hanafi imams.
D) He is liable only if the slave did not complete the work.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school records a disagreement: Abu Hanifa holds no liability for the usurper consuming the slave's wage due to lack of ihraz, while the Sahibayn hold liability because it is the master's property.

Validity of Slave Accepting Hire and Master's Right to Take It
Ruling on slave's hire acceptance and master's repossession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates the slave's acceptance of hire, state the condition for the master's repossession, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on liability.

Core Idea
A slave's acceptance of hire is valid after work completion; the master may take it as his property—but liability for loss is disputed.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school on a peculiar scenario: a usurped slave hires himself out. After the work, can the slave validly take the hire? And what rights does the master have? The passage resolves these questions, introducing an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the matn
The passage states two clear rulings: (1) it is valid for the slave to take possession of the hire, and (2) the master takes the hire if it still exists (qa'imah).
2
Understand the rationale for validity
After completing the work, the slave is considered authorized (ma'dhun) to transact, so he can receive payment. This is agreed upon bil-itifaq.
3
Analyze the master's right to take the hire
The master finds his own property (mal) in the slave's hand. The hire is not safeguarded in the slave's hands because the slave cannot even protect himself from a usurper, so protection (ihraz) is lacking.
The text rebuts an objection using the analogy of offspring of usurped property.
4
Examine the liability dispute
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold the slave is liable if the hire is destroyed because it is the master's wealth. Abu Hanifa's position (implied) is that the slave is not liable, as he is an amin after completion.
This difference affects who bears the loss if the hire is destroyed before the master takes it.

وصح للعبد قبضها، ويأخذها مولاه قائمةً

The book of Ijarah / Ijarah of the slave. And it is valid for the slave to take possession of it (the hire), and his master takes it as it exists (as a tangible asset). And both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he (the slave) is liable because it is the wealth of the master. (And it is valid for the slave) to take possession of it, and his master takes it as it exists; this is by agreement because after the completion (of the period) he is considered authorized as previously mentioned. So it is not conceivable that he is a protector (muhriz) by his own protection, since he cannot protect himself from the usurper, so how can he protect what is in his hand from him? And what has not come into the hand of the master, either actually or constructively through deputyship, is not safeguarded for him. If it occurs to your mind that the usurper, if he consumes the offspring of the usurped object, is liable, and there is no safeguarding (by the usurper) in it, then repel it by (saying) that it is subsidiary to the mother because it is part of her, and she is safeguarded, unlike the hire, for it is obtained from the usufruct, which is not safeguarded. Thus they said. [1] Commentary: Because it is the wealth of the master; for the ijarah of the slave himself is valid on the condition of safety as previously, and the earnings of the slave belong to the master because it is ancillary to his ownership (raqabah), so the usurper commits transgression by taking and destroying it, therefore he is liable. [2] Commentary: The phrase 'and it is valid for the slave...' means it is permissible for the slave to take possession of the hire according to all of them because he is authorized to transact on the basis of completion, as previously. After completion, consideration is given to his right for validity, for beneficial transactions are permitted, and he is the contracting party, so rights revert to him, thus he has the right to take possession. Its benefit appears in the hirer being freed from liability for the hire, for it is achieved by paying him. The issue is placed in the case where the usurped slave hires himself; for if the usurper hires him, the hire goes to the usurper, not the owner, and there is no liability by agreement. If the owner hires him, the slave cannot take the hire except by the owner's agency, because the owner is the contracting party. Thus in al-`Inayah and others. [3] Commentary: The phrase 'and his master takes it as it exists' means if the master finds the hire in the slave's hand as a tangible asset, he takes it because he finds the very property of his own money, and the invalidity of pecuniary value does not entail invalidity of ownership, as with stolen property, for it does not remain valuable such that one becomes liable for destruction, but ownership remains in it until the owner takes it.
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the commentary on Ijarah of a slave. The matn states two key rulings: (1) it is valid for the slave to take possession of the hire (ujrah), and (2) the master may take that hire from the slave if it is still physically present (qa'imah). The commentary explains that this is agreed upon because after the completion of the work, the slave is considered authorized (ma'dhun) to transact, as previously mentioned in the chapter on permission (idhn). The slave cannot protect the hire as he cannot even protect himself from a usurper (ghasib), so the hire is not safeguarded until it reaches the master actually or constructively. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: if a usurper consumes the offspring of a usurped animal, he is liable despite no safeguarding of the offspring per se. The response is that the offspring is subsidiary to the mother, which is safeguarded, unlike the hire which arises from usufruct (manafi'), which is not a tangible object. The commentary then elaborates on each phrase: the hire is the master's property because the slave's earnings follow his ownership; the slave's right to accept payment is valid because he is the contracting party after completion; the master may take the hire as it exists because he finds his very property, and loss of marketability does not nullify ownership.

Key Terms
مأذون (ma'dhun): Authorized; the slave is considered authorized to transact after completing the ijarah period.
محرز (muhriz): One who secures/protects property such that it is considered in their lawful possession for liability purposes.
قائمة (qa'imah): Existing as a tangible asset; the hire is physically present and unprescribed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The slave must return it to the hirer.
D) It becomes the property of the usurper (ghasib).

Key Takeaway
The slave's acceptance of hire is valid, and the master may reclaim the hire if it remains, but liability for destroyed hire is disputed between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Hiring for Two Months with Different Unspecified Rates: Validity Through Default Interpretation
Validity of a two-month ijarah with differing monthly rates without specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a two-month ijarah contract with differing monthly rates without specification, and explain the principle of taharri al-jawaz that resolves the ambiguity.

Core Idea
The contract is valid because the first month defaults to the first rate mentioned.

In ijarah, ambiguity in specifying which month corresponds to which rental rate might seem to invalidate the contract. However, the Hanafi school upholds the contract by applying the principle that words are interpreted in the order they are spoken, and the first month refers to the period immediately following the contract. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Consider a contract where a hirer says: 'I hire this slave for two months: one month for 4 dirhams and one month for 5 dirhams' without specifying which month is for which rate. What is the ruling?
2
Recognize the apparent problem
The lack of specification (ta'yin) creates ambiguity. Some schools would deem such a contract invalid due to uncertainty in the rent (gharar).
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of taharri al-jawaz
Hanafi usul dictates that contracts are interpreted in a way that upholds validity over nullity. The wording 'first a month for four' is interpreted to refer to the month immediately following the contract.
This is analogous to saying 'I hire this slave for a month' without further detail – it refers to the next month.
4
Determine the order by insiraf
The first month referred to is the one adjacent to the contract. The second month then follows sequentially. Hence the first month is at the first-mentioned rate (4 dirhams).
5
Conclude the ruling
The contract is valid (sahih). If the slave works only the first month, he is entitled to 4 dirhams. If both months are worked, the rent is 4 and 5 dirhams respectively.

ولو استأجر عبداً شهرين شهراً بأربعة، وشهراً بخمسة صح والأوّلُ بأربعة.
[١] قوله : ولو استأجر ... الخ ; يعني لو استأجر رجلاً عبداً لشهرين شهراً بأربعة دراهم وشهراً بخمسة دراهم من غير تعيين منهما ، صح العقد على الترتيب المذكور، فالأول من هذين الشهرين بأربعة دراهم، حتى لو عمل في الأول دون الثاني استحق أربعة دراهم، فإنّه لما قال : أوّلاً شهراً باربعة ينصرفُ إلى ما يلى العقد تحرّياً للجواز. كما إذا قال : استاجرتُ منك هذا العبد شهراً، وسكت فإنه ينصرف إلى ما يلي العقد، ونظراً إلى قضاء الحاجة في الحال، فإنّ الإنسان إنّما يستأجر الشيء لحاجة تدعوه إلى ذلك، والظاهر وقوعها عند العقد، وإذا انصرف الأوّل إلى ما يلي العقد والثاني معطوف عليه ينصرف إلى ما يلي الأوّل ضرورة. [۲] قوله : عبداً شهرين ; وهذا أولى ما قال في «الهداية» : من استأجر عبداً هذين الشهرين، فإنّه محتاج التأويل كما لا يخفى على من له إلى الحذاقة سبيل.
And if he hires a slave for two months: one month for four (dirhams), and one month for five (dirhams), it is valid, and the first is for four. [1] Commentary: He said: 'and if he hires...' meaning if a man hires a slave for two months: one month for four dirhams and one month for five dirhams, without specification from either of them, the contract is valid in the mentioned order, so the first of these two months is for four dirhams, such that if he works in the first but not the second, he deserves four dirhams. Because when he said 'firstly: a month for four', it refers to what immediately follows the contract, seeking validity (taharriyan lil-jawaz). Just as if he said: 'I hired from you this slave for a month' and was silent, it refers to what immediately follows the contract, and considering the fulfillment of immediate need, for a person only hires something due to a need that impels him to it, and the apparent situation is that the need occurs at the time of the contract. And when the first refers to what immediately follows the contract, and the second is conjuncted to it, it necessarily refers to what immediately follows the first. [2] Commentary: The phrase 'a slave for two months' – this is more appropriate than what was said in al-Hidayah: 'Whoever hires a slave for these two months' because that requires interpretation, as is not hidden from one who has expertise.
Source pages p. 606

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific ijarah contract where the hirer agrees to hire a slave for two consecutive months, with the first month's rent being four dirhams and the second month's five dirhams, without specifying which month is which. The Hanafi ruling is that the contract is valid (sahih), and the first month (from the start of the contract) is considered to be the one at the lower rate of four dirhams. The reasoning is based on the principle of interpreting the contract in a way that makes it effective (taharriyan lil-jawaz): the word 'first' (awwalan) refers to the period immediately following the contract, and the second month follows that. This is analogous to a case where someone says 'I hired this slave for a month' without specifying details — it refers to the immediate next month. The commentary also notes a text from al-Hidayah where the phrase 'these two months' is used, which requires interpretation; the current phrasing is clearer.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of which month is intended; here absent, but contract still valid.
انصراف (insiraf): The default interpretation of a term to refer to the immediate context.
تحرِّي الجواز (taharri al-jawaz): Seeking to interpret words in a way that renders the contract valid and effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hirer says 'I hire this slave for two months: one month for 4 dirhams and one month for 5 dirhams' without specifying which month is which, what is the ruling?
A) The contract is invalid because the rent is uncertain.
B) The contract is valid, and the first month is for 5 dirhams (higher rent).
C) The contract is valid, and the first month is for 4 dirhams (the lower rent).
D) The contract is valid, but the slave must work both months and then the rent is decided by the master.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ambiguity in contractual terms that can be resolved by default interpretation does not invalidate the contract.

Dispute Over Timing of Slave's Illness or Absconding
Ruling on who has the stronger claim when hirer and master dispute timing of slave's illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the hirer and master dispute the timing of a slave's illness or absconding, and explain the proof based on the current state (hukm al-hal).

Core Idea
The current condition of the slave decides the dispute: the apparent indicates the past.

In a hire (ijara) contract, if the hired slave is found ill or absconded at the end of the period, the hirer and master may dispute when the condition began. The Hanafi school looks to the current state of the slave to resolve this dispute. This lesson explains the rule and its rational proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the dispute
The hirer claims the illness/absconding existed from the start; the master claims it happened recently.
The object is a hired slave, but the rule applies analogously to any hired property.
2
Understand the ruling — the hirer's word is accepted
If the slave is currently ill or absconded, the hirer's claim that it started at the beginning of the term is accepted.
This is not because the hirer is more trustworthy, but because the current state supports his claim.
3
Locate the evidence — the current state (al-hal)
The present condition of the slave is used as circumstantial evidence (qarinah).
Al-hal is a form of evidence in Hanafi fiqh when direct proof is absent.
4
Analyze the principle — al-zahir yadullu 'ala al-madi
The apparent state now indicates that it likely existed in the past. This is a rational principle used in legal reasoning.
It is not a definitive proof (qati) but a strong indicator (amarah).
5
Apply the principle to the ijarah contract
Because the hirer could not utilize the slave from the start due to illness or absconding, he is not liable for the full rent.
The consequence: the rent is reduced or cancelled proportionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحُكْمَ الحال إن قال مستأجر العبد : مرض هو، أو أبق في أول المدة. [٣] قوله : وحكم الحال; صورة المسألة : إنّ رجلاً استأجر عبداً شهراً بدرهم فقبضه في أوّل الشهر ثم جاء آخر الشهر والعبد مريض أو أبق، واختلف المستأجر والآجر في إبـاق العبد أو مرضه، فادعى المستأجر وجود المرض أو الإباق في أوّل المدة، وادعى المولى وجوده قبل الإخبار بساعة ، فجعل الحال حكماً بينهما. فلو كان العبد مريضاً أو آبقاً في الحال فالقولُ للمستأجر ; لأنّ الظاهر شاهد له، فإنّ الإباق والمرض ظاهر في الحال، وهو يدلُّ على ما مضى فكان عدم التمكن من
And the ruling of the current state: if the hirer of the slave says: he was ill or absconded at the beginning of the period. [3] Commentary: The scenario is that a man hires a slave for a month for one dirham and takes possession at the beginning of the month; then at the end of the month the slave is ill or absconded, and the hirer and the master dispute about the absconding or illness of the slave. The hirer claims the illness or absconding occurred at the beginning of the period, and the master claims it occurred an hour before the report. So the current state is made a judgment between them. If the slave is currently ill or absconded, then the word is with the hirer because the apparent situation supports him. Indeed, the absconding and illness are apparent in the current state, and that indicates the past, so the inability to utilize...
Source pages p. 606

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute in an ijarah contract. The scenario: a slave is hired for a month; at the end of the month, the slave is found to be ill or to have absconded. The hirer claims the condition existed from the beginning of the period (which would give him a right to reduce or cancel the hire), while the master claims it occurred only a short while before the end of the period (so no reduction). The Hanafi ruling: the court looks at the current state (al-hal). If the slave is presently ill or absent, the hirer's claim is accepted (qawluhu al-musta'jir) because the apparent condition (zahir) supports the claim of continuity. The reasoning is that the current state of illness or absconding is strong evidence that it existed previously, based on the principle that what is apparent now likely existed earlier (al-zahir yadullu 'ala al-madi). Thus, the hirer is not required to pay the full rent.

Key Terms
حكم الحال (hukm al-hal): The ruling derived from observing the current state of affairs; used as evidence in disputes.
ظاهر (zahir): The apparent or manifest state; here, the present condition of the slave serves as a circumstantial evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The master's claim that illness occurred recently.
B) The hirer's claim that illness existed from the start.
C) Neither; a judge decides based on oaths.
D) The claim is split, with compensation calculated proportionally.

Key Takeaway
In disputes over the timing of a condition in a hire contract, the current state of the object serves as circumstantial evidence, and the claim consistent with that evidence is accepted.

Hiring for Two Months with Different Wages: Validity by Order of Mention
Ruling on validity and wage allocation in a single rental contract with differing wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of insiraf (interpretation by order of mention) to determine the validity and wage allocation in a rental contract with unspecified timing.

Core Idea
In a rental contract with two differing wages, the order of mention dictates the sequence and validates the contract.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school: if a person hires a slave for two months with different wages (e.g., one month for four dirhams and one month for five) without specifying which month corresponds to which wage, the contract is valid and the first month is at the first-mentioned wage. The reasoning relies on the principle that when an ambiguous term is used, it is interpreted in a way that upholds validity (taharrīyan lil-jawāz), and the immediate context (the order of mention) serves as a clear indicator (qarina).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguity
The contract states two months with two different wages but does not specify which month gets which wage. This creates an ambiguity that could potentially invalidate the contract if left unresolved.
Ambiguity (gharar) in essential terms can render a contract fasid (voidable) in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Apply the principle of insiraf
The Hanafi school resolves the ambiguity by giving the words their natural order: the first mentioned month is understood to be the one immediately following the contract, and the second month follows the first. This is based on 'urf (custom) and the need for immediate fulfillment.
This principle is similar to interpreting 'a month' as starting from the contract date when no start date is mentioned.
3
Justify by seeking validity
The rule 'taharrīyan lil-jawāz' (striving to uphold validity) is invoked. Among possible interpretations, the one that makes the contract valid and enforceable is preferred.
This is a key usul principle in Hanafi fiqh, especially for contracts.
4
Determine the outcome
Consequently, the first month is at the lower wage (four dirhams) and the second at the higher (five dirhams). If the slave works only the first month, only four dirhams are due.
The same reasoning would apply if the wages were reversed in order.
5
Contrast with other views
Some scholars may require explicit specification to avoid ambiguity. The Hanafi position relies on strong qarinat (indications) from the order of mention and custom.
This is a point of ikhtilaf, but the Hanafi view is the mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو استأجر عبداً شهرين شهراً بأربعة، وشهراً بخمسة صح والأول بأربعة. [1] قوله : ولو استأجر ... الخ ؛ يعني لو استأجر رجلاً عبداً لشهرين شهراً بأربعة دراهم وشهراً بخمسة دراهم من غير تعيين منهما ، صح العقد على الترتيب المذكور، فالأول من هذين الشهرين بأربعة دراهم، حتى لو عمل في الأول دون الثاني استحق أربعة دراهم، فإنّه لما قال : أوّلاً شهراً باربعة ينصرفُ إلى ما يلى العقد تحرّياً للجواز. كما إذا قال : استاجرتُ منك هذا العبد شهراً، وسكت فإنه ينصرف إلى ما يلي العقد، ونظراً إلى قضاء الحاجة في الحال، فإنّ الإنسان إنّما يستأجر الشيء لحاجة تدعوه إلى ذلك، والظاهر وقوعها عند العقد، وإذا انصرف الأوّل إلى ما يلي العقد والثاني معطوف عليه ينصرف إلى ما يلي الأوّل ضرورة. [۲] قوله : عبداً شهرين ؛ وهذا أولى ما قال في «الهداية» : من استأجر عبداً هذين الشهرين، فإنّه محتاج التأويل كما لا يخفى على من له إلى الحذاقة سبيل.
And if one hires a slave for two months: one month for four and one month for five, it is valid, and the first is for four. [1] His statement: 'And if one hires... etc.' means: if a man hires a slave for two months: one month for four dirhams and one month for five dirhams, without specification from either of them, the contract is valid on the mentioned order. Thus the first of these two months is for four dirhams, so if he works in the first month but not the second, he deserves four dirhams. Because when he says first 'a month for four,' it is understood to refer to the month immediately following the contract, seeking validity. Just as if he says 'I hired from you this slave for a month' and is silent, it refers to the month following the contract, considering the need at hand. Indeed, a person only hires something for a need that calls him to it, and it is apparent that it occurs at the time of the contract. When the first is understood as the immediate month, the second, being connected to it, necessarily refers to what follows the first. [2] His statement: 'a slave for two months' - this is more appropriate than what is said in al-Hidayah: 'Whoever hires a slave for these two months,' for it needs interpretation, as is not hidden from one who has a path to skill.

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a specific rental contract where a slave is hired for two months with different wages (four dirhams for one month, five for the other) without specifying which month corresponds to which wage. The ruling states that the contract is valid and the first month is automatically the one at the lower wage of four dirhams. The commentator explains that this is because the first month mentioned in the contract is understood to be the month immediate to the contract, following the principle that when an indefinite time period is mentioned, it is interpreted as beginning right after the contract, as is customary and necessary for fulfilling immediate needs. The second month then necessarily follows the first. The commentator also notes that a similar expression in al-Hidayah requires interpretation, implying that the wording chosen here is clearer.

Key Terms
الانصراف (al-insiraf): The interpretation of an ambiguous term in a contract to the most plausible meaning, here referring the first month to the period immediately after the contract.
تحرياً للجواز (taharrīyan lil-jawāz): Striving to uphold the validity of the contract by preferring an interpretation that makes it enforceable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In a rental contract with two different wages for two periods, the order of mention establishes the sequence and validates the contract, with the first period immediately after the contract.

Rule of Dispute in Ijarah: The Current State as Preference-Weight
Ruling on who is believed when slave's condition at end of term is known

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the current observable state (al-hal) serves as a preference-weight (tarjih) in disputes between lessor and hirer to determine whose claim is accepted.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, the current state is not a proof but a preference-weight that tips the scale in disputes over past conditions.

When a lessor and hirer disagree about whether the hired object was usable during the rental period, how does a judge decide? The Hanafi school looks to the present condition of the object: the one whose claim aligns with the current state is believed. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its analogy with the watermill, and the key usul principle that the current state (hal) serves as a preference-weight (tarjih), not a full proof (hujja).

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and its analogy
The passage begins with the watermill analogy: the owner claims water was flowing, the hirer claims it was not. The judge uses the current state of the water to decide. This sets the precedent for the slave case.
The watermill case is the 'asl (origin) for the slave case.
2
Recognize the two scenarios for the slave
If the slave is presently a runaway (aabiq), the lessor's claim that the slave only ran away at the end is supported by the current state, so the lessor is believed. If the slave is present and healthy, again the lessor's claim that the slave was available throughout is supported, so the lessor is believed.
In both scenarios, the current state favors the lessor's claim that the hirer had the ability to benefit.
3
Understand the role of al-hal
The current state (al-hal) is not a formal proof (hujja) in the Hanafi school; it cannot independently establish a fact. However, it serves as a preference-weight (tarjih) to decide between two conflicting claims when other evidence is lacking.
This distinction is rooted in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
4
Note the usul principle about tarjih
The commentator emphasizes that preference (tarjih) always occurs by that which is not a proof in itself. Al-hal, though not a proof, is sufficient to tip the balance. The passage references al-Zayla'i's discussion in 'al-Tabyin' for further detail.
This principle is consistent with Hanafi methodology: when two claims are equally plausible, external factors can give weight to one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال المؤجّرُ في آخرها أصلُ هذه المسألة الطاحونة، فإن المالك إذا قال : ماء الطاحونة كان جارياً في المدة، وقال المستأجر : لم يكن جارياً يُحْكُمُ الحال. الانتفاع فيما مضى ثابتاً ظاهراً، فالمؤجر بقوله : ما أبق إلا في الحال، يدعى أنه كان متمكن من الانتفاع، والمستأجر منكر، فكان القول قوله.
وإن كان صحيحاً في الحال أو غير آبق فالقول للمؤجر ؛ لأنّ التمكن منه ثابت فيما مضى ظاهراً بدلالة الحال، فالمستأجر يدّعي فوات التمكن فيما مضى، والمؤجر منكر له، فيكون القول قوله، والحال وإن لم يصلح حجة عندنا يصلح مرجحاً، إذ الترجيح إبداً إنما يقع بما لا يصلح حجّة، كما قالوا وهاهنا إشكال ذكره الزيلعي في «التبيين» مع تفصيل جوابه، فطالعه إن شئت. [1] قوله : فإنّ المالك... الخ ؛ توضيحه : إن مستأجر الرحى إذا اختلف مع صاحب الرحى في جريان الماء في المدة، فإنّ القول قولُ مَن يشهد له الحال، فإن كان الماء منقطعاً وقت الخصومة فالقولُ للمستأجر فيما مضى، وإن كان جارياً فالقولُ لرب الرحى مع يمينه.
وإن اختلفا في قدر الانقطاع فقال المستأجر : عشرة أيام، وقال الآجر: خمسة آیام، فالقولُ للمستأجر، والبيئة [؟] للآجر، وهو يصلح مرجحاً إن لم يصلح حجّة في نفسه إذ الترجيح أبداً إنما يقع بما لا يصلح حجّة، وقد عرف في أصول الفقه. كذا في «الكفاية».
And the lessor said at the end of it: The origin of this issue is the watermill. When the owner says: 'The water of the mill was flowing during the period,' and the lessee says: 'It was not flowing,' the [current] situation is judged. Benefit in the past is outwardly established, so the lessor by his saying 'He only ran away in the present' claims that he was able to benefit, and the lessee denies it; thus the lessor's word is accepted. If the slave is healthy in the present or not a runaway, then the lessor's word is accepted because the ability [to benefit] in the past is outwardly established by the evidence of the current situation. The lessee claims loss of ability in the past, and the lessor denies it; thus the lessor's word is accepted. Although the current situation is not a valid proof in our school, it is valid as a preference-weight, since preference always occurs by that which is not a proof in itself. As they said, and there is a difficulty here mentioned by al-Zayla'i in 'al-Tabyin' with a detailed answer, so consult it if you wish. [1] His statement: 'Indeed the owner...' etc.; its clarification: When the hirer of the handmill disputes with the owner of the handmill regarding the flow of water during the period, the word is accepted from the one whose situation supports him. If the water is cut off at the time of the dispute, the word of the hirer is accepted regarding the past; if it is flowing, the word of the mill owner is accepted with his oath. If they dispute the amount of the cut-off, the hirer saying 'ten days' and the lessor saying 'five days', the word of the hirer is accepted, and the evidence is upon the lessor. It is valid as a preference-weight even if not a proof in itself, since preference always occurs by that which is not a proof, as is known in usul al-fiqh. Thus in 'al-Kifaya'.
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the procedural rule for disputes in ijarah contracts. The commentator begins by stating the principle: the origin of this issue is the watermill analogy. When the owner of a mill and the hirer dispute whether the water was flowing during the rental period, the decision is based on the current observable state (al-hal). The reasoning is that past benefit is presumed to have been possible if the current state shows it was possible. The commentator then applies this to the case of hiring a slave: if the slave is presently a runaway (aabiq), the lessor claims the slave only ran away at the end, so the lessee had the ability to benefit in the past. Since the current state supports the lessor (the slave is now absent), the lessor's word is accepted. If the slave is present and healthy, the current state supports the lessor's claim that the slave was available, so again the lessor's word is accepted. The commentator clarifies that while the current state is not a formal proof (hujja) in the Hanafi school, it serves as a preference-weight (tarjih). This is a principle from usul al-fiqh: that which is not a proof can still be used to prefer one claim over another. The passage ends with a reference to al-Zayla'i's 'al-Tabyin' for a deeper discussion and also cites 'al-Kifaya'. The practical consequence is that in disputes about past conditions, the judge looks at the present situation to decide who is more credible.

Key Terms
الحال (al-haal): The current observable state or situation at the time of dispute, used to infer past conditions.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Giving preference to one party's claim over another based on supporting factors, even if those factors are not independent proofs.
المؤجر (al-mu'jir): The owner of an object or slave who leases it out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute between the lessor and hirer of a mill about whether water was flowing during the rental period, according to the Hanafi ruling, whose word is accepted if the water is currently cut off?
A) The lessor's word
B) The hirer's word
C) Both are equally credible
D) The one who provides witnesses

Key Takeaway
The current state (hal) determines credibility in ijarah disputes, not as proof but as a preference-weight.

The Owner's Word is Taken: Disputes in Ijarah over Work and Payment
Explanation of evidentiary rules when owner and artisan dispute work description or payment in ijarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule when an owner and artisan dispute the description of work or the basis of payment, explain the qiyas argument, and identify the consequences including the owner’s choice of remedy.

Core Idea
In ijarah disputes, the owner’s word is taken with oath because authorization originates from him.

Contracts of hire (ijarah) often give rise to disputes between the owner of a garment (or any item) and the artisan. Two common scenarios are disagreement over the type of work ordered and disagreement over whether the work was for free or for a wage. The Hanafi school provides a clear evidentiary rule: the owner’s statement is accepted with oath in both cases. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, the qiyas (analogy) used, and the practical consequences for liability and compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two dispute scenarios
Recognize that the passage covers two distinct disputes: (1) disagreement on the description of the work (e.g., qaba’ vs shirt, red dye vs green dye) and (2) disagreement on whether the work was for free (gratuitous) or for a wage (ijarah mu’awadah).
The first scenario involves a contract that both parties acknowledge existed, but they disagree on its terms. The second scenario involves a dispute on the existence of a contract itself.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
In both scenarios, the owner’s word is taken with an oath. The artisan’s contrary claim is not accepted without evidence. The ruling is not about the validity of the act but about who is believed in court.
The ruling is procedural: it determines who must provide evidence and who is the defendant. The owner is the defendant because he denies the artisan’s claim.
3
Analyze the legal reason (ta’lil)
The reason for the ruling is that the authorization (idhn) to work on the garment comes from the owner. Since the owner originated the permission, his word about what he authorized is given precedence. This is analogous to a case where the owner denies the entire contract (claiming the garment was a deposit). In that case the owner’s word is also taken, so here too.
This is qiyas jaliy: the effective cause (‘illa) is the ownership and authorization.
4
Understand the consequences after the oath
Once the owner swears, the artisan becomes liable for the garment. The owner has a choice: (a) claim the unworked value, in which case the artisan gets no wage; or (b) claim the worked value, in which case the artisan receives the equivalent wage (ujr al-mithl) but not exceeding any named wage. This choice arises because the artisan’s work is partly consistent with the owner’s claim (the fact of working) but inconsistent as to the specific description.
The owner’s choice is a practical remedy that prevents injustice: the artisan is not entirely deprived of compensation if the owner opts for the worked value.
5
Apply to the payment dispute
In the second scenario, the owner claims the work was gratuitous (without wage), and the artisan claims it was for hire. Here the owner denies the contract itself. Since work is only compensated by contract, and the owner denies the contract, his word is taken with oath. The work is then considered a voluntary assistance (i’anah), which does not entitle the artisan to any wage.
This scenario is simpler: the artisan’s claim of a wage would impose an obligation on the owner, which the owner can deny under oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الاختلاف في الإجارة
وصُدِّقَ رَبُّ الثَّوْبِ في : أمرتك أن تعمله قباء، أو تصبغه أحمر لا أجير قال : أمرتني بما عملت وفي عملت لي مجاناً لا صانع، قال : بل بأجر
( وصدق ربُّ الثَّوْبِ في : أمرتُك أن تعمله قباء، أو تصبغه أحمر لا أجير قال : أمرتني بما عملت ؛ لأنَّ الإذنَ مُسْتَفادٌ من ربِّ الثوب، والمراد أن يُصَدِّقَ باليمين
(وفي عملت لي مجاناً لا صانع، قال : بل بأجر ) ؛ لأنَّ المالك ينكر تقوم قوله : وصدق...الخ ؛ يعني إذا وقع الاختلاف بين الخياط ومالك الثوب، فقال مالك الثوب : أمرتك أن تعمله قباء، وقال الخياط : أمرتني أن أعمله قميصاً، أو قال مالك الثوب للصباغ : أمرتك أن تصبغه أحمر، وقال الصباغ : أمرتني أن أصبغه أخضر، فصدق مالك الثوب، ويكون القول قوله. قوله : لأنّ الإذن مستفاد من ربِّ الثوب ؛ ألا ترى أنه لو أنكر أصل العقد بأن قال : كان ذلك وديعة ، كان القول قول ربِّ الثوب، فكذا إذا أنكر صفته. قوله : والمراد أن يصدق باليمين ؛ لأنه أنكر شيئاً لو أقر به لزمه ذلك الشيء، فإذا أنكره يحلف فإذا حلف فالخياط ضامن، وصاحب الثوب مخير إن شاء ضمنه قيمة الثوب غير معمول فلا أجر له، أو قيمته معمولاً فله أجر مثله لا يجاوز به المسمّى ؛ لأنه موافق من وجه وهو أصل العمل، مخالف من وجه وهو الصفة، فيميلُ إلى أيهما شاء. كذا في «التبيين»، وغيره. قوله : وفي عملت...الخ ؛ يعني إذا اختلف المستأجر ومالك الثوب في الأجرة ، فقال مالك الثوب : عملته لي بغير أجر ، وقال الصانع عملته لك بأجر، فالقول يكون لمالك الثوب لا للصانع. قوله : لأن المالك ... الخ ؛ لأنّ العمل يتقوم بالعقد، ولا عقد هاهنا حيث ادّعى العمل بغير أجر، ودعوى العمل بغير أجر إعانة ، والإعانة تبرع. كذا في «الكفاية».
Chapter on differences in hire. And the owner of the garment is believed in: 'I ordered you to make it a qaba'' or 'dye it red' [and the artisan says 'I did what you ordered'], and in 'You worked for me for free, not for hire' when the artisan says 'Rather for hire'. (And the owner of the garment is believed in: 'I ordered you to make it a qaba'' or 'dye it red' [and the artisan says 'I did what you ordered'] because the authorization is derived from the owner of the garment, and what is meant is that he is believed with an oath. (And in 'You worked for me for free, not for hire' when the artisan says 'Rather for hire') because the owner denies compensation. His saying: 'And his word is believed' etc.; meaning if a dispute occurs between the tailor and the owner of the garment, and the owner says 'I ordered you to make it a qaba'' and the tailor says 'You ordered me to make it a shirt', or the owner says to the dyer 'I ordered you to dye it red' and the dyer says 'You ordered me to dye it green', then the owner of the garment is believed, and his word is taken. His saying: 'Because the authorization is derived from the owner of the garment'; do you not see that if he denied the original contract by saying 'That was a deposit', the word of the owner of the garment would be believed, so likewise if he denies its description. His saying: 'And what is meant is that he is believed with an oath'; because he denies something which if he admitted would obligate him to that thing, so if he denies it he takes an oath, and if he takes an oath then the tailor is liable, and the owner of the garment has the choice: if he wishes he may make him liable for the value of the garment unworked and he has no wage, or its value worked and he has its equivalent wage not exceeding the named amount; because he agrees in one aspect (the original work) and disagrees in another aspect (the description), so he may incline to whichever he wishes. Thus in al-Tabyin and others. His saying: 'And in 'You worked for me for free' etc.'; meaning if the hirer and the owner of the garment dispute over the wage, and the owner says 'You worked for me without wage' and the artisan says 'I worked for you for a wage', then the word is of the owner of the garment, not the artisan. His saying: 'Because the owner...etc.'; because work is valued by contract, and there is no contract here since he claimed work without wage, and the claim of work without wage is assistance, and assistance is a gift. Thus in al-Kifayah.
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on rulings when the owner of a garment and an artisan (tailor or dyer) dispute about the work ordered or about payment. The author explains two scenarios. First: if they disagree on the description of the work ordered (e.g., owner says 'I ordered a qaba'' and artisan says 'I was ordered to make a shirt', or owner says 'I ordered red dye' and artisan says 'green'), the owner's word is taken with an oath. The reason is that the authorization for the work comes from the owner, so his statement about what he authorized is trusted. This is based on a clear analogy: if the owner denies the contract entirely and claims the garment was a deposit, his word is accepted; similarly, if he denies the specific description. The commentator clarifies that the owner is believed with an oath because he is denying something that, if admitted, would create an obligation on him. Once he swears, the artisan becomes liable for the garment. The owner then has a choice: either claim the unworked value of the garment (and the artisan gets no wage) or claim the worked value (and the artisan gets the equivalent wage, not exceeding the agreed amount if any). This is because the artisan's work is partly consistent with the owner's claim (the fact of working) and partly inconsistent (the specific description), so the owner may choose the option that benefits him. This ruling is found in al-Tabyin and other works. Second: if they dispute over payment, with the owner claiming the work was gratuitous and the artisan claiming it was for hire, the owner's word is again taken. The reasoning is that work is compensated only by contract, and here the owner claims there was no contract for hire, which would make it a voluntary act. Voluntary acts are not compensated. This is from al-Kifayah. Both rulings illustrate the Hanafi principle that in disputes arising from a contract of hire, the party whose authorization is the basis (the owner) is believed over the party performing the work, because the latter's claim of a different order or of entitlement to payment involves asserting an obligation on the owner, which the owner can deny under oath.

Key Terms
صدق (saddaqa): His statement is accepted as true (with oath) in a dispute.
إذن (idhn): Permission or authorization from the owner to perform the work on his garment.
أجر مثل (ujr al-mithl): The equivalent wage for the work done, determined by market rates, not exceeding the agreed wage if any.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the owner of a garment says to the tailor 'I ordered you to make it a qaba'' and the tailor says 'You ordered me to make it a shirt', what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The tailor is believed because he did the work.
B) The owner is believed with an oath, and the tailor becomes liable.
C) They split the difference.
D) The case is dismissed.

Key Takeaway
In ijarah disputes over work description or payment, the Hanafi school gives precedence to the owner's statement with oath, reflecting that authorization originates from him.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
6 min
Dispute Over Description of Work in Ijarah: The Owner's Word is Taken
Ruling that owner's word is taken in describing work order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disputes over work description in ijarah, apply the owner's word with oath, and determine the owner's options after the worker's liability.

Core Idea
The owner's word is taken because permission originates from him.

When a cloth owner and a tailor or dyer disagree over the specific work ordered, Hanafi law gives priority to the owner's statement (with oath). This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from istihsan via analogy, and the practical consequences for both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize the scenario: the owner claims he ordered a specific garment or color, the worker claims a different one.
2
State the ruling
The owner's word is taken (with oath) – he is believed over the worker.
3
Understand the proof
The proof is istihsan through analogy: if the owner denied the contract entirely (claiming deposit), his word would be taken, so likewise for denial of a specific description.
4
Apply the consequences
After the owner's oath, the worker becomes liable. The owner may choose to claim value unworked (no wage) or value worked (paying fair wage not exceeding agreed price).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الاختلاف في الإجارة ( وصدق رب الثوب في : أمرتك أن تعمله قباء، أو تصبغه أحمر لا أجير قال : أمرتني بما عملت؛ لأنَّ الإذن مستفاد من رب الثوب، والمراد أن يصدق باليمين. قوله : وصدق...الخ ؛ يعني إذا وقع الاختلاف بين الخياط ومالك الثوب، فقال مالك الثوب : أمرتك أن تعمله قباء، وقال الخياط : أمرتني أن أعمله قميصاً، أو قال مالك الثوب للصباغ : أمرتك أن تصبغه أحمر، وقال الصباغ : أمرتني أن أصبغه أخضر، فصدق مالك الثوب، ويكون القول قوله. قوله : لأنّ الإذن مستفاد من ربِّ الثوب؛ ألا ترى أنه لو أنكر أصل العقد بأن قال : كان ذلك وديعة، كان القول قول ربِّ الثوب، فكذا إذا أنكر صفته. قوله : والمراد أن يصدق باليمين؛ لأنه أنكر شيئاً لو أقر به لزمه ذلك الشيء، فإذا أنكره يحلف فإذا حلف فالخياط ضامن، وصاحب الثوب مخير إن شاء ضمنه قيمة الثوب غير معمول فلا أجر له، أو قيمته معمولاً فله أجر مثله لا يجاوز به المسمّى؛ لأنه موافق من وجه وهو أصل العمل، مخالف من وجه وهو الصفة، فيميلُ إلى أيهما شاء. كذا في «التبيين»، وغيره.
Chapter on disputes in Ijarah: The owner of the cloth is believed in (saying): 'I ordered you to make it a qaba' or 'dye it red' – not a hireling said: 'You ordered me to do what I did' – because permission is obtained from the owner of the cloth, and the intent is that he is believed upon oath. His statement: 'and is believed...' etc. means: if a dispute occurs between the tailor and the owner of the cloth, and the owner of the cloth says: 'I ordered you to make it a qaba'' and the tailor says: 'You ordered me to make it a shirt', or the owner of the cloth says to the dyer: 'I ordered you to dye it red' and the dyer says: 'You ordered me to dye it green', then the owner of the cloth is believed, and his statement is taken. His statement: 'because permission is obtained from the owner of the cloth' – do you not see that if he denied the original contract by saying: 'that was a deposit', the statement of the owner of the cloth would be taken, so also if he denies its description. His statement: 'and the intent is that he is believed upon oath' – because he denied something which, if he acknowledged it, would bind him, so if he denies it, he takes an oath, and if he takes an oath, the tailor is liable, and the owner of the cloth has the option: if he wishes, he can claim the value of the cloth unworked, in which case there is no wage for him, or its value worked, in which case he gets a fair wage not exceeding the specified amount, because he agrees in one respect (the basis of work) and disagrees in another (the description), so he may incline to whichever he wishes. So in Al-Tabyeen and others.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This is a ruling on disputes in Ijarah (hire/lease of services). The passage type is a ruling with proof. When a dispute arises between the owner of cloth and a tailor or dyer over the description of the work ordered, the owner's word is taken (with oath). The proof is that the permission to work originates from the owner; analogically, if the owner denied the contract altogether (claiming the cloth was a deposit), his word would be taken, so it is the same for denial of a specific description. Once the owner takes an oath, the tailor becomes liable for the cloth. The owner has a choice: he can claim the value of the cloth as unworked, in which case the tailor gets no wage, or he can claim the value as worked, paying a fair wage not exceeding the agreed price. This is because there is agreement on the basis of work but disagreement on the specific type. The commentary is from Al-Tabyeen and follows the Hanafi position from the zahir al-riwayah.

Key Terms
رب الثوب (rabb al-thawb): The owner of the cloth who hires a tailor or dyer.
قباء (qaba'): A type of garment (a long coat).
أجير (ajir): A hired worker (tailor or dyer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute between a cloth owner and a tailor about whether the owner ordered a qaba' or a shirt, whose word is taken and why?
A) The tailor's word, because he did the work.
B) The owner's word, because permission originates from him.
C) Both are equally credible, so a compromise is reached.
D) The court decides based on custom.

Key Takeaway
In disputes over work description in ijarah, the owner's word is taken upon oath, and after the oath, the owner has the option to claim the value unworked or worked with a fair wage.
